A Kingdom by the Night

by visadero

Summary

“You’re early,” Agatha managed, feigning a flicker of annoyance, though her pulse quickened.
"I missed you.” The words were simple, almost soft. Her dark gaze held Agatha’s, steady and unyielding.
"Agatha huffed, “Is that so?” She turned away, trying to mask the slight flush rising to her cheeks. "I’d think the Queen of Shadows wouldn’t be so sentimental.”
The woman’s lips curved ever so slightly as she closed the distance between them. “Think what you want. But here you are."

Notes

we're taking some liberties here folks. loose adaption in every sense aka taking the bits I like and ignoring the rest.

Songbird

The night was unusually cold for early spring, and the damp chill seeped through her cloak as she stood in the center of the clearing, waiting. Moonlight dappled the forest floor, casting long, strange shadows that seemed to breathe with life of their own. Her coven stood in a circle around her, their faces shadowed under hoods, murmuring softly in unison—a chant. Old words she’d only heard in fragments, whispered and half-forgotten, from ages long past. Tonight they dared to call upon something ancient. Something that hadn’t answered in centuries.

Perhaps it wouldn’t work. Part of her hoped it wouldn’t work, if only to make the others feel folish. Why should she be made an example of when she hadn’t done anything wrong? Her fingertips itched, maybe something would go wrong. Something that would allow her to dart off. Away through the woods, another village, another life. She could do it. They didn’t understand. They saw the chaos of an untamed wild child who couldn’t control her magic even after a couple of decades. Never mind that not one of them had taken even the slightest interest in teaching her. She knew they were afraid of her. Which meant she must be incredibly powerful. She just didn’t know how to reach that. Not yet.

She also knew with certainty, that human sacrifices typically had a pretty short window of opportunity to get it together. Her eyes searched, seeking a single face but the hoods obscured her coven. If she could catch her mother’s eye, surely her mother wasn’t going to allow this. Surely, this was just an overreaction to teach her a lesson. Agatha wouldn’t humiliate herself, she wasn’t going to beg. But she would never understand why they couldn’t see—she could be a good witch. Not particularly nice, or helpful, or kind perhaps. But good at being a witch. Powerful.

The earth trembled beneath her feet, subtly at first, then with the power of something deep and vast, like the stirring of a slumbering primordial beast. Agatha’s heart hammered against her ribs as she clutched a small bundle of herbs for protection—a ritual comfort more than a shield.

A fissure split the ground at the center of the clearing, revealing a narrow, shadowed path spiraling down into darkness. Cold air surged from below, sharp and biting, carrying the scent of stone and smoke. From the blackness, a figure emerged, stepping not out of, but with the shadows as though they were merely part of her cloak.

She was a formidable presence, with a piercing gaze that seemed to drink in the moonlight itself. Her eyes were shards of obsidian, and her dark hair spilled over her shoulders in waves smooth as silk. Every line of her face, from the high cheekbones to the slight curve of her lips, seemed chiseled from stone—unmoving, untouched by time.

A small gasp escaped Agatha. Beautiful. Curious, she hadn’t expected her to be beautiful.

The Queen of Shadows, Lady of the Underworld. 

Agatha’s coven fell silent as she stepped forward. They bowed low, their hands still clasped in reverence. The one who led the ritual—she recognized Helene by those awful heeled boots—spoke with a voice that quivered despite its attempt at formality.

“We bring the offering as promised,” she said, gesturing to Agatha. “As payment for our continued protection. She is…she is our finest, with powers strong and untamed.”

The Queen’s gaze settled on Agatha, her expression unchanging. Agatha held her breath, feeling that gaze pierce through her, and she couldn’t help but shiver slightly.

“Step forward,” she commanded, her voice as smooth and deep as the shadows themselves.

Agatha glanced back at her coven, searching for some flicker of reassurance in their veiled faces. But they remained silent, heads bowed, hands clasped. She was on her own. Steeling herself, she stepped forward, closer than any living mortal had likely been in ages.

The Lady took her in for a moment, her head tilting just slightly as she examined Agatha like a curiosity, a specimen. At last, she spoke a faint edge of amusement curling her words.

“So, this is your offering. Tell me, witch, do you come willingly?” The question hung heavy in the air, almost mocking.

Agatha swallowed, her mouth suddenly dry. “I…come as a member of the coven,” she replied, her voice soft but steady. “Our agreement with you binds us to protect the lands above, to keep the seasons in balance. I honor their choice.”

The smile was cold, knowing. “A well-rehearsed answer.” She circled Agatha slowly, her gaze sweeping over her from head to toe, assessing, weighing her value. “You speak of honor, yet you are unproven. Your magic has not reached you fully.”

“I am good enough,” Agatha replied, lifting her chin. “And I am not afraid of you.”

The coven gasped softly behind her, but The Lady only chuckled, a low, resonant sound. She stepped even closer, so close Agatha could feel the cold radiating from her skin like the breath of a winter storm. She reached out, brushing her gloved fingers along Agatha’s cheek, a surprisingly gentle touch.

Agatha shivered but kept her composure.

“Not afraid, are you?” she murmured. “Then look into my eyes, Agatha of the coven. And tell me—what do you see?”

Agatha met her gaze, feeling a strange, pull within those depths. The clearing, the coven, all around them faded. Fragments of vision rushed through her mind. Endless, winding corridors beneath the earth, stone walls lit with blue fire, shadows that moved and whispered, a wicked and curved throne looking upon it all. It was horrifying. It was beautiful.  She did not look away.

“I see…you,” Agatha whispered, her voice barely a breath. “And I see the choice you’re giving me.”

The taller woman’s lips curved, her eyes gleaming. “Wise enough to know a choice when you see one. Yet you still stand here, willing to face the darkness.”

“What’s darkness but the unknown, and what’s the unknown but an opportunity,” Agatha replied, steadier now. “For my coven.” See? She could be so good.

The Quen held her gaze a moment longer as if testing her. Then she nodded, her smile fading into something colder, more distant.

“So be it,” she said, her voice echoing through the clearing. She extended her hand to Agatha, palm up, fingers outstretched—a silent command. “You will spend half your days below and half above, tending the cycles of life and death, bound to my realm as its consort.”

Agatha hesitated, feeling the weight of eternity in that hand. With a final glance back at her coven, who still knelt in reverent silence, she reached forward and took the hand offered to her. The chill sank through her skin, spreading through her like ink in water, freezing and binding her to the Queen of Shadows.

“I will return for you. A few months from now. Be ready.”

Agatha nodded, watching intently as her hand was lifted up towards the Queen’s lips. For a brief moment, she thought that she may kiss her hand and that thought made something prickle inside her. But instead, a soft whisper against her knuckles, surprisingly warm breath passing over her skin.

“Te veo.”

The Queen of Shadows was gone, leaving Agatha and her coven alone in the clearing.

The clearing was utterly still, as if Agatha, the coven, the whole world still held its breath. Slowly, the coven raised their heads, watching Agatha with wary, almost fearful eyes. She was bound now, marked by the Underworld’s Queen. There was no turning back.

Her mother stepped forward, her lips thin, eyes hard as she regarded Agatha. “You have done what was needed,” she said with a clipped tone. “Our coven will flourish with this bond.” But there was no warmth in her voice, only a tense satisfaction.

Agatha clenched her fists, feeling the weight of her new fate press into her chest as her nails dug into her palms. Her coven’s safety might be assured, but her future belonged to the Queen of Shadows. 

As they turned to leave, Agatha lingered, looking back over the clearing, memorizing the spot. The fissure in the ground had closed, but she knew the pathway to the Underworld was there, waiting for her, always.

The weight of the Queen’s whispered words echoed in her ears.

 

“I see you.”

 

Way Down

Chapter Summary

A few months later, it's time to be collected

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Green. Everything was green. The smell of overripe fruit hung heavy in the air. Leaves lay wet and dark underfoot, glistening with the aftermath of fresh rain, clinging to her boots as she trudged forward, purposefully leaving tracks in the mud. Normally, she would’ve erased every trace of herself, vanishing into the underbrush like a whisper of wind. But today, she expected to be found. If she was honest with herself, she wanted to be.

In the weeks following the ritual, life had crept back to its familiar, stagnant pace. Her days empty, as if she'd been hollowed out and stuffed full of dust and clay in place of her own life. Daily, she woke to the same murmurs and side glances from her coven. Every evening she toiled in silent isolation, her power seething beneath her skin, eager, brimming, yet ever unwelcome.

It was as if, after all the thrill and dread of that ritual, she now existed on the edge of some new invisible precipice. The edge of a knife. It’s not a good sign when your home casts you out so completely that lodging up with death herself seemed like a refreshing change of pace.

The mist still hung low to the ground, as at first light she wandered out to gather herbs in the woods. She moved through her task, mindlessly, until something caught her eye—a cluster of strange black lilies. As though they had clawed their way up through the soil, they bloomed here curling upwards in long finger-like tendrils, each petal gleamed as if slick with oil.

She knelt, reaching out to brush her fingertips along one of the petals, but quickly jerked her hand away as it seemed to pulse in response to her touch. The flower seemed to drink in the light, its dark, rippling surface oddly comforting. A message as clear as if it had been whispered directly to her. 

She was coming.

And, for the first time in six months, a surge of emotion. A feeling familiar but that had not been felt since that night. Excitement. She would finally leave this place of endless suspicion, no longer bound to these wary stares and muttered rumors. Life here had always been so quiet, so gray. There was an incredible freedom in the thought of leaving, even knowing she faced something so vast and untamed. Something so completely unknown but undeniably powerful.

She liked power.

Agatha surprised herself as she chuckled, fingers running under the delicate petals of the flower. Velvety smooth. For a moment she hesitated, there was good reason travelers warned about taking things from these woods. But perhaps it was a gift and it would be rude not to. 

“Gods it’s just a damn flower,” she growled, exasperated with herself for agonizing over something so foolish. “We don’t need anyone’s permission.” She plucked the flower, hissing in pain as it sprouted a thorn, cutting her. She pressed her finger to her lips sucking away the drop of blood that had sprung up. The flower pulsed again and she watched as a single petal fell, drawn to the cut, binding around it to stop the bleeding. It felt so delicate, like a lover’s kiss. She glanced at the flower again and smiled. Beautiful and dangerous. Just her type.

She finished gathering the herbs and practically flew back to the cottage. This would be her last day here. At nightfall, she would find the glade. And then she would be taken to somewhere else. For six months. That was time enough out from under the coven’s thumb. The underworld had to be full of magic, unlike anything anyone had seen. A tool, something she could harness and use. By the time she returned here next, everyone would see that Agatha Harkness was undeniable.

Humming softly, Agatha paused, her gaze sweeping over the forest. She found her quarry in an almost perfectly circular clearing. The trees here were different—a stark contrast to the lush life behind her. Their limbs were bare, bark cracked and withered gray as if drained of all color and warmth. Branches jutted out at sharp, disjointed angles, pointing straight up toward the sky like skeletal fingers grasping at clouds. The air here was colder, and her breath came out in short puffs of mist.

At the clearing’s center, Agatha spun in a slow circle, her coat fanning out around her as she raised her arms in a dramatic flourish. "Here I am!" she called, a mischievous smile tugging at her lips. Silence. She frowned, dropping her hands with a sigh. The art of a dramatic entrance, the thrill of a grand reveal—it was always a delicate game of timing. Well, you win some, you lose some. As she turned back, her breath caught in her lungs.

The lady of death stood before her. She hadn't heard a single footstep, hadn’t sensed a whisper of presence before Her arrival. Though she had slipped in like a shadow, Agatha felt very clearly the presence that seemed to pull all warmth from the air around them. Agatha’s eyes flicked over her, taking in the stern set of her mouth, the faint, knowing smile just beneath it.

Something about that smile sparked something in her. Agatha didn’t need her knowing how eager she was to be here. Negotiating always required leverage, and this early, when she wasn’t even yet sure what she wanted of her, she couldn’t give a single thing up.

“You’re early,” Agatha managed, feigning a flicker of annoyance, though her pulse quickened. 

“I missed you.” The words were simple, almost soft. Her dark gaze held Agatha’s, steady and unyielding.

Agatha huffed,  “Is that so?” She turned away, trying to mask the slight flush rising to her cheeks. "I’d think the Queen of Shadows wouldn’t be so sentimental.”

The woman’s lips curved ever so slightly as she closed the distance between them. “Think what you want. But here you are. Also, its Rio. The whole Queen of Shadows thing, it’s a mouthful.” She extended a gloved hand, palm up—a gesture surely intended to be commanding but which looked so inviting. “Shall we?”

Agatha eyed the outstretched hand. No turning back now. She could do worse.

“Do you plan to stare at my hand all day?” Rio’s voice cut through her thoughts.

Agatha smirked, her confidence returning. “I thought you liked the anticipation. You waited this long after all.” But she took Rio’s hand, feeling the cold bite through the leather of her gloves. As their hands met, a faint surge of energy hummed between them, like the pulse of hidden magic.

Without a word, Rio turned, guiding Agatha toward the far edge of the clearing, where the ground seemed to fall away into a shadowed descent. As they stepped forward, the verdant green faded, giving way to earth and rock, every trace of color leaching from the surroundings. Blood draining from the corpse. Agatha felt the weight of the descent press upon her, heavy and ancient. Every step they took seemed to pull her deeper into something colder, darker.

At last, they reached the mouth of the underworld. It was no more than a narrow archway at the base of a stone outcropping, draped in trailing vines like the grasping tendrils of some deep-rooted thing. Rio’s grip on Agatha’s hand tightened for a heartbeat before releasing.

“This is your last chance to turn back,” Rio murmured, though her tone held no real expectation. It was an empty offer. A trap. No, It was a trial she realized as Rio quirked an eyebrow back at her. Agatha met her gaze, lips quirking in defiance.

“Do you think I would back out now?” she replied, her voice steady.

Rio regarded her for a long moment, eyes glinting in the half-light as if searching for something. Then, with a nod, she turned and stepped into the shadows. Agatha followed, feeling the cold close around her like a shroud. As they entered, the doorway sealed behind them, the last sliver of light vanishing, leaving only darkness and the echo of their steps as they began their descent.

 

Down. 

Down.

Down.

Garden of Shades

Chapter Summary

Welcome to the Underworld.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

They walked in silence. Agatha a step behind Rio. It smelled like moist earth which wasn’t surprising but there was another note of something sharp and slightly acrid. It wasn’t unpleasant. 

A small breeze drifted past from further down the tunnel. A gasp of warm air taking the quickest path to the surface.  But as the breeze passed her, it was accompanied by a woman’s screen. Goosebumps instantly formed on Agatha’s skin as she startled and leaned back against the wall.

“Don’t mind them.” Rio had stopped, glancing over her shoulder. “Just a lost spirit. Sometimes when they first get here they’re… restless.” Her eyes traced over Agatha as if assessing her propensity for fleeing.

Agatha forced a laugh trying to contain her nerves. She wasn’t naive, she’d expected to witness the macabre. But she’d envisioned corpses not physically feeling someone’s dying gasps. She fucking hated ghosts.

She tried for deflection “And here I thought everyone was dying to be here!”

The corner of Rio’s mouth almost quirked into a smile. Agatha watched as her tongue pressed into the inside of her cheek. Holding something back? Perhaps death wasn’t humorless.

“Keep close,” Rio said lowly, turning again to the path ahead. As Agatha focused back on the path ahead she realized the landscape had changed completely.

Jagged stones like broken teeth jutted out of the rock, marking a path to an immense shadowed archway carved into the mountainside. The arch was illuminated by an etching that glimmered faintly, old runes pulsing a sickly green. She was transfixed, her gaze lingering as she reached a hand to trace her fingertips-

“Don’t.” A stern order as her wrist was grabbed sharply. Agatha winced, Rio hadn’t dropped her hand, instead pulling Agatha away from the arch and towards her. “We don’t touch what doesn’t belong to us.”

Agatha scowled as she looked at her wrist held between them. Rio’s nails began to elongate, sharpen, unsheathing like claws, pressing into her skin. She felt one begin to prick at the vein in her wrist. “You’re going to hurt me.” She said quietly.

Rio seemed unmoved. “I’m not going to hurt you.” Her eyes held Agatha’s for a long moment. “But we need to be very clear about something. There are many dangerous things here. Many things that as my consort you are shielded from. But there are magics of death and magics of fate. I only control the first one.”

“Who controls the other?” Agatha asked, trying to hide the hunger in her voice.

Rio rolled her eyes before finally releasing her hand. “No one.” She replies. “But if you are hellbent on trying, at least take the time to learn your surroundings before putting your fingers on the first trap glyph you see.”

“A trap? What kind?” Agatha couldn’t help her eagerness this time.

In an instant, Rio had closed the gap between them, wrapping her hand in the neck of Agatha’s cloak and pushing her backward. There was a flash in her eyes, manic and predatory. As Agatha’s back was forced closer to the archway she began to feel a sharp sting of magic tendrils biting at her back and she wondered if Rio was about to push her into it. “Wanna see?” Rio growled, her smile unsettling.

In that moment, she knew Rio was absolutely capable of pushing her into whatever ward and punishment the glyph carried. It was not a good sign for her self-preservation that that knowledge sparked intrigue instead of fear.

“Not really,” she quipped, she wondered briefly if she looked as feral as Rio did. She felt it. “Lesson learned, don’t touch things that don’t ask for it. Consent is sexy and all.” She had a death wish. That was the only explanation.

But her cheek was rewarded with an actual chuckle. A quick bark that seemed to surprise Rio as much as it did her. She was pulled back away from the arch, gently this time. Rio’s hands left her and as they did it seemed like the air grew a bit cooler again.

“We have farther to go. Keep up.” She turned away again, walking a well-treaded path, the weight of her presence an anchor pulling Agatha deeper into this strange darkness.

They descended a steep path, the ground beneath them rough and uneven, leading into a vast cavern that seemed to expand endlessly in all directions. As her eyes adjusted, Agatha saw what looked like a sprawling city, tucked into the very bones of the earth. Towering spires of black stone, bridges of dark iron twisted above them, connecting structures like a dark web spun by some ancient wrought thread.

Everything gleamed with a hard, metallic sheen. The stone streets were lit by the glow of dim, ghostly lanterns, casting greenish light across every jagged surface. The lights flickered in time with the eerie, rhythmic hum of machinery somewhere deep below. They were pulsing, as though they were drawing breath, and Agatha shivered.

“It’s… larger than I thought,” Agatha murmured, her voice swallowed by the cavernous expanse. “I expected…”

“It’s endless,” Rio replied, her tone neither boastful nor humble, simply stating fact. She paused, glancing over her shoulder, her eyes catching the greenish light. “It grows, it changes—just like those who come here.”

Eventually, they reached the edge of the city and at its boundary surprisingly was a train station. An obsidian locomotive spewed black smoke as figures cloaked in shadow, souls just arrived, emptied onto the platform. Agatha watched them with morbid fascination, feeling the weight of her own heartbeat as she saw a group of the translucent figures drift by.

"All your creation?" she asked, her voice hesitant.

Rio nodded. “Every corner, every shadow. These are my domains. They answer to me—and, parts, to you now.”

Rio’s words lingered, sending a strange shiver through Agatha as they turned and continued their path deeper into the city. The farther they went, the darker and denser the structures became. Buildings rose higher, their facades carved from smooth obsidian, and tall smokestacks belched shadow rather than smoke, strange darkness that seemed to dissolve into the sky.

They walked through narrow, labyrinthine streets lined with ancient buildings that looked strangely both organic and crafted as if they had grown from the rock itself but had been deliberately manipulated in their construction. Great iron pipes snaked along the ground and up the walls, disappearing into the rock above. Each turn brought them closer to the heart of the city, where the industrial noise grew louder—the sounds of machines turning, and the occasional hiss of steam.

Finally, they came to an intricate gate, wrought from iron and onyx. Beyond lay a secluded part of the city—a vast courtyard garden, where shadows themselves seemed to bloom. Dark roses with jagged thorns, vines with silver-tipped leaves, and trees that looked as though they had been molded from blackened glass grew in eerie, organic harmony.

“This is the garden,” Rio explained, “I thought you might… it's a place to kill some time.”

The garden was beautiful and unsettling, wild and strange in a way that Agatha could not yet name. She felt the magic of the place wrap around her. Again she smelled that strange acidic scent from before. Here it seemed stronger. Sweeter.

“Thank you,” she said, surprised at the words that came to her. For all its eerieness, the garden felt like an offering.

Rio’s lips curved faintly. “It’s yours to tend as you see fit.”

Agatha took another few steps into the garden, feeling the strange, thrumming pulse of the place wrap around her The dark roses and sharp-edged vines drew her attention, each plant more uncanny and beautiful than the last, until she spotted a single flower standing out from the others, half-hidden among shadowed thorns.

It was the same flower she’d seen in the overworld, just before Rio came to collect her—a striking bloom with inky-black petals that shimmered with an otherworldly green iridescence. She kneeled next to it and reached out, almost entranced, the memory of finding it tugging at her.

Rio noticed her staring and took a step closer. “You recognize it.”

“Yes,” Agatha replied, glancing up. “It was growing by my coven’s grounds just before you came for me.”

Rio nodded, thoughtful in her gaze. “A Shadebloom. A marker between worlds. Its roots take hold in both, for a time.”

Agatha felt her chest tighten, memories of the boredom and longing, her anticipation before Rio’s arrival. As Agatha’s fingertips brushed over the Shadebloom, she felt an irresistible pull—a compulsion to touch it, to hold it. She knew better, of course. It wasn’t exactly a welcoming bloom; it was a messenger, a reminder of all that tethered her here. Yet, despite herself, she let her fingers trail just a little too close to the stem.

A sudden sting shot through her hand as a thorn bit into her. She hissed, pulling her hand back and watching as a single drop of blood welled up on her fingertip. The thorn had pricked her deeply this time, as if somehow aware of her hesitation. 

Rio’s gaze flicked down, her mouth almost curling into a smile. “Didn’t we just go over the rules about touching things here?” Her voice was light, and eyes playful in a way that made Agatha’s breath catch.

Agatha suppressed the urge to roll her eyes, pressing her thumb to the tiny wound. “Maybe I just like testing my boundaries,” she muttered, her voice carrying a bit defiance and a strange, low thrill she didn’t fully understand blossomed in her chest.

Rio watched her for a moment, her smile fading. She took a step closer, her fingers reaching out as though to touch Agatha’s hand, but stopping just short. “There are… consequences here, Agatha, ones you won’t always see coming.” Her voice softened, her gaze lingering on Agatha’s injured finger. “But sometimes, the pain means you’re growing.”

Agatha didn’t look away, instead meeting Rio’s gaze, that small spark of defiance still lingering. She lifted her finger, still stinging, to examine it closely. “Maybe I don’t mind a little pain,” she said, tilting her head. “Especially if it means the garden remembers me.”

Rio’s mouth quirked slightly, her tone laced with something nearly fond as she replied, “Then I suppose the Shadebloom will keep you in good company.” She plucked it from the soil and twirled it between her fingers for a moment. “If it is tended, it will return,” she said quietly. “Like all things bound to the cycles between worlds.” She kneeled next to Agatha and in a quick but gentle movement tucked the stem into a button loop at the collar of Agatha’s cloak. A pause, then: “This garden will grow as you care for it, Agatha.” Rio stood, brushed the dirt from her knee then abruptly turned and continued walking.

Agatha swallowed, fingers brushing the cool petals— a reminder of her own life now bound between worlds. But also, a gift, a token from the woman who had not asked for her to come here but seemed to be at the least amicable to her presence. She wasn’t at all what Agatha had expected. A cruel captor would’ve been straightforward. Far too easy. But Rio teetered between aloof and something unplaceable so familiar that it twisted her stomach with anxiety.

They continued their walk, moving past the garden and through another darkened corridor. At the end of it, Rio paused before an arched doorway. She pushed it open, revealing Agatha’s quarters.

Inside, the room was illuminated in a subdued twilight. Arched windows of black and purple crystal let in a silvery glow across the room. The bed was carved from dark whirled wood, with linens in a rich midnight blue. A stone hearth flickered with a cold, silver flame, casting enough light to illuminate several shelves of books, a small table, and a pewter cauldron tucked into a corner.

“This space is completely yours,” Rio said, watching Agatha’s reaction carefully. “You’ll find things you might need—books, a few familiar plants. Your magic may feel… restrained here. But give it time. The Underworld has its own power.”

Agatha nodded, her eyes drifting over the details, feeling a strange, unexpected thrill in the center of her chest. This space, somewhat austere but comfortable, was hers to shape and command. She could sense Rio’s influence everywhere—the cold flame, the dark crystal—but it felt like an invitation rather than an imposition.

It had a more human touch than she expected and she wondered, had this been built just for her? Or did Rio lounge on a throne in some macabre mansion somewhere? “Where do you sleep?”

Rio glanced curiously at her arching an eyebrow, “Pardon?”

“I meant, do you sleep? You knew how to do up the room. It’s nice. I didn’t expect you to be an interior decorator.” She said quickly.

“Everyone needs hobbies.” Rio shrugged, leaning against the door frame. “If you were expecting a crypt, you should’ve had your coven summon a vampire.”

Finally, Agatha looked back at Rio, feeling a spark of determination and a hint of something she couldn’t place. “Well, thanks. I’ll make it mine,” she said.

Rio gave a single nod. “See that you do. I mean it, it's yours. No one will enter without your invitation. Including myself.”

“I thought you weren’t a vampire?” Agatha teased.

Rio scoffed and rolled her eyes before slipping back into the shadows, leaving Agatha alone to explore the realm that was now hers to share.

Left alone in the cool quiet, Agatha took a long, slow breath. She moved across the room, letting her fingers brush over the edges of the shelves, glancing at the odd assortment of books and trinkets. She wasn’t sure what to make of Rio’s gesture, but there was no denying the care in the details, the deliberate choices in the objects that filled the room. The cauldron, the shelves of old and unfamiliar spell books, herbs hanging in small bundles, even the rich color of the fabrics…there was almost an understanding of who she was. Agatha smirked a little, surprised by the thought.

In the near-silence, Agatha caught again the faintest echo of distant gears grinding, a muffled thrum that seemed to pulse in time with the dim lanterns that cast their glow across the city streets outside her window. Even in stillness, this place was alive with quiet energy, a city that breathed beneath the earth. 

After a moment, she took another steady breath and walked toward the window, tracing her fingertips along the dark crystal. Her gaze roamed the industrial sprawl of the city below. This place was vast and ancient, strange and alive with its own kind of magic, one she didn’t yet understand. But she would.

She saw figures clad in workwear, large gloves and heavy aprons, moving through the street. More souls? Demons perhaps? She wasn’t sure, the eyes were always a tell but each figure here had them covered by thick goggles. The lenses reflected green light like an animal's eye caught in the dark. But she only saw those glimpses for a moment. They were busy with their work. Some pushed wheelbarrows of coal while others pulled at pulleys manipulating large parts of machinery.

It was ominous. It was magnificent.

And somewhere within it, Rio was watching over it all. Lording over it all.

The question tugged at her, nearly unbidden. Why did she make this place? Why did she give me a place within it?

She smirked again, caught in the odd wonder of it all. “Guess I’ll just have to find out.”

The curiosity simmered, sharpening the restlessness she felt. She left the window and paced back to the door, her fingers grazing the edge of a worn leather spine on the shelf. She picked it up, flipping through pages inked with runes she couldn’t decipher. Perhaps she would try; perhaps Rio would teach her.

Maybe, just maybe, she thought with a quiet thrill, there was more for her here than she could have ever imagined.

Chapter End Notes

putting the slow in slow burn. a rose by any other name and all that.

Tendril and Thorn

Chapter Summary

A change of perspective as Rio takes care of some housekeeping

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

She’d let the girl rest. Though she didn’t need it herself, mortal constitutions were more fragile than they realized. Even the spirited ones. Especially them.

She rolled her tongue over the inside of her cheek, running it across a small scar that had formed from many years of biting the inside of it. A bad habit. A reminder she could still feel pain.

It was a curious business, the coven sending this girl here. She wasn’t one to argue, a witch down below was one less to deal with up above. But she wondered. Why was this one their choice?

It was undoubtable that Agatha had a strong magic potential. That much was clear in the way the energies of the realm, Her realm, was reacting to the girl's presence. Perhaps that potential had frightened her coven. It was easier to send unruly women away than to deal with them.

Maybe that’s why she’d accepted the coven’s offer. Too many difficult women were sent to her in such untimely ways as it was. She felt no guilt, it wasn’t her doing, and souls were souls. But as she appraised them she wondered who they could have been, had someone been there to tend to them.

She wondered idly if Agatha would flourish under a bit of pruning, if given a trellis to wind her magic up and around.

A train whistle sounded, shaking her from her thoughts. Never mind lost witches. There were souls that needed to be attended to. More souls would be arriving shortly.

She closed her eyes and felt her body disperse into the atmosphere, her glamour dropping as she flew, half corporeal smoke half something resembling a human form. 

Rio passed through the streets with purpose, slipping into her routine as a way to anchor herself. She began her rounds, checking on the various areas of her domain—the factories where the workers toiled. But even as she carried out her business, her mind kept drifting back to Agatha. The memory of their brief exchange replayed in her thoughts, the challenge in Agatha’s eyes igniting a curiosity that she hadn’t felt in a few centuries. She couldn’t shake how piercing those clever blue eyes were.

In the heart of the city, where the machinery throbbed with life, each clank and hiss was a brash reminder of her responsibilities. Here, she directed the laborers, guiding their movements with a flick of her wrist, her voice commanding, laced with an authority that had been forged over countless years. The souls executed each order with precision.

Later, Rio found herself wandering towards the garden once more, a sanctuary amidst the chaos. The one place that carried the reminder of her origin as The green witch.

Once, she had been the caretaker of the grounds above and below. But as time had drawn on there had been many others to toil in the sun. To grow orchards and bend rivers. To make beautiful fields full of plant and animal life.

But no one ever wanted to cull the excess. No one but her recognized that there could be no appreciation of beauty without the threat of losing it. So she had taken up the responsibility of trimming back the world. Creating an After so that every living thing could appreciate the present.

It had been a gift.

It hadn't been received as one.

Their loss. For a time she had been bitter. But when you lived infinitely, you couldn't carry any one emotion forever.

She admired the garden again, the dark roses swayed slightly as if responding to her presence. She knelt beside them, running her fingers over the velvety petals, feeling the pulse of magic that surged within them. She murmured to the flowers, a rare moment of vulnerability creeping into her voice, “Keep an eye on her won’t you?” They swayed gently, their thorns glinting ominously in the dim light. 

Rio rose to her feet, “Perhaps it’s time to learn more about you, Agatha,” she whispered to the garden, as if it could somehow provide insight into the enigma that was the woman who had come to share her home.

She passed back through the winding paths of the city, her mind racing with possibilities. On the day of their bargain, Agatha had mentioned the unknown being an opportunity. Perhaps their perspectives were aligned. What could she teach the witch that would make her useful for the months when she returned to the surface? There was a hunger for knowledge, for power. Over her coven perhaps? Rio hoped her vision wasn’t that limited. 

Mortal squabbles were so uninteresting. Each and every one of them ended up here all the same. It wasn’t a fair fight. It was hardly a fight at all, she considered. But Agatha, she had challenged her. Her rapid heartbeat had given her away but all the same, she had snarked back at Rio in a way she hadn’t experienced ever. It wasn’t often that death got to live new experiences. It had been fun. Perhaps there was a way to nurture that.

She must be careful though. A spark of rebellion could rapidly spread into unruly flame. If Agatha had the drive, that Rio suspected she might, that would be enough to fuel her long enough for Rio to decide whether she would continue to prove interesting. 

Limited contact, she decided. That would be important. She began contemplating how best to observe Agatha from a distance, to understand her without being ensnared in the chaos of her emotions. I will not lose myself again, she vowed silently. It would be a trial—not just of Agatha’s resilience, but of her own strength to resist the pull of something so intoxicating. With her mind made up, Rio took one last look at the darkening cityscape. 

Though she wouldn’t engage directly, she still had work to do after all, she would observe, adapt, and prepare- for whatever this witch was to become. The dance between them had only just begun after all. Six months was a long time.

As she rematerialized at the gate that marked Cerberus’ territory, the air thickened with an ancient, primal energy. The great beast was a sight to behold—a mass of muscles and sinew, with three heads, each adorned with gleaming molten gold eyes. The central head bore a crown of jagged teeth, while the others were slightly smaller. They each carried their own personalities, the center head was fierce and unwavering, the second cunning and playful, while the third wise beyond mortal comprehension. It was a closely kept secret which was her favorite. But she definitely had one.

“Cerberus,” Rio called softly, her voice echoing in the stillness. “Come here, boy.”

The ground trembled slightly as Cerberus rose from his resting place, his massive frame stretching and yawning, revealing rows of sharp teeth. 

As he approached, the three heads moved in unison, tongues lolling out in eager anticipation as a giant tail wagged, splintering a stalagmite into hundreds of shards. Rio’s fingers brushed against his coarse fur, the warmth of his breath misting against the chill of the Underworld. “You’ve been a very good guardian while I’ve been away, haven’t you darling?” she murmured, feeling the usual comfort of their bond. He understood darkness and solitude as well as she did.

Cerberus responded with a low growl, his heads tilting slightly as if sensing her distraction. The beast nuzzled a head on either side of her, seeking her attention.

Drawing a deep breath, Rio reached into her cloak and summoned a scroll, its edges shimmering. It unfurled before her, revealing the names of the recently arrived souls she had collected in the days since her departure. Her fingers traced the names, pausing as one caught her attention—a vile man, a murderer who took lives carelessly, not out of malice but out of a twisted sense of enjoyment. She remembered him. How dare he believe that he could wield Her power

The fury that perpetually simmered within her resurfaced. This man had disrupted her schedule, sending several souls here far before their time,  and now he would pay the price. “Cerberus,” she commanded, her voice taking on an edge, “find this one.” She pointed to the name on the scroll, the words almost burning against her fingertips. “Make him regret his existence.”

Cerberus’s growl deepened, a rumbling sound that echoed in the chamber, his three heads nodding in eager agreement. He loved a good chase, and his instincts kicked in at the command.

Without hesitation, the beast bolted forward, a blur of fur and teeth, disappearing into the shadows with a single-minded determination. Rio could hear the echoes of his footfalls, a thunderous cadence that made the ground tremble beneath her. She knew Cerberus would not stop until he had hunted the man down, toying with him as a cat might with a mouse before taking his time tearing the man apart. Of course, the soul would reform in a few days, but if he was lucky by then she’d have someone new to take her annoyance out on. There were always more scoundrels.

As the sounds of the chase faded, a familiar sense of satisfaction washed over her—a cruel joy in the execution of justice. But this time, it was tempered by her earlier encounter. A part of her wished she could share this moment with the young witch, to see the way she would respond to the raw power of Cerberus. Would she be in awe?

Standing alone in the cold, echoing depths, the thrill of punishment felt hollow. The joy she once derived from such acts was muted, overshadowed today. How annoying.

With a heavy sigh, Rio started back toward her duties, the shadows of the Underworld welcoming her. She had souls to guide, energies to balance, and punishments to enforce—there was no time to dwell on a mortal who had stirred her interest. But as she moved through the winding paths, her thoughts remained tangled.

Reaching a particularly bustling district where the energy of the souls flowed like a river, she felt the familiar pulse of her realm. The factory machines clanked, and the air was thick with the scent of industry and carried the bitterness of mortal regret. Here, the souls labored under her watchful gaze, and she found a semblance of solace in the rhythm of their toil.

Yet, each soul’s weary expression reminded her of the young witch’s contrasting spirit upon arrival. That cheeky smirk. Petulant. She shook her head, trying to clear her thoughts as she approached a cluster of souls who had just arrived, fresh from the mortal world.

“Welcome,” she called, her voice carrying authority. “You’re dead. Sorry about your luck.”

A few of the souls cowered, groaning as they prostrated themselves. Pathetic.

“Why do you bother to moan? This place is inevitable. Don’t take it personally” she drawled, addressing no one in particular. “It only makes your time more painful.” 

The souls shifted uneasily at her words, but she continued, “You cannot change what has been done. Accept it and move on. There is work to be done.” 

Yet, as she spoke, she felt an unfamiliar twinge of frustration. Did human philosophy ever evolve? Was this still after centuries how they saw her? Just as cruel as the forces that had brought them to her? How simple of them. The thought festered, a nagging feeling she had long since buried.

She dismissed it, concentrating on the souls before her. The clever would operate machinery. The strong would haul coal and generate power. The obstinate would be sent to toil at the wall. It was an efficient system that she prided herself on.

When she had started here there was nothing. Not even ground or atmosphere, simply void. And now, she had built a full city, ever improving, just as alive as any up above. Full of little playthings to keep her entertained. Boredom had never suited her, and it certainly didn’t play out well for the overworld when she got restless. 

Every soul in her dominion had a purpose. All serving the expansion of her kingdom. Building shaded replicas of whatever took her fancy during her visits up above. Mortals were quite innovative, accomplishing what they did when the majority of them had to do without magic. 

An idea took root, a plan unfurling in her mind. If Agatha was to remain in her domain, she would need a role as well. 

With renewed purpose, Rio summoned a tendril of magic, allowing it to flow from her fingertips and into the earth. As she worked, she felt a shift in the air, the darkness around her humming with power and intent. Perhaps this would keep her from feeling too entangled in the girl’s fate. Perhaps she could remain detached, merely the orchestrator of events, while Agatha navigated the path before her.

“I will keep you at a distance,” she vowed, her voice firm. “But I will not let you slip through my grasp.”

As she finished her enchantments, she stood and took one last look across the realm, her eyes lingering on a purple crystal window, now illuminated with a growing light from within. 

In that moment, the chase had begun again—not for a soul to punish but for a spirit to grow.

Her ears perked as she heard sounds of a distant struggle, muted as if echoing underwater. Her lips curled into a grin. War was taking place somewhere above. Humans were so cyclical and predictable about these things. Like the clockwork that drove the machinery. She spared a parting glance at the window. It would be good for the girl to have time to settle in. 

And it would be good for Rio to have something to keep herself preoccupied.

To battle, she disappeared.

Communion

Chapter Summary

Rio hasn't been seen in days, and Agatha is tired of waiting for answers.

Chapter Notes

TW: Blood. There's a lot of it, if you're squeamish or eating this may not be the right read for you. Please heed the updated rating.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

In the days following her arrival, Agatha found herself once again wrapped in a familiar blanket of isolation. This time it felt heavier though, as if the very air conspired to remind her of her place. She’d explored as much of the Underworld as she dared, taking in its jagged landscapes, towering shadows, and hollow-sounding corridors. Yet for all her efforts, she hadn’t once caught sight of Rio.

She filled her days with a growing restlessness, like a caged animal in a world so vast yet so closed off to her. Every morning, she woke to the strange, muted light that filtered through this realm, casting everything in shades of ashen gray. She attempted to explore the crumbling halls, the shadowed gardens, and the cavernous stretches of Rio’s city. But apart from the garden, she found very little to work with. Each exploration only served to sharpen her impatience and, worse, her confusion about why Rio had given her free reign if only to leave her adrift.

On the first day, she tried to find the patterns in the strange underworld flora, the alien flowers with sharp thorns and glowing edges that seemed to whisper when she passed. Their vines twisted around each other, almost like they were conspiring. The flowers felt watchful, but when she would pause to examine them more closely, they’d seem to shrink back, as if sensing her intrusion.

By the second day, she’d wandered into the heart of the city, a place of industry, where the air was thick with metallic dust and acrid smoke. Though her instincts warned her not to touch anything, she couldn’t help but reach out toward the machinery now and then, trying to feel if it pulsed with the same dark magic that thrummed in the city’s bones. But by her assessment, this was mechanical, not magical in nature. Souls moved like shadows through the place, toiling away, their eyes hollow and unseeing guarded by heavy goggles. Agatha felt something twist in her chest as she watched them, feeling like an intruder in this strange routine of endless labor.

“Who are you? Come here often? Whatcha working on?” She’d tried all manner of trying to engage with these shades but they gave her no responses. Occasionally one of them would raise their head slightly and she’d feel a wave of mournful grief rush through her body. But no other indication that she had even been heard.

Through all these interactions, even when meddling with her subjects, there was no sign of Rio. No cool, knowing gaze in the dark. No sharp laugh to cut through the silence. Not even the barest whisper of her voice. Just nothing.

On the third day, her frustration reached a boiling point. She gazed at the mirror she had summoned, pulling her hair up and away from her eyes. Her thoughts churned as she stared at herself, seeing her own defiant, weary expression. Was this all just a game to Rio? A punishment for daring to challenge her? The endless waiting, the silence—this was a new kind of cruelty, one that she hadn’t prepared for.

“If you wanted to break my spirit,” she muttered aloud, voice swallowed by the oppressive quiet, “you could at least have the decency to face me while doing it.” Her own reflection glared back, a slight twist of bitterness in her eyes. If her words were heard by anyone else, they were not acknowledged.

It was later that day, when she found herself pacing along one of the garden paths, muttering half-formed spells just to have something to do, that she began to think she’d felt something. A familiar prickling, that sensation she’d felt when Rio was close. She stilled, gaze darting around. But there was nothing. Just the same empty, yawning silence.

The disappointment stung, and she felt her frustration slip closer to anger. She thought about calling Rio’s name. But she could already imagine how pathetic and desperate it would sound. Her voice echoing off the cold, stony walls of the garden, unanswered, swallowed by the looming shadows. No, she couldn’t have that. She wasn’t here to beg.

By the fourth day, she’d grown almost resigned to feeling like a guest forgotten in a house that didn’t care if she stayed or left. But there was still something defiant left in her. It simmered under her skin. She carried it like a curse, like a vow. She would not let Rio’s cold silence chip away at her resolve.

When she finally stumbled upon the dark cathedral, its monolithic structure looming high above, she felt an electric pull in her chest. For the first time, something in this realm called to her, a presence that didn’t just watch but beckoned. It was then that she knew—whatever this place held, it was finally offering her an invitation.

Agatha walked with purpose, squaring her shoulders as she approached. Maybe Rio would find her here, or maybe she wouldn’t. Either way, she was done waiting.

It was gothic in design of course but with no windows, just empty spaces between the walls. A dark wood door stood thirteen feet tall but as she approached she saw no discernable handle or knocker.

Rio had warned her about touching things she didn’t understand. But this place had called to her. Surely that wasn’t a mistake.

As she approached she noticed something out of place. A small splinter sticking out of the wood at a jagged right angle. Too obvious of a placement to be an accident.

She pressed her thumb to the splinter. Unsurprisingly it bit into her skin, sinking under the surface. Then the warm spring of blood, just a few drops, spilling against the door.

With a groan, the doors slowly swung inward. An invitation.

She crossed the threshold, her footfalls echoing as she walked over the transition from stone to dark marble. The interior of this place was similar to a cathedral but seemed neverending. A long cavernous mouth, illuminated by hundreds of candles lighting a path forward. 

It was hard to get a sense of the scale of this place she realized. It reeked of illusion. And if it was an illusion, it meant it had to have been crafted with intention. Her steps echoed as she continued forward, that hook in her stomach drawing her in. She wasn’t entirely sure if her feet moved by her own will or if something greater had tethered her here. No matter, she was here all the same.

An echo sounded, louder than her footsteps as the doors closed behind her.

Eventually, her eyes focused on a spot where the floor grew more reflective. The flickering candlelight was dancing across a new surface of some kind. As she approached, she looked down and saw a dark reflection of herself looking back up at her.

Agatha gazed down, captivated by the reflection at her feet, the liquid shimmering almost completely black in the dim candlelight. The surface was smooth, unnaturally so. Its depth was impossible to gauge. She tentatively knelt next to the pool, and the slick, glistening surface seemed to ripple, tiny waves moving outward as if responding to her presence alone.

A coppery tang hit her nose—subtle at first, then sharper, filling her senses until it was undeniable. Her heart stilled as the realization sank in. This wasn’t water.

Blood.

The vast pool lay before her, an expanse of thick, crimson fluid, dense as oil. Its surface mirrored the cathedral’s arches and the looming shadows above, but the reflection was distorted, a dark echo that twisted the light and seemed to absorb it. The candles’ glow danced off the viscous surface, casting eerie streaks that gleamed like rubies.

A sense of weight settled over her, as she stared into the pool. At closer inspection, the blood’s surface broke in places, tiny bubbles rising and bursting, sighing and settling with each breath. She couldn’t tear her eyes away, drawn by both revulsion and fascination. Her reflection looked back at her, her eyes hollow and deep as the depths beneath her.

Agatha felt her pulse race, yet she didn’t move away. The call she had felt since entering now seemed to emanate from this pool itself. It was whispering something to her, though the words remained just beyond her grasp.

She considered the closest analog she had to this pool in front of her. A baptismal. Something people thought they could cleanse themselves in, and use as a vessel to become closer to the god they worshiped. 

Communion.

The thought grew in her mind, unfurling. If this place was calling her, as Rio’s realm had seemed to from the moment of her arrival, perhaps it wasn’t just her place just to observe. Perhaps it was drawing her into a ritual, one that demanded her participation—demanded her surrender.

The pool’s surface held fast, a twisted baptismal font. Blood, rather than water, marked it as something not meant for absolution, but initiation. This wasn’t about cleansing away sins. This was a communion of power. And power wasn't a sin.

What if this was a well she could draw upon? Her hands tingled at the thought of it, her skin prickling with anticipation. This pool was calling her not as a guest, but as a participant, urging her to partake in a sacrament of flesh and blood. "So dramatic," she whispered.

She felt an urge rise in her, primal and raw. Beckoning, no, demanding her to dip her hands into the crimson depths, to feel this ancient reservoir seep into her skin. She could almost hear it—a soft hum, a murmur in the still air. It was as if the pool was promising her something—a connection, a link to something far older than her coven’s teachings, something that whispered of understanding and unclaimed energy.

Without breaking her gaze from the pool, she slipped off her shoes, her feet connecting with the cold, unyielding marble at its edge. A thrill shot through her—a recognition that she was on the verge of crossing into something forbidden. She inhaled deeply, steeling herself, the iron tang in the air filling her lungs.

Carefully, Agatha dipped the tips of her fingers just below the surface. The blood was ice cold but her face felt almost feverish. Tiny eddies formed where she touched, swirling outward, and she was mesmerized by the way her fingers emerged stained.

This would be her communion. She would let this realm claim her if only to see what it might reveal in return.

Rising from her crouched position, she dipped one foot into the pool, finding purchase on a step invisible underneath the thick surface. Her other foot followed. Another step down.

The pool was more frigid than she’d expected and she gasped as she descended deeper. As the pool lapped at her ribs and breasts, the cold ripped the breath from her lungs. But no revelations. No change in the air or space around her. No, she wasn't in deep enough yet. You couldn't reach only halfway for something just beyond your grasp.

Agatha grimaced again. The smell of iron was even more pungent and repulsive, she felt her stomach churn in response. No going back. If her lady had meant for her to find this place then surely she expected her to make something of it. She inhaled deeply, and then took a step forward, realizing simultaneously that the steps ended here, and there was nothing left awaiting but the embrace of the ritual. She submerged herself completely.

Below the surface she forced her eyes to open but could make out nothing in the murky space around her. Looking up she realized she couldn’t even see the flickering light from the surface above. Her heart began to speed up, panic and animal instinct beginning to take over.

It wasn’t lost on her that drowning had long been a true way to kill her kin.

As her dread grew she tried to force herself to swim back to the surface but her limbs were heavy and wouldn’t carry her. She swore and then cursed herself as she watched a few bubbles of precious air float away.

Fully panicking now she began to writhe, seeking her surroundings for anything to aid her. But there was nothing.

A thought sparked in her mind and then rooted itself in her stomach and heart with a cruel unflinching certainty. She had miscalculated. She was going to die here. In seeking power, instead, she’d found oblivion.

The last bit of air left her and she felt the thick oppressive liquid flow into her mouth, filling her throat and lungs. Stubbornly she kept her eyes open. For some reason, she thought of Rio at that moment. At the very least she knew that she’d be seeing a familiar face soon.

What would her reaction be? Would she be angry? Amused? Was Agatha the first, or just the most recent prey to fall into this snare?

Agatha finally closed her eyes and submitted to the void around her.

Quiet. Empty. Cold. Still.

“I thought witches bathing in the blood of virgins was an old wives tale?”

Her eyes sprung open.

Rio was sprawled haphazardly over a large throne, legs dangling carelessly over the arms as she spun a wicked curved knife between her hands. Completely nonchalant. Totally unsurprised to see Agatha here, covered in blood.

Agatha gasped and realized she could draw breath here. She was standing, no longer in the pool but somewhere else entirely. A comfortable room, an audience chamber perhaps based on the throne. She noticed she was actively dripping blood all over what was probably a beautiful and ornate rug.

“Blood of virgins?” She choked out, pushing away her thick matted hair and wiping the blood from her eyes the best she could. “Is that why it spit me out?”

Rio laughed, languidly leaning further back. “No,” she mused, sheathing the dagger and turning her head to grin wolfishly at Agatha. “It’s not that regressive.” She stood from the throne and stalked towards Agatha eyeing her curiously.

“Try again.” She challenged.

Agatha bristled a bit and spat, blood flying from her mouth and landing next to Rio’s boot. “Another lesson? Don’t go where I’m not invited? You here to reprimand me?”

Rio chuckled shaking her head. “Nope,” she said popping her lips around the word. “Next?”

“Well, you showed up.”

“You called me.” Rio said simply, taking another step closer. Two slender fingers passed down Agatha’s jaw, collecting the blood from her face.

Agatha flinched, her eyes darting to Rio’s hand.

“Well… I had to get your attention. You brought me here and then ignored me. For days I haven’t seen or heard from you. I thought we had agreed that I was brought here to learn from you.”

Rio smirked and raised an eyebrow. So lowly that Agatha had to strain to hear her, she seemed to draw out every word, “you are here, as my consort." 

“By what definition?” 

Rio’s hand froze mid-motion, her gaze narrowing slightly as if Agatha had just struck a nerve she hadn’t meant to expose. Then, in a whisper of amusement, her smirk returned, sly and shadowed. 

“By my definition,” Rio replied, her fingers tracing back down Agatha’s jaw with a deliberate slowness.

Agatha felt a heat rise under her skin, not entirely from anger this time. She clenched her jaw and met Rio’s gaze, refusing to give her the satisfaction of a reaction. “So you drag me into that… that pool”—she grimaced, wiping more of the blood from her face and flinging it off her hand to the ground—"just to toy with me?”

Rio’s eyes glinted, and her voice dropped into a mockingly gentle tone. “Ah, so you thought you could just wander through my domain, plunge into its darkest depths, and come back unscathed?” She traced her bloodied fingers down Agatha’s collarbone, exposing pale slivers of skin as the blood smeared. “A consort doesn’t just watch from a distance, Agatha. You’re expected to understand the marrow of this place.”

“So… it was a test?” Agatha asked, the defiance in her voice tempered by an uneasy curiosity.

Rio hummed, her gaze lingering on Agatha. “An amuse-bouche if you will,” she replied, her voice rippling with humor. “The blood you were having your little spa day in? It’s the collective history of this realm. Souls come and go, but the essence—the raw emotions, the power, the failures and fears—that stays. Those who are worthy can draw upon it.” Her eyes gleamed, and she leaned in close to her ear. “And the unworthy ones? They drown.”

Agatha’s skin crawled, and she felt a strange pull in her chest at the thought. This was more than a simple game. There was power at work here, and Rio wielded it like a weapon. 

“Suppose I… am worthy. What then?” she asked.

Rio’s smile was slow and sly, as if savoring Agatha’s defiance. “Then,” she said, “you’ll learn how to wield that power. But first, you have to prove yourself. Show me you won’t crumble under its weight.”

Agatha straightened, reaching up to wring some of the blood from her hair and wrinkling her nose as she felt it flow down her neck. She wasn’t sure if it was the warmth caused by Rio’s touch, or her own stubborn resolve, but something surged within her. “Fine. Then show me how to start.”

Rio’s laughter echoed softly through the chamber, low and dangerous. “Not here,” she purred, casting an appraising look at Agatha. “The real trials come soon enough. This is just the first taste.”

Her blood-stained fingertips drifted back up the column of her neck, over her jaw, to rest against Agatha’s lips.

Agatha had wondered before if she was feral. There was no absolutely no questioning that fact now. Her lips parted slightly, tongue flicking out, tasting the blood at the fingers offered to her.

“Delicious,” she growled, not recognizing her own low and hungry voice.

Rio grinned manically, fully baring her teeth as she gripped Agatha’s chin between her fingers.

“I was so hoping you’d think so, sweetheart.”

Chapter End Notes

this one is for anyone who is a little freak for sexy blood magic. these witches definitely are.

Worship

Chapter Summary

Power is played with, an agreement is reached.

Chapter Notes

As a commenter put it (love y'all), they match each other's freak. Friendly reminder that there's still a lot of blood involved.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Agatha had shared kisses before. Some early ones had even been sweet. Gentle promises, little whispers, “Come closer—do you like that—can I touch you here?” Others eager as her confidence grew, “Just like that honey—let me feel you—you’re so good.” She recalled hands woven in her hair, pinching at her breasts, slipping between her thighs. Her own hands, unfastening buttons, under skirts, over a mouth. 

Not one of those dalliances could have prepared her. Not for the way she hungered, the way her whole body felt starved. She didn’t feel out of her body. She had never felt more alive than just now, her chin cradled in death’s hand.

She reached out, just as desperately as she had when she thought she was drowning. Grabbing at the back of Rio’s head she crashed into her. She kissed her. And as she did she felt something deeply buried purr with content.
