“I just thought I’d try…to make it grow,” Agatha said, almost sheepishly. "I don’t really know why it’s working, or how. But I think maybe…these plants are connecting to me.” She looked at Rio, suddenly worried. “If it bothers you, I can stop. But...it feels different, like this place is responding to me.”

Rio’s gaze softened as she looked at Agatha. She took Agatha’s hand, tracing patterns absentmindedly with her thumb. “Don’t stop. I told you the garden was yours to tend to. You’re changing things here, that much is clear.”

Agatha felt a warmth in Rio’s touch, and before she could think twice, she squeezed her hand and asked, “Come to bed with me tonight. Just stay close for a while.”

Rio arched a brow, her lips curving in a wry smile. “I don’t sleep, remember?”

“I know,” Agatha replied, her voice soft. “But… I just want you nearby.”

Rio studied her for a moment, as if trying to read her intentions, then gave a slight nod. “Fine. I’ll stay as long as you need.”

Together, they walked back through the hallways of the dark fortress, Rio silent and watchful by her side. The rooms felt less oppressive with Rio there, her silent presence a balm to the shadows and her steps the only echo beside Agatha’s. When they reached Agatha’s chambers, she removed her outer clothes and climbed into bed, settling against the cool, crisp sheets. Rio sank beside her, not touching her but close enough she could feel her weight on the bed, quiet, her gaze roaming over the dark room.

As the night wore on, Agatha felt herself drifting off, the warmth of Rio’s hand still lingering in her memory. Her last glimpse was of Rio, still and watchful as ever, her gaze cast out towards the window where a faint, silvery light filtered through.

In the middle of the night, she felt an arm tentatively wrap around her waist. Half asleep she tried to roll towards the touch, but the arm tightened, holding her close. Holding her in place. Agatha mumbled in her sleep and nestled back against the body pressed against her. As she drifted back to sleep she swore she heard a low pleased hum against her hair.

In the morning, Agatha awoke, stretching as the last remnants of sleep faded. Her room was quiet, but her heart sank a little as she noticed she was alone. She thought for a moment she’d dreamed it all—Rio's warmth, her quiet presence by her side. But then, her eyes fell on the pillow next to her, where a single flower lay.

She recognized it immediately, a symbol of memory, something left in places of significance, a token of promise.

She held it in her hand, letting her fingers trace the delicate petals. A faint smile tugged at her lips, despite the solitude of the moment. Even if Rio wasn’t there in person, the bloom meant she hadn’t truly left.

Just then, a soft breeze stirred through the room, carrying with it the faintest whisper of Rio’s chuckle, though Agatha couldn’t tell if it was her imagination or something more. It felt like a promise, a gentle reminder that Rio hadn’t gone as far as the shadows suggested.

And perhaps, in some ways, she hadn’t left at all.

Chapter End Notes

no finale spoilers here, but as a writer, empty space is such a wonderful gift to get to play with. I hope you'll stick with me and other stories about these two for a long time. we're only just beginning.

Lay Me Down

Chapter Summary

Power and possibility. Promises. Above ground, the season carries on. Spring approaches.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

The days began to blur together as Agatha and Rio fell into their quiet rhythm—a wordless understanding that carried them from one day to the next. The tension that hung between them, though subtle, was unmistakable; Agatha could feel it in the way Rio’s eyes lingered on her sometimes, and in her own racing heartbeat whenever Rio was near. It was like standing on the edge of something vast and unknown. 

The mysteries of the underworld were not the most interesting secrets here. All the same, when Rio was away, the call of the magic buried in that awful bloody pool beckoned her.

Agatha kneeled now, beside the pool, the dark surface reflecting an image of herself. She pressed her fingers to the surface, focusing her intent, letting the quiet stillness of the cathedral fall away until all that was left was the pool’s unyielding depth. Just as she began to pull her awareness inward, a sudden image flared into her mind, vivid and unsettling.

The lush, vibrant garden she’d come to adore was withered and gray, the foliage brittle and lifeless. Shadeblooms, which usually glowed faintly, now lay scattered in strange, chaotic patterns, dotting the floor with dark, shriveled petals.

The silence was oppressive. She couldn’t feel Rio’s presence, a hollow ache settling in her chest as she reached out, but her hand only brushed cold air. She focused her mind and a new image formed. The throne was vacant, its form barely visible in the dim, unnatural darkness that seemed to swallow every inch of the room. Agatha stumbled forward, the weight of what she saw pressing in on her until—

The vision shattered, the pool rippling under her fingertips as she gasped, her breath ragged.

A moment later, she sensed Rio’s presence beside her, solid and steady. Agatha turned to face her, still reeling, her heart racing as the images from the vision lingered like ghostly afterimages in her mind.

Rio’s face softened, concern flickering in her eyes. “What did you see?” she asked, voice soft but edged with a faint tension.

“I… I saw the throne room. Empty. And everything was… wrong,” Agatha whispered, unable to shake the strange weight that had settled over her. She forced herself to meet Rio’s gaze. “It felt like something was missing.”

Rio’s expression didn’t change, though Agatha saw something flicker in her eyes—an understanding, perhaps, or something deeper. But as quickly as it came, it was gone, replaced by her familiar, composed mask.

“That was only a vision,” Rio said evenly, but Agatha could feel the slight hesitation in her words. “Magic can reveal many things, not all of them real. Sometimes we see what we want.”

Agatha nodded slowly, yet the vision continued to gnaw at her, an insidious doubt creeping into her thoughts. She needed answers, something more than Rio’s quiet reassurances. She wanted Rio to tell her what the vision meant, to let her in on the mysteries that seemed to keep them separated.

“Is there something you’re not telling me?” Agatha pressed voice barely a whisper. “Something about… about all of this?”

Rio’s eyes met hers, steady and unflinching, but instead of answering, she turned her gaze back to the pool, her silence like a heavy curtain drawn between them. The distance Agatha had felt earlier seemed to swell, taking root in that single unanswered question, the quiet between them fraught with an unspoken truth that Rio refused to share.

After a moment, Rio stood, her hand hovering over Agatha’s shoulder for a fleeting second, as though she wanted to say something more but couldn’t find the words. And then she was gone, leaving Agatha by the pool, her heart caught in a place between wonder and fear.

Agatha growled in frustration. She would not be deterred. If Rio wouldn’t give her answers, she would take them.

Determined, Agatha returned her focus to the pool's shimmering depths, her mind racing. The whisper of possibilities beckoned her, promising secrets she had yet to uncover. She needed to know the full extent of her power, to command it and prove that she was more than just a visitor in this realm—she was a force to be reckoned with.

At the edge again, the familiar sense of trepidation coursed through her veins, but she quickly silenced it. She had faced dark things before, and had embraced the unknown. This time would be no different.

Taking a deep breath, Agatha focused on the surface, allowing her fingertips to skim the pool’s edge. She felt the energy thrumming beneath her skin, a familiar pulse that sang to her instincts. Closing her eyes, she began to chant softly, weaving words of summoning that were unfamiliar but seemed to spring forth from her very bones. The incantation hung in the air, charged with a sense of urgency and ambition.

The blood began to swirl, its surface rippling like a restless sea, the deep burgundy and crimson blurring into a chaotic dance. Agatha felt exhilarated; she was touching the very fabric of magic itself. She pushed deeper into her thoughts, envisioning something to summon, perhaps a guiding spirit, someone who could provide the insight that Rio had denied.

But as the incantation built, so too did the power, swirling wildly around her. Agatha’s focus began to waver, the chaotic energy spinning out of her control. Tendrils of magic lashed out, wrapping around her, pulling her toward the dark edge of the veil—the thin barrier between the living world and something beyond the boundaries of the realm she found herself in now.

As she was drawn closer to the void, the world around her began to distort. She could see it now—a swirling darkness, a vast expanse of emptiness, where the echoes of lost souls lingered like distant whispers. The shadows writhed like smoke, swirling and coiling around her, their shapes shifting and pulsating with an eerie life of their own.

Agatha's heart raced as she realized she was teetering on the brink of something far more dangerous than she had anticipated. Panic surged through her as she felt herself being pulled into the void, shadows encroaching from every side, their wispy forms clawing at her, trying to drag her into their depths. The air felt thick and heavy, filled with the muffled cries of those who had been lost—specters of despair and longing that echoed in the recesses of her mind.

“Agatha!” 

The commanding voice cut through the chaos like a beacon. Rio’s presence ignited a flame of recognition, grounding her in the midst of the spiraling shadows. Agatha felt the grip of the darkness falter as Rio rushed forward, her expression a blend of fury and fear.

“What have you done?” 

Agatha gasped, fighting against the tide of energy that threatened to drag her further away. “I— I was just trying to see! I thought I could control it!”

“Control it?” Rio’s voice rose, sharp and slicing through the panic. “You’re playing with forces you don’t understand! This is not a game, Agatha. You could have been lost here permanently!”

With a swift motion, Rio extended her hand toward Agatha, channeling her own magic to counteract the swirling chaos. Agatha felt the familiar warmth of Rio’s power envelop her, anchoring her to the present, and pulling her back from the precipice of despair.

The shadows writhed in defiance, and Agatha could almost hear their lament, the cries of the forsaken who lingered at the edge of existence. They were not willing to lose their prize. The darkness felt alive, an ever-hungry void yearning to consume, and for a fleeting moment, she understood the fragility of her own life.

Just as the shadows began to close in again, Rio’s magic surged, a brilliant flash of green light that pierced through the gloom. Agatha felt the shadows retreat, their whispers fading into nothingness. She found herself collapsing back onto solid marble, breathless and trembling.

As she looked up at Rio, who knelt beside her, the intensity lingered in the air like static. “Do you understand the danger you were in?” Rio’s voice was fierce.

“I… I didn’t mean to—” Agatha stammered, shame flooding through her. “I thought… I thought it could bring me closer to—”

Rio shook her head, her anger palpable. “You must respect boundaries, Agatha. Otherwise, you risk losing everything.”

The silence stretched between them, heavy with the gravity of what had just happened. Agatha looked away, ashamed. “I didn’t think…”

“I know,” Rio interrupted, her voice softer now. “But that is why I’m here—to help you navigate this place. You must trust me, Agatha, as I trust you.”

Agatha nodded, her heart aching with the reality of her actions.

“I will,” she promised, a newfound resolve settling within her. “I’ll be more careful. I don’t want to lose...” She trailed off not quite knowing how to finish that thought.

Rio took a deep breath, the tension in her shoulders easing slightly as she met Agatha’s gaze. “Then listen to me. There is much you can learn, but it requires patience and respect for the magic we’re dealing with.”

Agatha nodded.

That evening, as the glow of twilight settled across the garden, Agatha found herself watching Rio from across a fountain that she had conjured here a few days ago. She was arranging a few of the luminous Shadeblooms, their soft glow casting her face in ethereal light, and Agatha felt the familiar pull, an ache she didn’t quite understand but had long since stopped resisting. She walked over to where Rio stood, her footsteps soft against the stone, and reached out to place a hand on Rio’s shoulder.

Rio glanced at her, something else beyond her earlier frustration in her gaze tonight—something heavier, as if she, too, could feel the unspoken words weighing down the silence.

Agatha’s fingers tightened slightly on Rio’s shoulder, grounding herself. “I know you’re still mad about the pool. I just… I want to understand it better. I feel close to unlocking something. But I feel like I’m not going to have enough time. Have you… ever thought about it?” she asked softly, her voice barely more than a whisper. “What it might be like if I just… stayed?”

Rio’s expression didn’t change, but her hand stilled over the flowers, her gaze fixed on something distant. For a long moment, she didn’t speak, and Agatha felt a pang of fear that she had gone too far, that she’d shattered the delicate balance they had managed to build.

But then Rio turned to face her, and her eyes softened, though there was still that impenetrable shadow in them. “It’s not as if I don’t think about it,” she murmured, her voice low and even. “But… you belong to a world that’s bigger than this. One that can give you more than I can here. Remember what you came here for? Don’t get distracted.”

Agatha’s heart twisted at the words, an ache that settled into her bones. She took a step closer, reaching out to gently touch Rio’s face as if she could somehow make her understand the depth of her feelings through that one simple gesture. “What if I don’t want more? What if… this is enough?”

Rio’s eyes closed briefly, as though she were savoring the touch, or maybe bracing herself against it. When she looked at Agatha again, her gaze was filled with a mixture of affection and something darker—acceptance, perhaps, of the very thing she was holding at arm’s length.

“Don’t say that now. You don’t mean it,” she said, her voice so soft it was almost lost in the rustle of leaves around them. “When the time comes, Agatha, you may see things differently. You may find that what you want… has changed.”

Agatha shook her head, feeling a flash of frustration. “Why do you always do that?” she demanded, her voice laced with a bitterness she hadn’t meant to show. “Why do you keep putting distance between us, as if you’re already… preparing to lose me?”

Rio’s expression grew pained, but she didn’t look away. “Because I know what it’s like to want something you can’t keep,” she replied, her voice heavy. “And I’ve learned that sometimes, it’s easier to let go before it hurts too much.”

The words cut deep, and Agatha felt the sting of tears prick at the corners of her eyes. She wanted to argue, to tell Rio that it didn’t have to be that way, but part of her knew that Rio’s fears weren’t unfounded. A deal was a deal and neither pacts between witches nor death were easily broken.

Taking a steadying breath, she took Rio’s hand in hers, intertwining their fingers. “Then let me be the one to decide that,” she said firmly. “I want to be here—I chose to be here—isn’t that enough?”

For a long moment, Rio didn’t answer, and Agatha feared she might pull away, and retreat back into that guarded place that Agatha could never quite reach. But instead, Rio’s fingers tightened around hers, her gaze softening, and Agatha felt the faintest hint of a smile.

“It is enough,” Rio murmured at last, her voice barely more than a whisper. “For now.”

The words should have been a comfort, but they only deepened the ache in Agatha’s chest. This promise was fragile, as though it could shatter with the slightest push. Yet, she held on, clinging to the warmth of Rio’s hand and the closeness that, for now, was enough.

The garden around them was hushed tonight, steeped in a comforting darkness that made the faintly glowing blooms seem almost ethereal. 

Agatha settled beneath sweeping tendrils of the willow tree that had grown rapidly to now stand proudly at its full height. She leaned against the bark as the leaves played their own kind of music as they brushed against the grass and stone. After a moment, Rio joined her. She surprised Agatha as she moved to lay down, resting her head in Agatha’s lap. 

Her anger and fear from before had simmered. Now she just looked tired. She relaxed now and Agatha scratched at her temples, both content, enjoying the quiet company. Perhaps it was easier if they didn’t speak. She focused on the solid warmth of her presence, listening to the rhythmic rise and fall of her breathing. It was peaceful—too peaceful, in fact, for the thoughts stirring within her.

Curiosity gnawed at Agatha. It had been weeks, maybe a month, or perhaps more. It was hard to tell the passage of time in this strange place. Beyond the whistle of the train signaling more souls arriving there was nothing to mark any difference between one moment and the next. And despite however much time had or hadn’t passed, this strange, compelling woman against her felt like a mystery she’d only begun to unravel. Every so often, there’d be a look or a stray comment, something that hinted at a life before, at experiences Agatha couldn’t imagine. She knew so little, and after everything they’d shared, this unknowing was starting to feel like a barrier she wanted to cross.

“You know,” Agatha began quietly, her voice soft, testing the waters, “you’ve never really told me much about… well, yourself.”

Rio’s posture stiffened ever so slightly, a subtle shift that only someone close could notice, though she didn’t pull away. Her eyes were fixed on a night-blooming flower nearby, its dark purple petals curling open in the cool air.

“What are you wanting to know?” Rio replied lightly, though her tone held a faint edge.

“Anything, really. I mean… I don’t even know how you became… this,” Agatha said, choosing her words with care, though her curiosity was earnest. “Or if you’ve always been this way.” She glanced down at Rio, hoping for a glance in return, but Rio remained unmoved, her gaze distant. 

Rio took a deep breath, finally letting her head fall from Agatha’s lap and she rolled to her back, looking up at the starless sky. “There’s not much to tell. Or at least, not much that would make any sense.”

“Try me,” Agatha urged, her voice warm and encouraging. She slipped down the tree until she was lying on her side facing Rio. She reached out and placed her hand on her ribs, trying to coax her into opening up. “I just want to know more about you. I know you’re supposed to be this mysterious being beyond comprehension,” she teased before her voice grew gentle again. “But I know there’s more to you than that.”

For a moment, Rio’s expression softened, a brief vulnerability flashing across her face. But it was gone as quickly as it had appeared, replaced by a neutral mask, and Agatha felt her skin grow colder under her touch. She watched her hand rise and fall against Rio’s ribcage as the woman breathed in the cool air.

“There are some things, Agatha,” Rio said, her voice low, almost reluctant, “that are better left unspoken. My past is one of them.”

Agatha hesitated, trying to gauge how far she could push without losing this moment of closeness. “I don’t mean to pry… but, don’t you think it’s only fair I start to know more? I mean… after everything.”

Rio’s gaze finally met hers, but her eyes were guarded, a flicker of something—regret?—in their depths. “I’m not hiding things to be cruel,” she replied, a slight edge creeping into her voice. “But whatever you imagine, I can promise you it’s not nearly as interesting as you’d hope.” She moved her hand to cover Agatha’s.

Agatha could feel the distance creeping back in as if an invisible wall had slipped between them despite their current closeness. Her chest tightened, and she scrambled to keep the connection alive.

“Try me. I’m not looking for some fairytale,” she countered, trying to keep her tone light. “I just… I want to understand you better. Who you are now and who you were.”

Rio sighed, her jaw tightening. She rolled to face Agatha fully, her expression harder than Agatha was used to seeing it, an almost steely resolve taking hold. “The woman, whatever I was, Agatha… she doesn’t exist anymore. She hasn’t for a very very long time.” Her voice carried a note of finality. “You’re asking me to dig up a grave.”

Agatha sat in silence, her mind racing as she considered Rio’s words. Part of her wanted to push further, to pry open that closed door and reach the woman behind it. But the tension in Rio’s posture, the way she seemed to withdraw into herself, gave her pause. Agatha didn’t want to drive her away.

A heavy quiet settled between them, broken only by the soft rustle of leaves in the breeze. After a long moment, Agatha tried to bridge the gap again, this time with a softer touch. Her hand moved to trail along Rio’s arm.

“I didn’t mean to push,” she said quietly. “I just… I care about you.”

Rio’s expression softened just a fraction, though her eyes remained shadowed. “I know.” She reached out, touching Agatha’s face briefly, letting her thumb brush against her cheek before pulling back. “Just… don’t expect me to be someone I’m not.”

Agatha managed a small, sad smile. “I wouldn’t dream of it.”

Rio nodded, but said nothing more. They lay together in silence, closer yet separated by an invisible chasm that Agatha could feel widening even as Rio remained by her side. She had wanted honesty, and she had it—though the truth, it seemed, came with its own form of distance.

Agatha couldn’t shake the feeling that Rio had drifted to a place she could never follow. Like when she made her trips above to the surface. She always came back, but then always left again. And Agatha couldn’t help but consider again the time that had already passed here. For the first time, returning to the surface seemed like a hollow thing. 

As the minutes passed, the garden around them began to feel colder, more shadowed, and Agatha was left with a deep ache—a sense that something precious was slipping through her fingers, though she couldn’t say why. 

Agatha lay there, quiet, staring at the canopy of leaves above, and felt that emptiness settle deep in her chest. The months were creeping by faster than she’d anticipatedd, and the realization struck her with a clarity she hadn’t prepared for. Soon, her time here would be over—this strange, miraculous sanctuary she’d carved out with Rio would be gone. 

Initially, she had been so sure of herself, convinced that her return to the surface would be triumphant. She’d envisioned herself unlocking her powers, mastering them, rising to face her coven with undeniable proof of her strength. She’d imagined the awe on their faces, the respect that would be hard-earned but at last freely given. It was a fantasy she had clung to, like armor, against all her uncertainties. But now, that triumphant return felt like a faded echo of something she no longer wanted. The thought of stepping away from Rio, from this place, was unbearably bitter.

Agatha shifted on the ground, her hand trailing across the grass as she fought the impulse to reach for Rio again, to cling to her as if that could make everything stop. Her voice came out in a whisper, almost as if she were afraid of the truth in it.

“You know, when I first came here, I thought this was just… a stepping stone.” She hesitated, searching for the right words. “I thought it would lead me somewhere bigger, somewhere more… victorious.”

Rio didn’t speak, but her eyes flickered with an intensity that showed she was listening.

“I just wanted to be powerful,” Agatha continued, voice laced with an unfamiliar edge of bitterness. “To return with this great, undeniable magic, enough to make my coven see what I could be. To prove I was… worthy.” She shook her head, a soft, rueful laugh escaping. “But now that feels… small. Empty.”

Rio’s gaze softened, but still held a hint of that guarded sorrow she always kept close. “Why does it feel empty now?” she asked quietly.

“Because I didn’t know what I’d find here,” Agatha murmured, her eyes searching Rio’s face, though Rio wouldn’t quite meet her gaze fully. “I didn’t know I’d find something—someone—worth more than all that. I’m not ready. I want more time.”

Rio’s expression flickered, a flash of something raw that she quickly tried to cover, her mouth pressed into a thin line. “You have a life beyond here, Agatha,” she said, her voice low and carefully neutral. “A future, a path to follow. I won’t be the thing that takes you from that. That wasn’t the bargain.”

Agatha’s hand moved to rest over Rio’s heart, as though holding her there could keep her from slipping away. “But what if I don’t want that deal anymore? What if I found something here that means more than whatever might be waiting for me up there?”

Rio’s eyes darkened, her face an unreadable mask, and Agatha felt a flicker of frustration at how effortlessly Rio managed to retreat behind it, shutting her out. For weeks, they had fallen into a quiet, intimate rhythm. They’d spent countless nights like this, their silences filled with an unspoken trust. But now, with her heart laid bare, Agatha felt more alone than she had in a long time.

“I know what it’s like to let go of a path,” Rio finally said, her voice barely more than a murmur. “And sometimes… what you find after isn’t always what you hoped.”

Agatha could feel the distance creeping back, but something in her resisted. She felt a swell of resentment, raw and unexpected, toward the world above that expected her to return—to be the same person she had been when she left. She wasn’t. She wasn’t sure she could ever be.

She leaned closer, voice trembling with something fierce and desperate. “But I don’t want to look back at this as some… some passing thing.”

Rio’s jaw tightened, and for a moment, her hand brushed against Agatha’s cheek, her fingers featherlight, as if caught between the urge to hold on and the knowledge that she shouldn’t. “Sometimes, things are meant to be beautiful for a moment, Agatha. That’s what makes them precious,” she said, her voice barely audible

The words hung in the air like a finality, and Agatha felt a chill settle into her bones. She could feel the expiration date looming over them, and the thought made her sick. She closed her eyes, leaning into Rio’s hand as if she could will it to stay, as if she could hold onto the warmth of this night forever.

She opened her eyes and took in Rio’s face, committing it to memory with a quiet desperation she hadn’t anticipated. She wanted to speak, to promise she would stay, that they could find a way. But the words wouldn’t come.

And somewhere, in the back of her mind, she realized the quiet darkness of the garden wasn’t as peaceful as it had seemed. It was the silence of something precious slipping away.

“We still have time though,” she said thoughtfully.

“And there will be more,” Rio murmured. “Don’t forget that. You do have to return. That deal is done. But you’ll get to come home.” Her lips quirked, displeased at her own words, as if she’d given something away.

Agatha studied Rio, the way she held herself with such certainty—an unshakable calm that seemed to reject the very notion of clinging. Agatha felt a pang, realizing how much she resented that serenity. She couldn’t reconcile the depth of what they shared with the thought that, one day, it might all be… over. Just a memory.

“You say that so easily,” she said, a tremor in her voice. “Like you don’t feel any of this.”

Rio’s gaze flicked back to her, a faint shadow crossing her face. “It’s not that simple,” she replied. “Feelings, memories—they’re powerful. They shape us. But clinging to them…” She hesitated, then let out a quiet sigh. “It doesn’t always keep them alive. Sometimes, it suffocates them.”

Agatha swallowed, fighting back a sudden rush of emotion. She wanted to argue, to find the words that would convince Rio of what she felt deep in her heart—that this wasn’t fleeting. That it couldn’t be.

“Maybe,” she whispered, leaning close, “I’m not ready to accept that yet.”

Rio’s fingers brushed along her cheek, a fleeting touch that left a trail of warmth and ache in its wake. “Then hold on to what you must,” she murmured, her voice softer than Agatha had ever heard it. “But remember—this is your path. And no matter where it takes you… you’ll always find your way back.”

The words settled over them, thick and heavy, the “to me” left unspoken. There was strength in the vulnerability of this bond shaped by both the beauty of the moment and the looming shadow of its end.

“I will, always,” she said firmly before closing the space between them, rolling on top of Rio to kiss her again.

If she had but moments, she’d make them worthwhile.

This would be worth it.

She brushed Rio’s hair from her face, and noticed how it fanned out like a shroud around her.

They had kissed many times, but hadn’t progressed further since that encounter on the throne. Importantly, she hadn’t been able to touch Rio fully. There was a new desperation brewing in her. Not the primal want that they’d been swept up in before. Not the hunger that had led to her splayed out breathless upon that throne. Not the need that crept up around during the nights that she had touched herself imagining hands that weren’t her own. This was something else entirely.

Agatha’s hand lingered in Rio's hair, fingers slipping through the dark strands as her eyes traced Rio’s face, committing each line and shadow to memory. Her proud jaw, the almost imperceptible freckles scattered over her nose, the bow of her lips. The tension between them, a delicate balance of need and restraint, hung in the air as Agatha leaned closer, her heart pounding. They had shared so much, and yet, tonight, there was a rawness—a need—that she could no longer ignore.

Her voice softened, almost a murmur against Rio’s lips. “Let’s stay like this, just… for tonight.” She kissed at her jaw, trying to prove her want wasn’t selfish. She wanted to serve.

Rio’s gaze flickered with something deep and unreadable, but she didn’t pull away. Instead, her hand moved to Agatha’s back, steady and grounding, like an invitation without words. Agatha’s breath hitched as Rio’s fingers traced along her shoulder, anchoring her there, welcoming her closeness.

Who was she to deny her. She couldn’t fathom it. Slowly, Agatha closed the space between them again, her lips brushing Rio’s with a tenderness that promised more than words ever could. She didn’t think about the future or the uncertain goodbyes—only this moment and the warmth shared between them.

Rio sighed softly, lifting her chin and anchoring her hand in Agatha’s messy hair. The tree's leaves grew thick around them, curtaining them, shielding them. Every touch was exceedingly gentle as she removed Rio’s clothes. Each kiss against newly revealed skin was a promise. A plea.

Rio seemed to glow here underneath the ethereal light. Her body was unblemished, not a single scar or imperfection. Agatha’s hands moved with reverence. She wanted to absorb everything.

Her lips moved to Rio’s breast, taking it gently into her mouth and letting her tongue explore. She smiled as she felt Rio arch up closer to her. The gasp as the woman’s breath hitched was something that she’d never be able to shake. She could never want to. She moved to the other side, trailing a hand down the dip beneath her ribs, over her stomach.

Another sound, a whimper, the most beautiful noise she had ever heard. A siren’s song. Agatha smiled, moving her head back to kiss the hollow of her shoulder.

“You’re so beautiful,” she sighed against her skin.

“You’re the only one who thinks so.” Rio replied, her words coming out as a half gasp as Agatha’s clever fingers moved lower still.

Agatha chuckled against her neck and pulled her head away for a moment. Rio made a small displeased sound but it was soon silenced by another kiss. Agatha flashed a wry smile at her, “Good. I don’t like to share.”

Any further quips were silenced, as Agatha pressed the tips of two fingers inside her. Rio cried out, a sharp needy sound that broke the calm of the garden.

Her fingers pressed deeper, curling as she beckoned death closer. It was a certainty that Agatha would far too soon be the one called away. But until that time came, she was perfectly content to spend every minute just like this.

Chapter End Notes

as time clips on, remember dear reader, absence makes the heart grow fonder. also keep in mind, power unchecked is a dangerous thing.

The Coldest Night

Chapter Summary

Doubt comes in
And meets a stranger
Walking on a road alone
Where is she?
Where is she now?
- Doubt Comes In

Chapter Notes

back into Rio's thoughts for a spell

See the end of the chapter for more notes

The throne room was silent as Rio sat alone. She had come to this place often lately, retreating to its familiar shadows whenever she felt the need to think. Though Agatha’s sly mischief and warmth filled most corners of her world now, there were moments like these when solitude reminded her of what she’d allowed herself to be exposed to. What she now felt. What she would soon need to let go.

Agatha’s hunger to understand, to command , was admirable—and dangerous. So unreasonably attractive. But Rio knew all too well what power did to those who pursued it too ardently; it was intoxicating and unforgiving. Agatha might not yet realize how much she’d changed, but the shift in her was undeniable. Every day, her magic grew stronger, sharper, more adept. And every day, the memory of Agatha as she’d first arrived—the girl who knew little of who she was, or what she would become—faded. 

Rio closed her eyes, allowing herself a rare moment of rest. She thought of how Agatha’s laughter seemed to ease the weight she bore, her presence a balm she’d never thought to seek. Her rosy lips, a gentle caress. She couldn’t stop thinking about her. Why would she want to?

Moments in time came back to Rio like leaves on water, drifting into her mind unbidden yet comforting. There had been that day in the garden, for instance, when Agatha had leaned close to examine a newly bloomed sprout, her face lit with pure fascination. She’d looked back at Rio with a grin that almost dared her to feel something in return. Rio had looked away, but later, her mind would bring back that exact image with an almost painful clarity.

Or that evening under the willow, when Agatha had fallen asleep against her shoulder. The moment had been fragile, held together only by the quiet sounds of Agatha’s breathing, the weight of her resting there, trusting. Rio had sat unmoving for hours, almost afraid to breathe lest she wake her. 

“Have I been out long?” Agatha had asked, wiping the sleep from her eyes. Adorably disheveled.

“No, sweetheart,” she said, the pet name slipping from her freely. Agatha didn’t comment on it, but perhaps that was because had swooped in, magic assisting her only slightly as she lifted Agatha into her arms and whispered, “Let’s get you to your bed. Your back will hurt if you fall asleep on the roots again.”

The night after Agatha’s first true success with the pool’s magic… when she’d danced around the cathedral leaving bloody footprints in her wake, laughing with a joy so raw it left Rio speechless. In a rare, impulsive gesture, Rio had joined her in that unguarded moment, her fingers brushing against Agatha’s. She’d laughed then—one of the few times she could remember feeling free. Agatha had spun into her arms with a dramatic flourish. Like a partner in a dance. Agatha had grabbed her face and kissed her fiercely, drunk on victory. They’d spent the night together celebrating Agatha’s success. She loved how feisty success made her. How fiery she had been that night, as she told Rio, ordered her really , just where and how to touch her. Rio had been all too happy to oblige. Rio didn’t need sleep technically, but after that night she’d been a little more sluggish than usual as she went about her work the next day. And if a few souls got a couple hours of extra time, what of it?

However, as so often does when moments of contagious joy are experienced by those who have felt too little of it, a small dread had started to grow in her like a parasite.

She hadn’t been foolish to let herself believe in these fleeting moments, had she ? How easily she had begun to fall into them—letting Agatha draw her out, inch by inch, into spaces she had long since abandoned. She’d felt it in Agatha’s laughter, echoing through the corridors, in the gentle weight of her head resting on Rio’s shoulder as they watched shadows dance across the garden.

Such moments had begun to sink into her heart, even as she tried to guard herself. She was an immortal indestructible thing, not limited to a being, she was a force of nature. Never had she felt more exposed. It thrilled her. It frightened her. That was a new feeling and she didn’t know what to make of it.

More memories echoed. A night shortly after Agatha first came here, when they’d walked the edges of a spring that had formed in the corner of the garden. Walking together, fingers brushing as Agatha balanced on the rocks, her voice echoing with questions about ancient magics. Rio hadn’t meant to, but she’d reached out instinctually, steadying Agatha as she teetered on a loose stone. 

Agatha had laughed, a bright, genuine sound that struck Rio somewhere deep. She found herself looking at Agatha a moment too long, her hand lingering, feeling the warmth of her pulse. It was the kind of touch she hadn’t shared in centuries. Yet she’d quickly withdrawn, cloaking her heart behind practiced indifference.

Later that same night Agatha had fallen asleep in her room, a book still open in her lap. Agatha had invited her to return to her room that night when her business in the city was done. It had taken longer than expected. Something was making the shades restless. Unruly.

Rio had found her there, and without thinking, she’d brushed a stray lock of hair from Agatha’s forehead, her fingers grazing her skin. She’d felt her breath hitch, an unexpected tenderness seeping in as she watched Agatha sleep, her face softened by dreams. She’d convinced herself it was nothing, just a lapse, a result of the silence and the quiet vulnerability of the moment.

But those moments stacked up, creeping into her defenses, making her ache with a longing she hadn’t known in centuries.

The strongest memory, the one she visited most frequently and selfishly, was that night Agatha had claimed her in the garden. Rio hadn’t meant for things to go that far, hadn’t intended to let Agatha in so deeply. But the warmth between them had overpowered her caution, her resolve crumbling beneath the weight of that intimacy. 

She could recall every detail—the way Agatha’s fingers had trembled slightly, but her gaze held steady, vulnerable yet resolute. Rio had seen a tenderness there that stripped her of all her defenses, laying her bare in a way she had not felt in ages. For that single night, the carefully guarded boundaries she’d built around herself fell away, and she had allowed Agatha to see her, fully, without any of the armor that had long defined her.

That was the memory that lingered the longest, a constant thrum beneath the surface, a presence that filled the quiet spaces between them. She found herself recalling it when she was alone, the way Agatha’s face softened, the quiet intimacy of shared breaths, the moments where words had fallen away entirely, leaving a voice she didn’t recognize—even though it was her own—crying out.

They way Agatha’s had kissed over inch of her. How when they finally parted, there were dozens of meadow flowers left where their bodies had rolled in the grass.

That night had been a quiet surrender, one she’d never intended to give. One that had slipped out of her the moment Agatha’s finger had pressed inside her.

If she was honest with herself though, she’d surrendered— parts of her at least — to this witch much earlier.

Now, seated alone in her throne room, Rio let out a sigh, her chest tightening as the truth threatened to break through. She had been careless. She had been foolish, too easily entangled in this strange and tender connection they’d built together. Too clouded with lust. Agatha had sought her out for power; she had come here to learn and to leave.

That was what Rio told herself—that these shared touches, these glances, were nothing more than Agatha playing some silent game, gathering pieces of Rio’s soul to arm herself with, just to spite the world above. She told herself this, even as a quiet voice in her head whispered, “ You’re wrong . Don’t lie. You’ve never felt so alive. ”

Her hand closed into a fist, the ache blooming sharp in her chest as she forced herself to look past these small betrayals of her own restraint. All of this would change once Agatha left. How quickly would Agatha outgrow these memories, replace them with those of her newfound power, her life on the surface, her coven watching in awe?

How soon would she lose interest in Rio? How long before some other lover, one not made of sharp edges but warm sun-kissed skin, whispered sweet nothings, words that Rio would not allow herself to give. She couldn’t compete with the vibrancy of the living. Someone that Agatha could share in the experience of life with. To share ripe fruit on a hot day, to kiss in a spring rain shower, to love and grow old with. That human experience, the beauty of the mundane, Rio would never be able to offer her that. 

And yet, despite her bitterness, those memories—Agatha’s smile, her whispered secrets, her playful banter and bravado, the soft breathy gasps that she made when Rio touched her just so—refused to fade. Rio pressed a hand to her heart, willing it to quiet, but the ache only grew. She had been foolish indeed, she thought, to let this attachment bloom where it had no place. Soon, she’d be alone again. She’d be a memory, another stepping stone for Agatha’s ambition. She couldn’t even fault her for it.

But some part of her clung to the hope, even if she’d never admit it, that Agatha would remember her too—not just as a means to power, but as someone who, for a moment, had truly been hers. No one else had ever had that claim. There had never been someone like her.

Nevertheless, Agatha’s return to the surface was inevitable, and that thought was a thorn, lodging deeper with every passing day. Because once Agatha went back, what then?

Rio didn’t doubt that Agatha would become exactly what she wanted to be upon her return. Relentless. She would dazzle them, all of them , with her newfound power, perhaps more than she herself could even imagine. And Rio wouldn’t even be able to relish in that moment with her. She would have half a year's worth of life while Rio would be left completely in the dark. 

She worried, too, that Agatha might forget the fragile bond they’d built here. She imagined a world in which Agatha would return with a hunger no longer for Rio, but for even more power—a taste for the world above that would inevitably pull her away from the quiet, dark beauty they’d created together. She would just be a means to an end. An inconvenience. Wasn’t that always the way she’d been seen? A literal dead end.

Rio could almost see it now: Agatha, standing tall among her coven, her power undeniable, her spirit untamed, looking back on these six months as a strange but distant memory—a passing chapter in a long story.

Rio exhaled, steadying herself. She would steel herself, as she had before, knowing that whatever heartbreak waited, it would be nothing new. Her fingers tapped softly against the edge of her throne as she surveyed the empty hall, her thoughts tangled webs of regret and resentment. 

She’d been foolish—too open, too willing to let Agatha in, to share herself in ways she’d long forbidden. She’d known, from the moment Agatha arrived, that this connection would come with a price, but she’d let herself believe it might be different, that Agatha was different.

How naive. 

The more she dwelled on it, the more twisted the memories became. Those shared glances and touches, the nights spent in soft conversation felt suddenly tainted—like a spell cast over her, something meant to ensnare her, to soften her defenses so that Agatha could take what she wanted without resistance. Power. It was always about power with her. That’s what it was all about for them both, wasn’t it? Rio had seen it before: mortals were drawn to her domain not for understanding, not for connection, but for the allure of what lay beyond the veil, the promise of mastery over things forbidden.

Rio's lips pressed into a hard line. She bit the inside of her cheek harshly. She tasted the iron of her own blood. The bitterness and tang cleared the haze from her. Agatha, for all her talk of closeness and sincerity, had always had her own motives. She could see that now, couldn’t she? Agatha’s endless questions about magic, her incessant probing into Rio’s life and history, had all been a means to an end. A way to discover and harness whatever secrets Rio kept so closely guarded. Agatha was no different from the others who had come here wanting. Only, she had been cleverer, hiding her hunger behind a softness that Rio had let herself believe was genuine.

Rio clenched her jaw, her bitterness rising like bile. She saw Agatha’s touch in a new light now—each caress, each whispered confession, all part of some elaborate game. It was a dangerous thing, to mistake desire for affection. And she had played right into it, letting herself be drawn in, letting Agatha see parts of her she’d kept hidden for centuries.

Her chest tightened with a bitter twist of realization. What had she expected? That Agatha would leave her world behind? That she would come willingly back to this place of shadows and forget the taste of the sunlight above? When Agatha returned to the surface, she would have all the power she’d sought—more than enough to captivate her coven and take her place among them. And when the time came to return here, would she still be that eager? Or would she come reluctantly, no longer needing what Rio had to offer?

It was almost laughable. Rio had always prided herself on her distance, on the cool restraint that allowed her to navigate this realm and the one above without attachments. And now here she was, spiraling. 

She couldn’t have that.

“Enough,” she murmured, her voice hard, letting the word echo in the empty hall. 

It would not do to dwell on this. She weighed both streams of thought. The pleasant memories they’d shared, the cruel tales she’d twisted. The flower and the sickle held in opposite hands. Which would she carry?

Spring was almost here. She had seen it, the day before when she’d visited the surface to collect a soul. The air had carried the barest hints of change—the soft murmur of melting snow, the smell of thawing earth beneath the frozen ground. She could almost see the subtle shift in the colors of the sky, the slow warming of light. And in that quiet change, she could feel time slipping away from her.

Before, she had found herself drawn to the surface in those early days of the changing season, observing the slow, fragile rebirth of life with a cold curiosity. Spring was the season that always reminded her of loss—the growth she could not touch, the warmth she could never bring back with her. She would stand on the edge of the living world and feel herself a stranger there, an interloper in a place that pulsed with vibrancy.

This year, though, the season’s arrival carried an even greater weight. Agatha would go, back to that warm, blossoming world, and Rio would be left in the stillness. Her heart ached at the thought. Agatha’s presence had softened the sharp lines of this existence, filling spaces she hadn’t known were empty until now. She could feel it slipping from her grasp like sand through her fingers, and it was a sensation she found intolerable.

But tonight, she thought, she could choose differently. She could push aside the bitter coil of resentment and the tightening ache of loss. Just this once, she could let herself be with Agatha without thinking of the future, without calculating what their inevitable separation would take from her. Without her guard. Agatha would be leaving, her magic brightening with every passing day, drawing her closer to the surface. But until then, she was still here, still within reach.

The decision settled like a flame in her chest, and she found herself in motion, leaving the throne room and seeking Agatha. Her steps were determined and as she walked.

When Rio found her, Agatha was standing at the entrance to the garden, her back to her, shoulders wrapped in quiet contemplation as she looked out over the darkened flowers, many of which had grown and flourished under her touch. Her hair was down, messy from a day spent running her hands through it in thought. The silvery glow outlined Agatha’s form, casting her in an otherworldly light, a sight so striking that Rio felt it pierce through her heart like a physical ache. She couldn’t help the soft smile that pulled at her lips.

"Agatha," she called gently, the sound no more than a whisper, yet Agatha turned, her gaze softening with a warmth that made Rio’s resolve slip just a little.

"Rio," Agatha replied, her voice almost reverent. She looked at her as if she were something precious, something worth cherishing, and it made Rio’s heart stammer, though she kept her face composed.

Without another word, Rio crossed the distance between them, reaching for Agatha’s hand. She didn’t speak of what lay ahead, didn’t tell her of the emptiness she’d feel when Agatha left. Instead, she let herself hold on, entwining their fingers, her touch lingering with a tenderness that she had, until now, only allowed in fleeting moments.

“If this is to be your last night here before the world above calls you back…” Her voice was low, laced with something she couldn’t name, or perhaps was too afraid to. “Then let it be ours.” 

Agatha’s expression softened, a flicker of understanding passing between them. The tension of what lay unspoken dissolved into a quiet acceptance, and Rio allowed herself to give in, to pull Agatha close. She traced her fingers along Agatha’s cheek, memorizing the warmth of her skin, the way Agatha’s breath hitched ever so slightly at her touch. Tonight, she would not let herself think of the seasons ahead, nor the lingering ache of tomorrow. 

Just this once, she would let the night be enough.

She loved her so much in that moment.



Chapter End Notes

spring has come again

Up Above

Chapter Summary

Agatha returns to the surface to face the coven.

Chapter Notes

earned the added angst tag.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Agatha brushed her fingertips against her lips. She stood in the glade alone, left with the feeling of a parting kiss. A warmth that was rapidly fading. She traced her lips one more time and steadied herself, taking a deep breath, and took her first steps under the light of the sun.

Each step brought her closer to her coven, to the towering stone that marked the outer circle of their sacred ground. Here, the air was heavy with the familiar scent of wild herbs and damp earth, a place she’d once thought of as home. Now, though, it felt foreign, like she was intruding upon someone else’s domain. She shook off the feeling, reminding herself of the reason she had come—to show them what she had become, the power she had embraced.

But even that purpose felt hollow. The moment she’d left Rio behind, a weight had settled in her chest, the memory of Rio’s touch fading like morning mist. She pushed it aside, burying it under the sharper feeling of her resolve. This was her time to face them, to finally break the silence that had followed her since her first hesitant steps into their world. She was finally ready. She would be undeniable.

As she approached, the quiet murmur of voices grew louder, blending into a tense, wary hush as they noticed her presence. Seven familiar faces turned toward her, eyes narrowed, lips pressed tight. She stood at the edge of the clearing, the ground itself seeming to reject her, the cold and stillness seeping through her boots. Her mother was the first to break the silence, stepping forward with a gaze that seemed to pierce through her.

“Agatha,” her mother said, her voice a low, simmering contempt. “You’ve returned.”

Agatha straightened, meeting her mother’s gaze with one of defiance. “I have.”

Another member of the coven, a tall, dark-haired woman Agatha had once admired, sneered as she took her place beside her mother. “And what do you think you’ve brought back with you?” she asked, her voice dripping with disdain. “More wild tales? Or something worse? You stink of death, Agatha.”

The bitterness in their words stung, but Agatha swallowed it down, lifting her chin. “I’ve learned things that none of you could have taught me,” she replied, her voice steady. “I went beyond your boundaries, sought power you told me was beyond reach. And I have returned stronger for it.”

Her mother’s lips curved into a scornful smile. “Power,” she echoed, her eyes cold as she looked Agatha up and down, as if she were a stranger. “What makes you think you’re deserving of that?”

Agatha blinked, startled by the venom in her mother’s voice. “Deserving?” she repeated, clenching her fists. “I thought I wasn’t good enough mother, that I didn’t meet your expectations. So I went and—”

“Good enough?” her mother cut in, her voice like ice. “You were never anything close to good, Agatha. Your very existence was a mistake.” She took a step closer, her voice lowering to a whisper laced with contempt. “You’re nothing but an evil thing. You always have been. From the moment you drew breath you were touched with darkness.”

Agatha’s heart pounded in her chest, the words slicing through her like a blade. She had always felt the distance between herself and the coven, but this… She searched her mother’s face, looking for some sign of remorse or reluctance. But there was only cold certainty, a conviction that left her breathless.

The other members of the coven stood silent, their eyes cast down or narrowed in disgust. Agatha’s gaze swept over them, searching for someone who might stand beside her. Looking for anyone who would even make eye contact. But they only looked away, as if her presence was tainting the very ground beneath them. Cowards.

“So this is it, then?” she said, her voice shaking. “This was never about my magic, or how unruly I was. You just… didn’t want me here.”

Her mother sneered, folding her arms. “You think yourself so clever, coming to this revelation at last. You don’t belong, Agatha. Not here, not with us. The only thing you’re good for is bringing ruin.”

A silence settled over them, thick and suffocating. Agatha’s hands trembled as she struggled to keep her composure, to keep her emotions in check. The power she had returned with hummed beneath her skin, a steady rhythm that reminded her of the depth she’d gained in Rio’s realm. The strength she’d learned to wield was hers, and hers alone.

“Fine,” she said, the words slipping through gritted teeth. “You don’t have to see it. But I’ll never be what you wanted, and I won’t let you tell me who I am.”

A ripple of power surged through her, and the air around her shifted, a faint, dark purple aura forming as her magic reacted to the anger seething within her. She saw the flicker of fear in their eyes, and it filled her with a cold, satisfying vindication.

Without another word, she turned her back on them, refusing to give them the satisfaction of seeing the pain on her face. She would walk away from them, from this place of bitterness and smallness.

But her mother didn’t let her. “Agatha!” she called, “Where do you think you’re going.”

“Isn’t it obvious mother? You don’t want me here. I don’t have to settle for somewhere I’m not wanted anymore,” she hissed, turning to face her.

Her mother laughed cruelly. “Child, you’re not wanted anywhere. You never will be.” She raised her hand and twisted it in the air. “Sisters! I cannot undo my mistake in bringing this spawn into this world. But with your help, we will scourge her from this surface.”

The witches approached as Agatha stayed put, rooted in this spot. Her heart raced. She would not give them the satisfaction of running. She wasn’t afraid. She would never be afraid again.

The coven moved as one, encircling Agatha like predators closing in on their prey, their hands crackling with ominous energy. Agatha kept her stance firm, her jaw clenched as she felt her own magic stir within her, deep and steady, fueled by something stronger than anger. She had left behind the last of her fear in Rio’s realm; here, she would stand her ground.

One of the coven members thrust a hand forward, sending a bolt of jagged, crimson light searing through the air toward her. Agatha reacted without hesitation, lifting her own hand to conjure a shield, her magic coalescing into a wall of shadow. The bolt slammed against it, scattering into harmless sparks.

Her mother sneered. “Is that what you came to boast you learned in the depths below? Tricks and illusions?”

Agatha didn’t respond. Another spell streaked toward her, an icy tendril aimed at her legs, but she twisted sideways, the ice skimming past her, leaving a frozen scar on the ground where she had stood. Another witch aimed a spell high, and Agatha ducked behind a tree, the blast scattering leaves and bark like confetti in the air.

The witches grew bolder, spells flying faster, yet none found their mark. Agatha moved between the trees, raising dark shields and deflecting bursts of magic that shattered in vibrant flashes against her defenses. She could feel their frustration mounting, feel them feeding on it, their energy only intensifying in the air around them. They would not relent. They wanted her broken.

She would not break.

Agatha’s mother watched her, eyes narrowed as she raised her arms, the air crackling with something darker, more insidious. Her voice echoed across the clearing.

“You think you’re so powerful?” she sneered. “Let’s see if you can match the strength of those who gave you your pathetic life.”

Her mother began a twisting gesture, her hands weaving a spell Agatha recognized—the binding. Agatha barely had time to react, attempting to summon a shield, but the spell coiled around it, sinking through her defenses with relentless force. The moment it made contact, a chill seeped through her limbs, paralyzing her, and locking her magic in place. She staggered, her body no longer under her own control, as the magical bonds solidified around her wrists and ankles, binding her to the spot.

The witches closed in, their eyes glittering with anticipation and malice. Her mother stepped forward, a triumphant smile spreading across her face. She raised her hand, fingers curling in a way that made Agatha’s skin prickle with dread.

“This is the end of the line for you, Agatha. You’re not welcome here. You’re not welcome anywhere ,” her mother spat, voice seething with years of pent-up disdain.

Agatha’s pulse quickened as she struggled against the bindings, feeling her own magic rise in defiance, but her mother’s spell was tightening like a vice. She could feel her power trapped beneath the surface, struggling to break free.

Agatha's breath came in sharp, shallow gasps as she strained against the binding, every fiber of her being resisting the enchantment. In this moment, she thought of Rio’s voice, steady and unwavering, guiding her as she’d learned to tap into the pool’s energy. Her mother’s cruel words echoed, mingling with the memory of Rio’s instructions, her assurances that Agatha’s strength lay not only in her own power but in her connection to the vast, unfathomable forces around her.

Her mother circled her. “Look at you now, helpless,” she sneered. She leaned closer, her voice a poisonous whisper. “Useless. You never belonged among us. Weak, unruly... nothing but a curse.”

A spell surged from her mother’s hand, striking Agatha’s chest with searing pain. Her vision blurred as her muscles seized, agony lancing through her body. She felt her magic struggling against the binding, flaring in response to the attack, a trapped fire clawing to escape. Another spell hit her, followed by another, until the rest of the coven joined in, spells slicing into her like seven swords, waves of brutal, unrelenting pain.

But beneath the torment, something else stirred. Agatha’s thoughts drifted to the pool, to the way she’d drawn magic from it, allowing the energy to flow through her, surrounding her and sustaining her. She focused, straining to reach the well of power, to unlock the connection she’d learned in Rio’s realm. She reached out not with desperation but with intent, imagining herself as Rio had always carried herself—calm, deliberate, powerful.

As another surge of pain wracked her body, Agatha drew the energy in. The coven’s spells, their hatred, their own vicious magic poured into her, filling her with a burning, terrible strength. Her mother’s horrified expression shifted, sensing the change, but it was too late. Agatha felt their magic seeping into her like water through cracks in a dam, filling her veins with a raw, electric charge that ignited her every nerve. Her bindings cracked and shattered under the force of the siphoned magic, leaving her free. She screamed in rage.

The coven gasped, their fear feeding her, their spells fading as she drew not only from their magic but from their life force itself. The witches stumbled, one by one, their faces paling, and then, in a single moment of overwhelming, blinding power, Agatha felt them drop. The ground fell silent as they collapsed in a ring around her, lifeless.

The bodies lay around her, her mother among them, eyes still open in her final, hateful glare. Agatha stood over them, her heart heavy not with remorse but with a deep, unyielding sorrow. 

 She felt nothing for what she’d done; if anything, a sense of grim satisfaction settled in her chest. They had forced her hand, and left her with no choice but to end them before they could destroy her. 

But the weight of it all came from something else. She looked down at her mother, the woman who should have loved her with the same ease she breathed. Agatha felt the ache of all the years she’d hoped for something that would never be—acceptance, kindness, a mother’s embrace that might soothe the edges of her magic instead of stoking its fires. 

They had never loved her; they had only ever tolerated her presence, a misfit among their ranks. She’d wanted to prove herself, to show them she could be something more, but that hope had been crushed long ago.

She grieved, not for them but for herself, for the innocence she’d lost in wanting something as simple as love. They had forced her into this battle, forced her to show the very power they’d feared all along. And now, in her bitter victory, she knew that in their eyes, she’d become exactly what they accused her of: a dark force, a threat, something monstrous.

Agatha straightened, her face hardened and resolute. If they had made her into this, she would bear it proudly. There was no regret. She looked around one last time, then turned her back on the scene, moving away from the place that had once held all her hopes and had now become nothing but a ruin.

This would be her last farewell. She was done with them.

Death surveyed the bodies. A massacre.

She’d feared this.

One by one, she walked to the body of each coven member, knelt beside them, and closed their eyes. She was emotionless and clinical as she passed over each of them.

Last she came to Agatha’s mother. The woman who had summoned her. Who had traded her child. Who had been cruel and scarred her daughter’s heart. This is the woman that had tried to break her. She could feel her spirit, still roiling with hatred and contempt.

Death pulled a jagged curved knife from her belt. This one didn’t deserve a graceful transition.

The body was already cold, but Death slit her throat for good measure.

In the months that followed, Agatha’s strength bloomed. Every morning, she woke with the thrill of it buzzing beneath her skin, a tangible power that felt boundless. It crackled and roiled in her as certain and steady as her heartbeat. She marveled at the magic she could now wield, at how the spells she’d once struggled to master now flowed through her effortlessly. It was as though each incantation, each spark, had always been there, lying dormant until she’d claimed it as her own.

The initial sorrow she’d carried—the ache of her mother’s rejection, the bitterness of that final confrontation—softened with time, reshaping itself into something almost triumphant. The betrayal no longer felt raw, but instead a faded scar she’d wear as a testament to her survival.

As her power deepened, she often found herself thinking of Rio. She would close her eyes and imagine the woman’s expression, her cool gaze softening in approval or, perhaps, curiosity. Sometimes, she allowed herself to imagine that Rio might be proud, that her calm, detached demeanor would crack, at the sight of Agatha’s newfound prowess. 

It was a bittersweet fantasy. She also wondered if Rio would have tried to caution her, to remind her of what power could cost, or if she would have understood, silently bearing witness to what Agatha had become. But whether Rio would celebrate her growth or see it as dangerous, one thing was certain: Agatha wanted her to know. To witness what she’d managed to carve out of the darkness.

As summer stretched on, Agatha’s days filled with purpose. She roamed the forests alone, strengthening her craft. Many days she brought herself to the edge of exhaustion and beyond it. She learned the language of the land, and felt her senses sharpen until she could almost feel the roots stirring in the soil beneath her feet. She’d let her magic play across her fingertips, watching the smallest sparks flicker, humming softly as if in conversation with her. Her spells became her company, her refuge.

As each day crept by, Agatha felt the slow drag of summer pull her down, every sticky, humid afternoon making her long for the cool, shadowed stillness of the underworld. The realm above had lost its luster, its relentless sun pressing down on her until she felt ready to melt into the earth itself. How she missed the way Rio’s domain had whispered with a soft, perpetual chill. The sense of endless space and shadow offered comfort instead of confinement. Here above, the walls of heat closed around her, tightening like a spell gone wrong.

Despite her powers now humming with a mastery she’d once only dreamed of, a nagging hollowness tempered the satisfaction. She had no one to share her triumphs with. 

She began to think of Rio more with each passing day, wondering if, by some unspoken tether, Rio could feel her longing, could sense the ache that refused to dull. In her mind’s eye, Agatha would replay those moments in the underworld—Rio’s cool hand guiding her through magic so immense it felt like the pulse of the earth itself, her dark eyes studying Agatha with a quiet intensity. It hadn’t been warmth, exactly. But it was something , something that Agatha had come to crave.

Sometimes she’d stop, mid-spell, and find herself staring out toward the edge of the forest, feeling that pull grow stronger. The thought of seeing Rio again, of letting her see the strength she’d cultivated here, kindled a flame of anticipation. She wondered if Rio might reach out to her, call her back as the veil between realms grew thin. The coolness of autumn would soon descend, and with it, her time on the surface would wane, an inevitability she felt winding closer every day. Anticipation coiled within her.

But for now, she kept to the forest, channeling her magic, her mind drifting always to the woman who had sent her back with a wordless promise in her eyes.

The leaves had finally begun their slow turn toward russet at the edges, and the once-warm winds grew crisper, especially in the mornings. Late-blooming wildflowers dotted the fields, but their colors were softer now, as if they, too, were winding down, preparing to retreat into the earth. Days grew shorter; the golden glow of late afternoon came sooner, casting long shadows that deepened with each passing week.

Agatha wondered if Rio could sense her strength, wherever she was, as keenly as Agatha felt it within herself. That pull, that undeniable thread, was still there, more potent than ever, like a gravity she couldn’t defy. In the quiet hours when she allowed herself to let her guard down, she imagined how it might feel to stand in Rio’s presence again, to let her feel the vastness she’d claimed.

She dreamed what it would be like when she finally was able to touch her again.

One evening, she walked through the dense forest, tracing the path of fading sunlight filtering through the thinning canopy. She stopped by a small stream, watching as leaves—some already tinged with the first signs of red—floated downstream. She’d been here often, listening to the water’s murmurs, letting it drown out the silence that sometimes haunted her. But tonight, it felt different, like a prelude, as if the world itself was shifting, bending toward some culmination.

Her heart stopped. Balanced on top of a wide maple leaf, like a twisted variety of lotus, a single dark and rich bloom. Her flower from the garden. A calling card.

She clutched her hand at her heart, and tears pricked at the corners of her eyes in a sudden surge of relief. Gasping, she felt her lungs fill to bursting. Agatha laughed, cackled really, as she clutched the flower between her fingers. She raised it to her lips and let the thorn pierce her skin.

As she tasted blood she grinned wildly.

Soon, soon, soon. Finally, finally, finally.

Rio.

Blood in the Cut

Chapter Summary

The reunion doesn't go like either of them planned.

Chapter Notes

I'm sorry. blame k.flay for the title and soundtrack of this one.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

The moment Rio appeared in the woods Agatha ran to her. Her hands grasped desperately at Rio’s arms, her hands, her face. She clung to her as if she were drowning. “I did it,” she gasped, pulling her close and burying her face in the woman’s neck. She inhaled deeply, breathing in the smell of her. “Did you see? I did it. The coven, they turned on me. I unlocked my power. But I did what we practiced at their pool, I took their magic.” Agatha was breathless. Almost crying in relief of not only returning to this familiar embrace but to finally be able to share in her success.

Agatha didn’t see the thin line Rio’s lips had pressed into. She hadn’t noticed the worried knot at her brow. “I saw, Agatha,” she said softly, carefully.

Agatha laughed softly, her joy spilling over as she clung to Rio. She didn’t register the tension, the way Rio’s body felt less yielding, or how her arms wrapped around her at an unexpected distance. “You saw,” she repeated, breathing the words against Rio’s shoulder.

Rio’s hands rested on her shoulders, but she seemed hesitant, her touch restrained. “I did,” she replied, her voice measured and careful. “You’ve grown… much stronger, Agatha. More than I imagined.”

Agatha pulled back slightly, eager to catch Rio’s gaze, her own bright with excitement. She searched Rio’s eyes, looking for that glimmer of pride or admiration. But Rio’s expression was guarded, her jaw tight. She noticed a vein in her neck throb. 

“Don’t you… aren’t you proud?” Agatha’s voice softened, her excitement faltering as she registered Rio’s demeanor. She felt the joy of her accomplishment waver under the weight of that distant expression.

Rio’s face softened briefly, but the warmth didn’t quite reach her eyes. “It’s not pride or admiration that concerns me, Agatha,” she said quietly, her gaze shifting to the ground. “It’s the weight of things. That kind of power… it doesn’t come without consequences.”

Agatha straightened, feeling the sting of disappointment settle in her chest. She could almost feel herself deflating under the scrutiny of Rio’s words. “Consequences?” she repeated, her voice tinged with disbelief.  She pulled away with a pained expression. “You know what I faced. You know why I did it. After all that we—” She stopped, biting back her words, her own voice trembling.

Rio’s hand dropped from Agatha’s shoulder, and she took a measured breath, as though each word had to be carefully chosen. “It’s not about what you faced, Agatha. I’m not doubting you, or what you went through. I don’t care that a few witches fool enough to come after you fell. I’m only worried about the cost.”

Agatha felt her face flush with frustration. She had waited for this moment, had imagined Rio’s face alight with admiration, with shared pride. For months she had dreamed of how they would reunite, how they would celebrate this blessing. All of that shattered. Now she was met with this nightmare, this careful, restrained detachment, as if Rio couldn’t bring herself to give Agatha even a fragment of satisfaction.

“Cost?” Agatha’s voice sharpened, her shoulders squaring as she stepped back. “You think I haven’t paid it already? I fought— alone —against everything that tried to break me. I didn’t expect a lecture about the ‘weight of things.’” Her words came out sharper than she intended, but she couldn’t hold them back.

I just want to make sure you’re—”

Rio’s expression softened, and for a moment, Agatha saw a flicker in her eyes, that look she got when she was on the precipice of vulnerability. But the look was brief, dissolving as quickly as it had come. “It’s not that I don’t understand, Agatha,” she replied, her tone firm but softened around the edges. “It’s that I’m… afraid. Power like this… it has a way of taking more than it gives.”

Agatha’s fists clenched at her sides, her chest tightening. “You’re not afraid of my power. You’re afraid of me. And you can’t stand it.” Her words were a barely whispered accusation, but they rang heavy in the space between them.

Rio’s face turned to stone, a shadow passing over her eyes. “If that’s what you think, Agatha, then you haven’t understood me at all.” 

The silence hung between them, thick with all the words left unsaid.
