Rio’s shoulders stiffened, but she kept walking, saying nothing, her face set like marble. 

Agatha’s patience snapped. She surged forward, stepping in front of Rio to block her path. “No, you don’t get to ignore this. You don’t get to shut down when it’s me wanting answers. For months, I’ve thought of nothing but you. And this—” She waved her hands, gesturing to the dark, silent landscape around them, her voice rising. “This is how you welcome me back?”

Rio’s eyes flashed with something unreadable, but her face remained guarded. “We can discuss this later, Agatha.”

“No. We discuss it now ,” Agatha hissed, closing the space between them. “I want to know if everything I thought we shared was a lie. If every time you looked at me, you were just waiting for me to fail.”

Rio’s jaw clenched. Her eyes held Agatha’s gaze, but there was something distant as if she’d already pulled herself away. Rio’s voice was low, her words laced with bitterness and hurt. “I was trying to protect you—”

“From what?” Agatha shouted, shoving Rio’s shoulder, in a desperate attempt to shake her out of that infuriating composure. “From becoming something you can’t control? Or from becoming someone you might actually care about?”

Rio staggered back, her expression swirling between many emotions—shock, pain, anger—it was hard to tell. But she didn’t respond. Instead, she stood there, breathing hard, as if the weight of what Agatha had said was settling over her.

“I thought I meant something to you,” Agatha whispered, her voice barely holding together. “But if all you see in me now is a threat, then maybe I never did.”

Rio’s face softened, and she reached out as if to touch her, but her hand fell short, hanging in the air between them. “It’s not… it’s not like that,” she murmured, her voice breaking.

“Don’t.” Agatha spat, slapping her hand from the air. Rio quirked an eyebrow at her, pressing her tongue into her cheek, but let her hand fall.

“Don’t say it’s not like that when it is!” Agatha’s frustration boiled over, her heart racing with a mixture of anger and an undeniable longing. She stepped forward again, her fingers trembling with an energy that was raw and uncontainable.

In a sudden surge of impulsive passion, Agatha reached out and grabbed the front of Rio’s shirt, pulling her closer. Before she could think better of it, she crashed her lips against Rio’s, pouring all her frustration, her hurt, and her longing into that single kiss. It was fierce, demanding, and full of desperation that she could no longer contain. It was a hungry beast now spiraling out of control.

For a moment, time stood still. Agatha felt Rio’s body stiffen in surprise, her lips unyielding at first. But then, slowly, reluctantly, Rio responded, her hands finding their way to Agatha’s waist, drawing her closer as if trying to ground herself in the intensity of the moment.

Agatha’s heart raced as she pressed harder, deepening the kiss. She kissed her fiercely. She tasted the salt of her own tears as they slipped free, mingling with the heat between them.

Why couldn’t she just have been happy for her? Why was this passion being fueled by fury instead of the eager delight of returning to a lover? Why was she kissing Rio like she hated her?

When they finally broke apart, Agatha gasped for air, her chest heaving. She searched Rio’s eyes for understanding. “Tell me it matters,” she pleaded, her voice trembling. “Tell me this… whatever it is, matters.”

Rio stared at her, her expression a storm of conflicting emotions. “Agatha…” she started, her voice shaky, but she faltered, unable to find the words. The vulnerability in her gaze flickered between fear and longing “You don’t know–”

“No,” Agatha interrupted, her voice fierce but laced with desperation. “I do know. I know I don’t want to hide from this, from you. You can’t go back to pretending that I’m some stranger you need to keep at a distance.”

Rio’s breath hitched, and for a moment, Agatha thought she might finally see the truth she had been searching for, but then Rio looked away, breaking the connection between them. The pain was evident in her voice. “You don’t understand what you’re asking.”

Agatha felt her heart sink, the weight of the world crashing back down around them. “I don’t want to understand anymore,” she admitted, her voice raw. “I want to feel. I want to be with you.”

A heavy silence settled between them as Agatha fought against the rising tide of sorrow, feeling the familiar sting of rejection. She hated herself for wanting Rio. She hated that she couldn’t resist her.

Her voice broke. “Please.” She couldn’t stop the tears that were falling now. Her voice was begging, pleading in a way she didn’t recognize. “Please, don’t make me hate you, my love.”

“Would it be easier on you if you did, sweetheart ?” Rio sneered. Her patience had run out. “I show concern for you, I tell you so clearly I care for you, and that is what makes you hate me?” 

“You’ve told me nothing ! Maybe if you did before we wouldn’t be like this right now.”

Rio’s eyes shone with hurt that quickly curled into anger. “Don’t you dare.”

She spun on her heel to leave, but Agatha—desperate, wounded, feral Agatha— pushed her against the wall. “Look at me.” She grabbed Rio’s face, turning her jaw, forcing her to hold her stare. “Look at me, Rio.” She knew her eyes were crazed, she felt all the blood rushing to her face. She chewed her lip as she studied Rio, for what she wasn’t entirely sure.

“Is that how you want this, Agatha?” Rio asked coolly, her hand wrapping around Agatha’s wrist trying to coax her back from the edge.

“You don’t give a fuck what I want,” she spat.

Rio was truly angry now. She drove her hands into the rock of the tunnel behind her and it exploded. They both were sent flying backward, crashing into the rubble. They struggled, scrambling and clawing at each other.

Agatha hit the ground hard but rolled quickly to her feet, adrenaline surging through her as she faced Rio. The rush of anger strengthened her. She lunged forward, her hands outstretched, not to summon magic, but to physically assert herself. 

Rio had barely regained her footing when Agatha tackled her, pushing her back against the jagged rock wall. They grappled, Agatha’s fingers digging into Rio’s shoulders as they struggled for control. “Why won’t you just let me in?” Agatha shouted, the words barely containing her rage.

Rio’s expression flickered with surprise, but it quickly hardened into resolve. “You’re making this impossible, Agatha!” she cried, twisting free from Agatha’s grasp and shoving her back with a force that caught Agatha off guard. She stumbled but quickly regained her balance, eyes blazing.

“Impossible?” Agatha shouted, charging again. She threw a fist toward Rio, who dodged to the side with a fluid grace that when elsewhere applied had captivated Agatha. But this time, there was no allure in Rio’s movements; there was only a fierce determination to keep her at bay.

“Agatha, stop!” Rio barked, her voice echoing in the confined space. She aimed a kick at Agatha’s side, but Agatha twisted away just in time, countering with a swift jab to Rio’s midsection.

They were both breathing heavily now, emotions running high as they exchanged blows. Agatha felt the heat of their fight mix with the cool air of the tunnel, the space charged with an electric energy that crackled around them. “You don’t get to walk away from this!” Agatha yelled, throwing another punch, this one landing solidly against Rio’s jaw.

Rio stumbled back, surprise flashing across her face. She spat out blood to the ground at Agatha’s feet. Regaining her footing she rushed at Agatha, tackling her to the ground. They hit the dirt with a thud, and Agatha felt the breath leave her lungs. 

“Why can’t you see what this is doing to us?” Rio’s voice was strained as she pinned Agatha down, their faces mere inches apart. “I’m trying to protect you, and you’re—”

“Protect me?” Agatha hissed, pushing against Rio’s weight, but Rio held firm. “You think pushing me away will protect me? You’re only showing me that you don’t trust me!”

Rio’s expression twisted, a mix of frustration and pain. “You’re not showing me that I can trust you!”

With a sudden burst of strength, Agatha flipped them, putting herself on top. She pinned Rio’s wrists to the ground, her heart racing as she stared into Rio’s eyes. “Then tell me what you want, because I don’t want this,” she pleaded, her voice fierce but trembling.

“I want you to understand the stakes!” Rio replied, her breath coming fast, anger still sparking in her gaze. “You think this is just about us?”

“Maybe it’s you who doesn’t understand!” Agatha shot back, frustration boiling over. She leaned closer, their breaths mingling. “I have fought so hard. I have changed so much. Why don’t you see me?”

Rio’s expression faltered for a moment before it hardened again. “You’re not the only one who’s changed, Agatha,” she said, her voice low and dangerous. “You’re walking a path I’m terrified of. I’m not scared of you. I’m scared for you.”

The silence hung between them, heavy with the weight of their unspoken feelings, the fight giving way to an uncomfortable truth. Inches from her face, Agatha could see the tears pricking at the corners of Rio’s eyes as she spoke again. 

“I saw what you did to the coven. I’m not mad at you for doing what you needed to to survive. But seven well-known coven members were drained of their power and the eighth went missing. There are people out there who can put the pieces together. People who will hunt you down for what you’ve done.” Rio blinked back her tears but couldn’t keep the truth from spilling out. She realized she didn’t want to. If Agatha demanded the truth, she would have it. “So for six months, Agatha, I spent six months terrified of seeing you. Of being called up to collect a body and it turning out to be yours.”

Agatha closed her eyes, wincing at Rio’s confession. She couldn’t look at Rio’s wounded face, she couldn’t live with the thought that she was the source of those tears. Another wave of hurt welled up inside her. She didn’t want this, didn’t want to feel so lost and torn apart. Agatha’s heart ached.

Finally, she let herself collapse, dropping her entire weight on top of Rio. She released her wrists and braced herself to be thrown aside. But a harsh touch didn’t come.

Harshness would have been easier. She wasn’t prepared for the gentle caress of Rio’s hand threading through her hair. Agatha turned her head and rested it on Rio’s chest. She listened to the steady beat of her heart as Rio’s other hand softly rubbed her back.

“I’m sorry.” She whispered.

“I know.”

“I’m sorry,” Agatha repeated, looking up at her. Her brow furrowed as she noticed the bruise blooming on Rio’s jaw. An ugly mark she had caused. Her fingers skimmed it.

Rio flinched slightly but didn’t pull away, allowing Agatha’s fingers to trace the bruise with a gentleness that felt foreign after their fight. Agatha’s touch was tentative, as though she were trying to erase the damage she’d inflicted, to make sense of the pain she’d caused. Her fingertips lingered, soft and apologetic, and for a moment, the anger between them seemed to dissolve, leaving only the raw truth of what they’d both been holding back.

“Does it hurt?” Agatha murmured, her voice barely above a whisper.

Rio’s gaze softened, her guarded expression slipping. “Not as much as this,” she replied, brushing her fingers along Agatha’s cheek, where tears had left tracks. Her hand was steady, grounding, as though trying to hold Agatha together. “I never want this.”

Agatha’s lip quivered, and she pressed her face into Rio’s chest, the remnants of her anger dissolving into something softer, more vulnerable. “I know. I just… I didn’t know how else to show you. I thought if you could see what I’ve become, you’d—”

“I do see you, Agatha.” Rio’s voice was gentle, a contrast to the tension that had existed only moments ago. “But I was afraid. Of losing you to this power you’ve claimed. I thought… if you grew so strong, so independent, maybe you’d never want to come back. I thought you’d be bored here.”

Agatha pulled back, staring at her in disbelief. “You think I don’t want to come back? I wanted you to be proud, to see how much I’ve grown, and all I wanted was to share that with you. All of it.”

Rio’s expression shifted, a hint of guilt and understanding flickering across her face. She reached up, brushing a stray lock of hair from Agatha’s face. “I am proud of you,” she said quietly, her voice breaking the silence between them. “I just was afraid of you outgrowing this—of outgrowing… me.” Rio’s hand stilled, her fingers resting against Agatha’s cheek.

The weight of their fears hung between them, unspoken for so long, but finally laid bare. Agatha leaned in, pressing her forehead against Rio’s, and for a moment, they simply breathed together, grounding themselves in each other’s presence.

“We don’t have to be afraid anymore,” Agatha whispered. “Not like this.”

Rio closed her eyes, exhaling slowly as her hand tightened gently in Agatha’s hair. “Then let’s start again,” she murmured, her voice low and earnest. “Let’s stop hurting each other.”

Agatha nodded against her chest and she felt Rio shift uncomfortably underneath her. “Anyway,” she said breezily, her usual teasing tone returning to her voice, “glad you’re here and all darling, but maybe we can kiss and make up not on bed of rubble?”

Agatha scoffed, “Well if someone hadn’t been so dramatic blowing up a wall.” She stood and offered her hand to Rio, pulling her up with her.

“I’m dramatic? You punched me! Who does that?” Rio snarked back. Agatha glanced quickly at her, still ashamed of how visceral their fight had been. But Rio’s eyes were playful as she reached up to her cheek healing the mark.

“Wait, this whole time you could’ve healed yourself?”

“Well, yeah. Of course. But you know,” Rio shrugged as they continued down the tunnel, side by side, “sometimes you’ve got to let yourself feel the hurt.”

Agatha hummed thoughtfully, leading them down the familiar paths back to her room. As they entered, her room was just as she’d left it. It felt so good to return to a familiar place. Coming home. 

“Well, let’s put those healing hands to work then, I think you left a few bruises on me too.” She said, smiling at Rio mischievously. 

Rio quirked an eyebrow at her, not seeing any wounds on her body. “I don’t see—”

Agatha smiled, unbuttoning her shirt. “Oh I do, don’t you see just there?” she teased as she pulled her shirt off and pointed vaguely at her chest. “Why don’t you come closer and—”

She laughed as Rio’s eyes brightened, catching her meaning, and hurried to tumble with her down onto the bed. “Won’t you be a dear and kiss it better?” She lilted, putting on a playful pout.

Who was Rio to deny anything from the woman she loved.

Confession

Chapter Summary

"And you didn't know how
And you didn't know why
But you knew that you wanted to take her home

It was like she was someone you'd always known"

“You’re mad with power.” Rio teased, laughing as she leaned down to kiss Agatha. She pressed one hand over Agatha's heart as she did, supporting herself there long enough to brush her lips to her cheek as well.

That was an understatement. Agatha had been insatiable. A woman possessed with a singular focus on spending the night drawing as many orgasms as possible from her lover. Blame her competitive nature. She was still coming down, her breaths still ragged, her body an overstimulated live wire. “That makes one of us.” She pressed a kiss to her neck before tapping Agatha’s hip. “Roll over, I want to hold you for a while.”

Agatha smiled and obliged, scooting back against Rio, sighing as strong arms wrapped around her, their legs tangling together.

They settled into the quiet warmth of the room, a comfortable silence wrapping around them. Agatha felt Rio’s breath steady against her neck, her arms tight but gentle. Holding her so protectively, as if she was afraid if she loosened her grasp Agatha would slip away again. She traced lazy circles on Rio’s forearm, savoring the closeness. 

After a few moments, Agatha tilted her head back, glancing at Rio over her shoulder. “So, I've been meaning to ask, what did you get up to while I was gone? Anything exciting?” 

Rio gave a dry chuckle, rubbing her thumb over Agatha’s stomach. "Exciting? Hardly. I spent most of it just keeping things in order. You know how it is. That plague in Dublin took up a good four months. I kept myself busy.”

Agatha pursed her lips, thinking of how those weeks must have dragged on for Rio, without anyone to talk to. "I mean, up there I would occasionally bump into someone. Traveling merchant, an occasional band of misfits lost in the woods. Sure, it wasn’t you, but… I could find occasional company.” She hesitated, wondering if her words might cut too close. “Did you… was there anyone here you could talk to?”

Rio’s hand paused for a moment before resuming its gentle rhythm. "Not really," she admitted, her voice quieter. "I don’t… make it a habit. The souls here are, preoccupied. Plus I can't give special treatment. I guess I just never really needed anyone down here."

A small pang twisted in Agatha’s chest. She realized, with a bit of sadness, that Rio truly didn’t have anyone else.

Rio let out a sigh, pulling Agatha a little closer, as if to hide in her warmth. “It’s never even been something I’ve… wanted, not until you.”

Agatha’s heart squeezed at that, her throat tightening. "So all this time, it was just… me?" she whispered, her voice barely audible.

“Yes, just you,” Rio replied softly, a hint of vulnerability slipping through. “And you… you were up there.” Her fingers stilled against Agatha’s side. “I didn’t realize until you were gone how quiet it would be.”

Agatha turned slightly in Rio’s arms, just enough to see her face. “I’m here now. And I’ll keep coming back.”

Rio’s face softened, but there was a faint shadow in her eyes like she wasn’t sure if she could trust the promise. She looked away, a small smile tugging at her lips. “You’d be the first,” she said, half-teasing, but Agatha heard the echo of loneliness there, something she doubted Rio would ever admit out loud.

Agatha took Rio’s hand and brought it to her lips, pressing a gentle kiss there. “Then I’ll just have to be the one who breaks all your rules.” She looked up, holding Rio’s gaze with steady conviction. “If you’ll let me.”

Rio’s lips quirked, her grip tightening around Agatha’s fingers. “I suppose I’ll allow an exception,” she murmured, her voice laced with something soft, something almost hopeful.

They stayed like that, wrapped up in each other, and for the first time, Agatha sensed that Rio was allowing herself to lean into that hope—into the idea that maybe she wasn’t alone anymore. She drifted off easily in Rio's arma and slept more soundly than she had in half a year.

When she woke up, she realized that Rio was still there with her and she felt a wave of affection rush through her. Agatha brushed her hair out of her eyes, grinning mischievously as she watched Rio stretch out beside her, looking relaxed and slightly amused as she noticed Agatha’s good mood. 

"So," Agatha began with an air of playful formality, "In making up for lost time, and because you were such a good sport last night, I’ve decided to take you on a date."

Rio raised an eyebrow, feigning surprise. “Oh?”

Agatha nodded, eyes sparkling. “Courtship is an intricate ritual,” she said in mock seriousness

A wry smile crept over Rio’s face. “Hmm, I seem to remember a certain someone skipping a few steps. Aren’t you supposed to court someone before… repeatedly falling into bed with them?”

Agatha’s cheeks flushed, and she couldn’t hold back a chuckle. “Minor details,” she replied, waving a hand dismissively. “It’s never too late to start, right? Besides,” she added more softly, “don’t you think it would be fun?”

Agatha smiled, something more tender settling in her expression as she took Rio’s hand. There was something almost heartbreaking about the thought that, for all her years, Rio may have never really had this sort of experience—a night meant just for her. 

“You’d be the first excited for a date with death.” Rio said with a wry smile.

“Seems I’m the first at a lot of things with you hot stuff.” Agatha teased with a roguish and over-exaggerated wink, laughing as Rio threw a pillow at her.

Agatha was meticulous, more so than she’d ever been with spells or training. She wanted this to be perfect, to give Rio something that felt special—a night that could belong to just them, untouched by the shadows and secrets that hung over so much of their past time together.

She had combed the underworld’s dim gardens for hours, gathering flowers with a careful eye for those that seemed to glow most brightly in the soft, blue-tinted light of the underworld. In the garden under the branches of the willow tree, Agatha arranged a spread of cushions and blankets she’d pilfered from her chambers—deep purples, silvers, and soft grays that seemed to echo the colors of the underworld itself. She set a careful bundle of dried herbs nearby, hoping to mask the ever-present, earthy dampness with a sweeter scent that would linger as they relaxed. She’d conjured a small spread—a blend of the underworld’s fruits and flask of wine she’d gathered during her time above ground.

When she heard footsteps approaching, she felt a rush of nervous excitement. She hadn’t seen Rio since morning and wondered if her little surprise would live up to her expectations. Taking a deep breath, she glanced around, reassuring herself that everything was in place.

As Rio approached, her eyes widened slightly, and a smirk tugged at her lips. “Well, you certainly went all out,” she murmured, a flicker of surprise brightening her gaze.

Agatha grinned, her cheeks flushed with a mix of pride and bashfulness. “Well, I’m trying to do this properly,” she replied, gesturing to the cushions and leading Rio to sit with her against them.

Rio’s expression softened as she glanced around the garden, her gaze lingering on the flowers Agatha had gathered. “It’s, very sweet,” she admitted, “Most people wouldn’t be able to… draw beauty out of this place.”

Agatha beamed a mischievous glint in her eye. “Most people don’t have you to impress,” she teased. She uncorked the dark, earthy wine and handed it to Rio, who took it with an amused raise of her brow.

As they settled into a comfortable silence, Agatha reached out to touch one of the Shadeblooms she’d woven into a makeshift garland nearby. “I don’t think you’ve ever mentioned it, but… do you ever spend much time out here, like this? When I’m not here,” she asked, curiosity sparking in her voice.

Rio leaned back, letting her gaze drift over the soft lights and shadows around them. “Not often. I used to, maybe, when I was younger,” she admitted, her voice low. “But there was never anyone else here to enjoy it with.” 

The words hung in the air, soft and sad, and Agatha felt a pang in her chest. She knew, intellectually, that Rio’s life had been isolated, but seeing it spelled out like this brought the reality of it home in a new way. “Well,” she said softly, her hand finding Rio’s and squeezing it, “I’m glad we get to enjoy it together now.”

Rio looked at her, and at that moment, Agatha could see something close to awe in her eyes, like she couldn’t quite believe this moment.

“I don’t know how you do it, Agatha,” Rio murmured, her fingers brushing over Agatha’s. “Making this place feel less… hollow.”

Agatha smiled, a little shy but certain. “Maybe that’s my real magic.”

Rio rolled her eyes. “You're laying it on a bit thick, no? Shmaltz, I think that’s what they call it?”

Agatha shrugged her shoulders and leaned in closer, noticing how the wine had darkened Rio’s lips. “Call it what you want. Is it working?”

Rio’s smirk softened into something warmer as she leaned forward, letting their noses brush together. “Maybe,” she murmured. “You’ll have to keep trying if you want a definitive answer.”

Agatha chuckled, sitting back with a flourish, her arm sweeping dramatically through the air. “Very well, then,” she announced, voice lilting and playful. “For my next trick…” She leapt up and extended her hand to Rio with an exaggerated bow, her eyes gleaming with mischief. “May I have this dance?”

Rio arched an eyebrow, looking at Agatha’s outstretched hand. “Are you planning to just pretend there’s music?” She asked dryly.

Agatha grinned, undeterred. “Do we need music?” She tilted her head, batting her eyelashes in a melodramatic, mock-innocent way. Rio rolled her eyes again before standing and brushing away the leaves that clung to her.

Agatha grinned and pulled Rio close to her. “So, come here often?” she asked, as if they were strangers meeting in a dim, moonlit corner for the first time.

Rio couldn’t help but laugh, the sound filling the quiet space. “Oh, is that your opening line? Pretty bold.”

“Hey,” Agatha countered, crossing her arms in mock offense. “I’ve been practicing that one. I think it’s rather charming.” 

"Well, in that case… how could I resist?”

Agatha stepped close, resting her hand on Rio’s waist, her other hand securely in Rio’s grasp. They began to sway, a gentle, unhurried rhythm as they circled one another in the dim light. The Shadeblooms cast a silvery glow around them, their soft petals swaying as if dancing, too.

Rio chuckled, glancing around them with a playful shake of her head. “You think we really don’t need any music then, do we?”

Agatha leaned in, her lips hovering close to Rio’s ear. “Not with you. But if you've got the lost souls of a four piece band milling about here do let me know. For next time.”

They continued to sway, slowly and softly, Agatha’s fingers tracing gentle patterns along Rio’s shoulder. The teasing melted into something quiet and tender as they moved together, breaths syncing, their laughter fading into soft smiles.

Rio let her head rest on Agatha’s shoulder.

As they moved together, Rio felt a still unaccustomed warmth settle over her, threading its way through her defenses. Agatha was pressed close, her laughter quiet but bright, her fingers soft where they laced through Rio’s own. There was no music, no rhythm but the quiet pulse of the underworld's machinery around them. And yet, in Agatha’s arms, Rio found herself lost in something she’d never thought she could want, let alone need.

She let herself look at Agatha—the way her eyes sparkled, the way she’d gone to such lengths to create this small, beautiful moment. It was such a simple gesture, but in its simplicity, it was more profound than anything Rio had experienced in centuries. Agatha’s fingers grazed her cheek as she moved, and Rio felt herself pull closer, her heart rising unbidden.

The realization was sudden, almost startling. This wasn’t just attachment, or admiration, or even infatuation. The word that lingered on her tongue, the one she’d never dared let herself consider, was love . It filled her with a longing she didn’t know how to put into words, a desire to meet Agatha’s vulnerability with her own. In that instant, Rio saw herself reflected in Agatha’s eyes, and it was as if her defenses melted away, leaving only her raw, unguarded self.

The bearer of last breaths had found herself craving the beating heart of another.

It was a thought that might once have terrified her, might have driven her to retreat, to push Agatha away. But tonight, it filled her with wonder. She wanted to tell her—to let Agatha know, without the usual reservations, that she had somehow woven herself into Rio’s very soul.

Rio felt another pulse of warmth unfurling within her, battling against the coolness of her usual stoicism. The laughter, the teasing moments, and the intimate glances they’d shared over the evening coalesced into something undeniable, something deep and wild that she had tried to cage for too long. 

With each gentle turn, she pulled Agatha closer, the rhythm of their hearts syncing in a dance that felt both old and new. The world around them dimmed, fading into the background, leaving only the sound of their breaths mingling in the quiet night.

“Agatha,” Rio began, her voice barely above a whisper as she spun them into a dip, holding her steady. She met Agatha’s gaze, those vibrant eyes filled with a mixture of curiosity and anticipation. “I need to tell you something.” 

Agatha’s brow furrowed slightly, but there was no trace of fear in her expression—only the kind of trust that made Rio's heart ache. “What is it?” she prompted, concern etched in her features.

Rio raised her back to standing and cupped her cheek with her hand.

“I’ve never… I’ve never really let anyone in,” Rio admitted, the confession spilling out before she could second-guess herself. “You know how I am, how I’ve always kept my distance. Even from you.” 

Agatha nodded slowly, her breath hitching as she sensed the weight of Rio’s words. “But…”

Rio took a deep breath, steadying herself. “But you’ve made me want to change that. You’ve made this place feel less like a tomb and more like a home.” She hesitated, her heart racing. “I’m not good at this, at being vulnerable, but... I think I might be falling for you, Agatha.”

The admission hung in the air, fragile yet potent. Rio felt her chest constrict as she fought against the surge of emotions flooding her, fighting against the instinct to retreat back into her guarded shell. 

Agatha's eyes widened, shimmering with surprise, and in that moment, Rio knew she had revealed more than just her feelings. She had laid bare the truth of her heart, and all that remained was to see how Agatha would respond to this leap of faith.

“Oh. I think that’s the most beautiful thing I’ve ever heard.” Agatha breathed out, voice full of awe.

Rio's breath caught in her throat as Agatha’s earnest words washed over her, a soft balm against her fear. The tension in her chest began to ease, replaced by something warm and radiant that spread through her like sunlight breaking through clouds.

“Really?” Rio asked, her voice barely above a whisper, searching Agatha’s face for any hint of doubt.

“Really,” Agatha affirmed, her smile blooming bright and full of life. “You don’t know how long I’ve wanted to hear that from you.”

Rio’s heart soared, but a small flutter of uncertainty still lingered. “But I’m not... I’m not exactly” she trailed off, a hint of hesitation creeping into her voice. “I mean I’m the embodiment of death, Agatha.”

“Exactly,” Agatha replied, her tone light and teasing. “You’re a literal goddess of the underworld. I’m punching way up!” She leaned in, her forehead resting against Rio’s. Seriously, she whispered, “I want all of you, even the parts that make you nervous.”

The sincerity in Agatha’s gaze melted away the last of Rio’s reservations. With a soft chuckle, she tucked a loose strand of hair behind Agatha’s ear. “You really are mad, aren’t you?”

“Madly in love,” Agatha corrected, her voice laced with affection.

Rio grinned, the tension melting away as they swayed in the dim light. “Then we’ll go mad together,” she murmured, leaning down to capture Agatha’s lips in a soft kiss. It was tender, electric, and filled with a promise of the journey they were walking together.

As they pulled away, Agatha’s eyes sparkled with mischief. “So, what’s next for us, oh mighty goddess? More dancing under the stars? Maybe a ghostly string quartet? Dancing on top of a grave? Scandalous!” She stuck her tongue out, biting it between her teeth.

Rio laughed, her heart light. “How about we start with something a little less ambitious? Just you, me, and a good bottle of wine.” She lowered them both to sit again under the tree.

Agatha beamed, her smile radiant as she snuggled closer, resting her head on Rio’s shoulder. “I like that plan.”

Together, they embraced the stillness of the night, the shadows around them fading into a canvas painted with the beginnings of something beautiful—a scene of love between a human and a goddess, bound by their shared spark and the promise of more to come.

The veil lifted from between them, their feelings and hearts laid bare... Agatha felt a certain steady feeling wash over her. Nothing would come between this.

She would not allow it.

Chapter End Notes

delivering them (and you) a little fluff... as a little treat.

Wants and Needs

Chapter Summary

Agatha begins to connect with the citizens of the underworld. Unfortunately, or perhaps it is fortunate for her, Death is the jealous type.

Chapter Notes

bumping the rating to E just to be safe

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Every day Agatha grew more comfortable in the place she now called home.

Hidden in the shadows, Rio watched as Agatha held court in her own quiet way, communing wordlessly with the souls that lingered around her. They approached Agatha with a kind of reverence Rio had rarely seen, though the dead could not speak their faces open and grateful, as if Agatha was a warm fire in the heart of the Underworld’s cold and endless night. 

Rio’s fingers clenched at her sides. Kindness, she thought, wouldn’t get these souls anywhere. This was the Underworld, a place built on the edge of desolation and despair; her strength was what kept it in line. Her command. For centuries, fear and order had been her tools, not soft words or gentle reassurances. Yet here were her subjects, her workers, drawn to Agatha as if she could offer them something Rio never could.

Agatha looked up and caught sight of her in the shadows. For a moment, her face shone with a startled awe, and then something softer, almost like gentle defiance. Pushing her boundaries. She whispered a parting word to the souls around her and moved toward Rio with a warm, familiar smile.

“You don’t have to lurk, you know,” Agatha teased, her voice light as she closed the distance between them. “I don’t bite.”

Rio forced a smile, though her jaw was tight. “Maybe you should, with the way they follow you.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow, taken aback by the sharpness of her words. She tilted her head, studying Rio’s expression. “What’s wrong?”

Rio’s eyes narrowed, the words bubbling up before she could stop them. “Nothing you need to worry about.”

The irritation in her tone was unmistakable, and she regretted it the moment it left her lips. But she couldn’t quite swallow down the frustration, the unsettling feeling that everything she had built was shifting beneath her.

Agatha searched her face, her smile fading. “Rio… if I’ve done something—”

Rio cut her off, unable to hold back. “Do you think kindness is enough to keep this place in line, Agatha? These souls need strength, they need fear to survive here. What you’re doing… it isn’t going to help them.”

Agatha’s face softened, though there was an edge to her eyes now, something stubborn and steady. “Strength and fear have their place,” she said, voice quiet but unwavering. “But sometimes, people need to know there’s more than that. That there’s something to hope for.”

Rio felt a strange, piercing twist in her chest at Agatha’s words, and it took everything she had not to retreat, to shield herself behind her carefully built walls. She looked away, her pride too sharp to admit how threatened she felt, how much she feared the growing light Agatha cast on her world—a light that made her own shadows loom larger than ever.

After a tense silence, Rio forced herself to look back at Agatha. “I don’t need hope to rule here,” she muttered, the frustration still pulsing beneath her words. “And neither do they. I give them work, I give them purpose. Trying to remind them of their past… I don’t think that’s a kindness. I think it’s twisting the knife.”

Agatha held her gaze, unflinching. For a moment, Rio thought she might argue, might push back with that quiet conviction that both infuriated and fascinated her. But instead, Agatha only reached out, resting a hand on Rio’s arm, her touch gentle and grounding.

“Maybe so,” she murmured. “But I’m here. And while I am… maybe it’s worth trying to reach them.”

Rio’s chest tightened, caught between her pride at her resolve and a faint shade of jealousy. She pulled her arm away, though the touch lingered like an ember beneath her skin.

“Do what you like,” she said coolly, before turning on her heel. But as she walked away, she felt Agatha’s eyes on her, and for the first time, she wondered if her world could survive a heart softened by love.

She paused a second, and took a deep breath. Perhaps she was being too harsh. People needed community. You couldn’t get everything from one person. Well, most people couldn’t, she only had one other soul that truly captivated her, but Agatha was exceptional. She was still wary of Agatha’s influence but if it was companionship that her love was looking for, maybe she could redirect her to a more suitable target.

After a moment’s hesitation, Rio glanced back at Agatha, who was still watching her, waiting with that same patient gaze. The pull between them felt too tense, and Rio, unsure of how to untangle it, took a deep breath and forced a lightness into her tone. 

“Since you seem so keen on company,” she began, her voice deliberately nonchalant, “there’s… someone I think you should meet.” 

Agatha tilted her head, her interest piqued. “Someone?”  

Rio nodded, a faint smirk tugging at her lips. “Or rather… something.” She gestured for Agatha to follow, and, with a lingering glance, Agatha fell into step beside her as they walked deeper into the Underworld, down winding paths lined with shadowed trees and jagged rock formations. 

As they approached a clearing, Rio stopped, her gaze sharpening. “Cerberus,” she called, her voice echoing through the cavernous space, commanding and steady. She whistled lowly.

There was a deep rumble, like thunder rolling through the earth, and a massive figure stepped out of the shadows. Agatha’s eyes widened as she took in the three-headed hound, each head watching her with an intensity that was both terrifying and awe-inspiring. Cerberus’ fur was a dark rippling black, eyes glowing red and yellow, his posture both imposing and regal.

“Meet Cerberus,” Rio said, her voice filled with a strange mix of pride and reverence. “He’s been by my side since I first took the throne. He guards the boundaries, keeping the lost souls in check.” 

Agatha took a tentative step forward, her eyes wide with wonder. “He’s… incredible.”

Cerberus sniffed the air, then took a step closer, his middle head lowering to inspect her. Agatha held still, meeting the creature’s gaze without flinching, and after a moment, the hound let out a soft chuff, his heads turning to Rio as if seeking her approval. Rio watched the exchange with a faint smile, feeling an unexpected warmth as she saw Agatha’s awe.

“He’s not used to visitors,” Rio said softly, stepping forward to lay a hand on Cerberus’ massive shoulder. “But I thought you might appreciate his company. A little… distraction from the lost souls, perhaps?”

Agatha looked over at Rio, understanding the offer behind the words. “Thank you,” she said quietly, reaching out to let Cerberus sniff her hand before giving him a gentle scratch behind his ear. One of the hound’s heads closed its eyes, leaning into her touch with a rumbling sigh, and Agatha laughed softly. “He’s a sweetheart, isn’t he?” 

Rio chuckled, a low, rare sound. “Sweetheart isn’t the word I’d use. But he’s loyal. And he’s powerful. Qualities I can rely on.”

Agatha glanced over at her, a softness in her gaze. “It sounds like you’re talking about someone else besides the dog.”

Rio’s smirk faded, a flicker of vulnerability passing over her face before she masked it. She reached up to scratch Cerberus’ head, her gaze averted. “He’s a reminder that strength doesn’t need… many words to be effective,” she muttered, but even as she said it, she felt a pang of doubt.

Agatha didn’t push, but she moved closer, her hand brushing against Rio’s. “Maybe it doesn’t,” she murmured. “But loyalty and strength don’t have to come from fear, Rio. Sometimes, they come from love.”

Rio tensed, her chest tightening as she looked away, back toward the shadows. But even as she did, Cerberus leaned against Agatha, nudging her hand with a low, contented huff, as though he had already chosen his side.

She sighed and deflected, trying to control the conversation. “Well, I know he’d like some more company. He gets antsy like his mama sometimes.” She laughed, as if to prove her point, Cerberus licked Agatha, his massive tongue lolling from her hand all the way up her arm and face.

Agatha laughed despite herself and scratched under his chin. “That’s okay… maybe like his mama he just needs a firm hand on his leash,” she teased, eyes sparkling mischievously.

Rio rolled her eyes.

A distraction, for now. But it wouldn’t last.

Rio had seethed with rage when she found a few shades lingering in the garden, in their garden, their sacred space. They had abandoned their duties, curiously following Agatha to this place. She stormed into the space, magic crackling at her fingertips as she lashed out with a sickly green bolt of energy. “Out!  All of you! You have work to do.” She hissed, a grim satisfaction passing over her as the souls rushed away.

“Rio,” Agatha said softly, realizing her lover’s temper was short today. “You didn’t need to do that. They were just keeping me company.”

Another silence. The faintest flicker of impatience crossed Rio’s face, and then her gaze snapped to Agatha, sharp and accusing. “They followed you to this place like they thought they could. Like they are an equal, like they get the same privileges you do. You do realize what that means, don’t you?”

Agatha blinked, thrown by the accusation in her tone. “What are you talking about? Rio, I’m just… I’m just trying to give them a space to rest. I’m not trying to take anything from you.”

Rio scoffed, turning away. “But you are, without even meaning to. They flock to you now, they pay attention to you. They look to you—and not to me.”

“Rio,” Agatha stepped forward, her voice soft, trying to soothe the bitterness she could see building in Rio’s eyes. “They still respect you—”

“Do they?” Rio’s voice rose, bitter and biting. “They look at you like you’re some guiding light, some warmth they’ve never known here. You’ve become a balm, a distraction. And now they’re beginning to question me, to question the very way this realm was built. They’re questioning what they’re doing here. And it’s not something they have a choice in. I give them jobs because if their minds aren’t occupied they start to think of everything up there, everything that they’re missing, it will drive them insane. It will change them, and not in the way you’re hoping!”

Agatha felt the words hit her like a cold wind, and she struggled to find a response that would steady Rio’s fears. “I didn’t… I didn’t mean to change anything. I was only trying to bring them some peace.”

Rio’s eyes narrowed, her voice lowering to a harsh whisper. “And by doing so, you’ve taken more than you know.”

Agatha’s throat tightened, the weight of Rio’s words pressing on her heart. She could see the hurt buried beneath Rio’s frustration, but reaching it felt like stepping through fire. “Rio… please, let me help—”

But Rio’s pride flared, and she pulled away, retreating further into herself. “I don’t need your help,” she said coldly, her voice closing like a door. “Maybe you should save your kindness for the souls who you seem to think need it more than I do.”

Without another word, she turned and left, her footsteps echoing through the empty space, leaving Agatha alone.

Agatha felt the chill left in Rio’s wake, the weight of what was happening settling onto her shoulders. She realized that this rift could not be mended easily.

But Agatha also knew that this anger was personal to Rio. She knew that in her way, the woman was trying to help them make the most of their situation. They just had different ways of going about it. Misaligned perspectives tied to the intrinsic truth that only one of them had lived experiences of human life. 

She would let Rio cool off a little bit. They were getting better at handling conflict. She had learned that with time she could usually bring Rio around to her point of view. It was a truth she wielded delicately though.

Some time later, Agatha found Rio lounging in a comfortable chair inside Agatha’s room. She approached slowly, careful not to startle Rio, who sat with her arms crossed tightly, her gaze fixed on some distant, invisible point.

But Agatha took solace in the fact that Rio wanted to be found. If not she wouldn’t be in Agatha’s room, occupying her favorite chair. Sulking, granted, but here. 

Agatha took a soft breath, then crossed the threshold, coming to perch on the arm of the chair next to her. For a moment, she tried to think of something to say that would cut through the heavy air, something to make her smile, even just a little. She leaned closer, raising an eyebrow, her mouth tilting into a tentative grin.

“Would it be weird if I tried to make you laugh?” she murmured, nudging her shoulder gently. “I know, it’s a tall order, but I’ve heard I can be pretty charming.”

Rio gave a small huff, the tiniest ghost of a smile tugging at the corner of her mouth, but she didn’t respond. Her arms stayed crossed, her defenses carefully in place.

Agatha’s heart clenched, but she swallowed her own pride and reached for Rio’s hand, folding her fingers over hers. Her voice dropped to a whisper. “You’re still their queen, and no one can replace you.”

Rio’s gaze softened, her eyes flicking to Agatha’s hand. “They’re not seeing me that way anymore, Agatha. And that’s because of you.”

Agatha bit her lip, the truth settling uncomfortably between them. She wanted to reassure her, to deny it, but the words wouldn’t come. Because, deep down, she knew Rio was right. Every time she extended a hand to the Underworld’s people, she felt her own purpose deepen. And with each of those moments, she felt a subtle shift, a slow but certain pull, as if her very presence here was drawing Rio’s people away from her, one by one.

“I didn’t mean for any of this to happen,” Agatha murmured, her voice barely above a whisper. “I don’t want to fight. I don’t want to upset you. I only wanted to help.”

“I know,” Rio said, but there was a sadness in her tone, a resignation that felt like an ache in the air between them. She ran a hand through her hair and poked her tongue into her cheek. “You’re changing things, Agatha. And I… I don’t know if I like it. I don’t know if I even understand it.”

Frustrated as she was though, Rio couldn’t stay truly mad for long. She had fallen in love with a human heart, she couldn’t fairly expect her to act against it. She sighed before moving her hand to Agatha’s waist, pulling her into her lap. “Come here. You know I hate it when you hover,” she grumbled.

“Well,” she murmured, turning so her gaze could catch Rio’s, brushing her nose against her jaw, “you’re still my queen, you know. And I… I can be a very loyal subject.”

Rio is called to the surface and is surprised to find Agatha waiting for her.

Even if she found the spell or ritual she needed, it might not work—or worse, it might ask something of her that would endanger everything she and Agatha had fought for.

Still, the risk was worth it. She could not bear the thought of losing Agatha, of separating her from their child. She had time, she reminded herself, a precious few months before Agatha’s return. A few after that before the child, their child , would take its first breath. And during that time, she would do everything in her power to find a way to keep them both safe here, within the only home she had ever known.

Her fingers flexed, her heart brimming with fierce determination. She would leave no stone unturned, no spell untested. She owed that to Agatha, to the love that had defied all odds, and to the child she had never dreamed could exist. 

She allowed herself a small, glimmering hope—maybe, just maybe, she would find a way to make this work.

Rio sank into her throne, letting herself imagine the life growing inside Agatha— their child, a soul born of two worlds, with one foot in light and the other in darkness. She tried to picture the face of this impossible miracle, her mind flitting over features she might recognize as her own or as Agatha’s, softened or sharpened in ways she couldn’t yet see.

Would their child carry Agatha’s bright blue eyes, with that fierce spark of curiosity that had always unnerved Rio? Or perhaps they’d have her own, darker gaze, tempered by the weight of ancient knowledge and a sense of stillness that only the underworld could bestow. She imagined a blend of their features: soft, smiling lips like Agatha’s, but framed by a serious expression that mirrored her own. A wild mess of hair, perhaps, something that would remind her of both Agatha’s resilience and her own stubborn nature.

And their temperament—would they take after Agatha, with her boundless compassion, that endless urge to nurture and heal? Or would their child inherit Rio’s guardedness, her silent strength, her need to protect those she loved even at her own expense? She wondered if their child might grow into a ruler like her, but with a softer hand, a gentler touch that Rio herself had never quite mastered. Or perhaps they would wield a fiery, rebellious spirit like Agatha’s, tempered with the wisdom and restraint that came from carrying death in their veins.

A smile, faint and unbidden, tugged at Rio’s lips as she imagined a laugh that would sound like both of theirs woven together—a unique echo of their love. She thought of small hands reaching for hers, of a voice calling her to her as its mother.

As these visions took hold, a wave of tenderness flooded through her. She could see Agatha’s influence, their love, their life together, woven into this child who might one day challenge both of them, who would come to know both the land of the living and the underworld as their birthrights. This child, she realized, could grow to be the best of both worlds—both theirs, but wholly themselves.

The thought was terrifying and beautiful, and it anchored her resolve to find a way to keep Agatha and their child safe, no matter the cost. For the first time, Rio allowed herself to hope that, somehow, this impossible dream could be more than fleeting. It could be a future—a future with Agatha, with their child, and with a love that defied even death’s own limits.

She would make it so. She had to. For all of their sakes.

Nesting

Chapter Summary

A miracle grows.

Chapter Notes

canon left me with more questions than answers so here's 6k of domestic pregnancy fluff

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Agatha sat on the porch of the cabin, gazing over the small clearing. It was isolated, surrounded by thick trees and dense fog that only seemed to clear around midday. Her hands rested on her stomach, almost protectively, as she took in the silence around her. It was hers now. She’d been decisive—ruthless, even—but she couldn’t bring herself to regret it. This cabin, nestled in the woods and smelling faintly of pine and smoke, could be the closest thing to a home she’d have for the coming months.

She couldn’t shake the anticipation that filled her as she thought of Rio joining her here. She’d be here soon. The previous owner, a hunter, lay just outside the threshold. Agatha hadn’t liked the way he’d leered at her anyway. The way his warning about how “a woman with child shouldn’t be in these dangerous woods,” had sounded like a threat.

At the familiar brush of cold air, she turned to see Rio appear just beyond the treeline. Agatha’s heart skipped as Rio’s gaze swept over her, then the cabin, taking in the surroundings with an expression of barely concealed curiosity. Agatha gave her a small, playful smile, trying to lighten the sudden weight in the air between them.

Rio’s mouth quirked into a smirk as she stepped forward. “So,” she said, her voice rich with amusement, “you killed someone else just to see me?”

Agatha rolled her eyes, though her lips curved in response. “Do you think I just kill someone every time I miss you?” She raised an eyebrow, a playful gleam in her eye. “I’d have a very long list by now, wouldn’t I?”

Rio’s smirk softened, a warmth flickering in her expression. She stepped closer, tracing her fingers over the cabin’s doorframe. As she traced the entryway, a wreath bloomed to hang just over the door. Woven branches of cedar for protection, and little bundles of lavender, rosemary, and mugwort to strengthen the effect. “It’s… more than I expected,” she admitted, glancing around, as if surprised Agatha had made this effort. “Though I truly didn’t expect to see you yet.”

She let her eyes roam over Agatha’s body, settling on the swell of her stomach. A few months had passed and it was obvious how her lover’s body was changing as their child grew. Rio had always been hopelessly attracted to her, but now every protective instinct she carried was heightened. 

“Oh, come now, Rio,” Agatha teased, her tone light but her eyes serious. “You get so few glimpses of this life we’re creating. And I… I want you here. I don’t want you to miss anything.”

At her words, Rio’s gaze softened, and she reached out, cupping Agatha’s cheek in her cool hand. “You did all this because you wanted me to see… what exactly?” she asked, voice low, a tenderness creeping in.

Agatha took Rio’s hand and placed it gently over her stomach. She saw the quick flicker of wonder in Rio’s eyes, and it sent a warmth flooding through her. “This,” she murmured, her voice steady despite the vulnerability that gripped her. 

Rio felt the unmistakable kick beneath her palm, and her breath caught, the sensation incredibly surreal. Her gaze stayed fixed on Agatha’s stomach, an awe spreading over her face that she couldn’t hide. She had expected to feel a stirring—some flicker of awareness—but this? This was life, tangible and undeniable, pushing back against her touch with a strength that left her stunned.

Her hand remained on Agatha’s stomach, fingers splayed as though to anchor her to this impossible reality. “They’re strong,” she murmured, her voice thick with reverence. “Our child… They’re already strong.” She knelt in front of Agatha and pressed a gentle kiss to her stomach. “Aren’t you little one?”

Agatha watched her, an almost shy smile tugging at her lips. “They take after you, I think,” she replied, her voice soft.

Rio shook her head, her gaze still glued to the place where her child had kicked. “You,” she said, an uncharacteristic, quiet certainty in her tone. “That spirit—that resilience—no one could mistake that for anyone but you.”

Agatha laughed, a gentle sound filled with warmth. “I think they’re a little of both of us, don’t you?” She reached down, brushing her fingers along Rio’s jaw, grounding her in the moment. “A life that could only be created because we found each other.”

Rio’s chin lifted, her gaze meeting Agatha’s. She hadn’t imagined, not even in her wildest dreams, that she could be a part of something so… alive. She, who had always been the bringer of endings, was here, holding the beginning of something precious and entirely hers.

“Agatha…” She paused, unable to find words grand enough to capture the wonder she felt, the fierce protectiveness that flared up inside her. It was a feeling so intense it threatened to overwhelm her, and yet, all she could do was whisper, “I… I will keep you both safe. No matter what it takes.”

Agatha’s hand reached down and pulled her to her feet, her fingers threading through Rio’s own. “I know,” she said simply, the unwavering faith in her voice grounding Rio even more.

They stayed like that for a long moment, the quiet punctuated only by their shared breaths, a peace settling between them that seemed to pull the whole world into focus. Rio’s hand lingered over the life they’d created together, marveling at the impossible future unfolding before her.

Agatha led her into the little cabin. “I thought… it’d make a nice cottage for a little while, somewhere we could… be together.” She smiled, a bit sheepishly. “Think of it as a tiny piece of the mortal world, where we can pretend.”

Rio let her hand linger over Agatha’s stomach, her fingers splaying with reverence. A strange mix of emotions crossed her face, as if she were seeing something precious and forbidden all at once. Her gaze turned almost teasing again, though her voice was laced with affection. “You’re lucky I’m rather fond of you, or I’d have to scold you and remind you not to kill anyone for me. Not every time, at least. You’re setting a bad example for the kid.”

Agatha chuckled softly, her free hand trailing up Rio’s arm. “I’ll try to restrain myself in the future.”

A quiet filled the space between them, charged yet tender. Rio’s gaze drifted down, lingering where her hand rested on Agatha’s stomach. Her face grew contemplative.

Rio’s voice dropped to a near whisper. “You want me to stay here… so I can see them grow,” she murmured, the words almost lost in the air between them.

Agatha nodded, her eyes bright. “Yes. I want you to be here… to be part of this. Whatever happens, Rio, this—” She placed her hand over Rio’s, pressing it gently against her. “This belongs to us. You’re part of this just as much as I am. And no one else, no person, no fate, nothing will stand in the way of that.”

Rio’s face softened, her expression unreadable as she studied Agatha’s face. “You’re… relentless,” she murmured, a faint, almost affectionate accusation.

“You love it,” Agatha countered, her voice warm, with that mischievous gleam that Rio could never resist.

Rio’s mouth lifted at one corner, and she drew Agatha close, pressing a kiss to her forehead, lingering a little longer than usual. “Maybe I do,” she admitted, her voice barely a breath.

They stood together in the silence of the cabin, the world around them hushed, as if the woods themselves respected the intimacy of the moment. And for now, at least, there was nothing but them—an unspoken promise hanging between them in that tiny, hidden cabin.

“Can you stay?” Agatha’s question was soft, hopeful, her eyes searching Rio’s with a quiet longing.

“I… have work,” Rio replied, her voice regretful, though her hand still lingered, reluctant to let go.

“Soon, then,” Agatha said, a gentle smile in her eyes as she squeezed Rio’s hand. “Just don’t take too long.”

Rio returned the squeeze, a rare softness in her own gaze. “I’ll come as soon as I can.” She leaned forward, pressing a lingering kiss to Agatha’s lips, then drew back slowly, her gaze flicking to Agatha’s stomach one last time. “I’ll see you both soon,” she murmured, a quiet promise lingering in the air between them. Then, with a final kiss, she stepped back, her presence fading into the cool night air, leaving Agatha alone with the heartbeat of their shared dream nestled beneath her own.

For a few precious months that summer, it was as if a great and subtle grace had swept over the world. The wars that had raged across continents seemed to slow, like tides drawn back to rest. Armies found themselves halting, the battles that had felt inevitable slipping out of focus, their edges blunted as treaties took hold where none should have. 

In places around the world, doctors and healers witnessed small wonders—patients who had been all but gone took unexpected, almost magical turns toward life. Plagued lungs strengthened, fevers broke, and doctors shook their heads, chalking it up to mysteries of medicine or blessings from above. But behind these recoveries was Rio, quietly holding back her hand from souls she might once have claimed.

And as she spent more time with Agatha, each recovery, each life saved felt like another step into a fragile and vibrant world she was still learning to understand. The weight of her usual duties became more distant, softened by Agatha's touch, by the feeling of their child growing day by day. When she looked into Agatha’s eyes or felt the soft pulse of their child’s heartbeat beneath her fingers, she felt her unyielding commitment shift, softened by something unthinkable—a willingness to let things be, to allow for joy.

She still had to frequently return to the underworld, she couldn’t allow the souls to grow restless and idle. There was also the business of what she would do when Agatha was due to return there. But when she was in the sun, sharing that sacred little home with her, she put those things out of her mind.

The world flourished with an almost tangible warmth, a soft but miraculous pulse of hope woven through even the simplest lives. Stories trickled through villages and towns of children who should not have woken up but had, of frail elders who somehow made it through the night hanging on just a little bit longer. These tales of unlikely recoveries filled people with joy and a quiet awe, as if, for a brief moment, they’d been allowed a glimpse of a life lighter than before. 

And for Rio, this peace felt like a stolen gift—a way to indulge in what she'd believed was impossible: a chance to share time, love, and life with Agatha and their unborn child. She knew, of course, that she could not stay away forever. Every person only had so much time. But for now, each of those reclaimed lives, those miraculous recoveries, seemed a fair trade for one more precious day together.

As the beginning of the end of summer cast its golden light over the cabin, Agatha shifted in her chair, trying to find a comfortable position. She was visibly uncomfortable, her hand resting on her lower back as she leaned forward, a weary sigh escaping her lips. Her once-swift movements had slowed, and even simple tasks left her breathless. The baby seemed to grow heavier by the day, pressing against her bones and pulling at her muscles in a way that was both miraculous and exhausting.

Rio noticed the strain in Agatha’s face the moment she walked in, and without a word, she slipped off her cloak and came to her side. She held a freshly-picked bundle of lavender and chamomile in her hands, the small flowers carefully arranged with a few sprays of delicate, tiny daisies in between.

“Lavender to ease your rest, chamomile to soften your worries, and daisies,” Rio said with a quiet smile, “for the innocence of new life.”

Agatha leaned into her touch, smiling despite her discomfort. “You’re too good to me,” she murmured, her voice filled with a weary warmth. 

Rio knelt down beside her, reaching for Agatha’s hand and pressing a soft kiss to her knuckles. “Good has nothing to do with it. I just… I want to see you relaxed. As much as you can be,” she added, her thumb brushing along Agatha’s knuckles with a tenderness that was somehow both gentle and fierce.

Agatha’s smile softened as she looked down at Rio, a tenderness filling her gaze. “I know,” she whispered, squeezing Rio’s hand. “And I’m grateful. I really am. But…” She hesitated, her words weighed down by a heaviness she’d tried to ignore. “It’s hard, Rio. Carrying them alone, even with you coming here as often as you can. It’s—” She broke off, her eyes tearing slightly. “It’s… a lot. And some days, I feel like I can barely make it through.”

The words tumbled out before she could stop them, and she lowered her gaze, feeling almost guilty for admitting her weariness. She wanted so much to be strong, to show Rio how much she could handle. But as the days had stretched into months, her strength had started to wane under the quiet but constant toll of carrying their child.

Rio’s face softened, and she brought her hand up to cup Agatha’s cheek, brushing her thumb gently along her jawline. “I wish I could be here every moment,” she said, a note of regret slipping into her voice. “If I could, I’d stay by your side and make sure you didn’t have to lift a single finger. I’d carry the weight with you if I could.”

Agatha’s eyes brightened, though a glint of tears shimmered there as she leaned into Rio’s touch. “I know you would,” she replied, her voice barely above a whisper. “And knowing that helps. It really does. But some days… I just wish you could be here more.”

Rio looked away briefly, her expression taut with frustration. She had bent so many rules, stretched the boundaries of her duties just to spend these moments with Agatha, but it was never enough. Not for either of them. Every time she left, she felt as though she was abandoning her, leaving her to bear the burden alone. And yet, each time she returned, Agatha was still there, waiting with open arms, as if every stolen moment was enough to sustain her.

Rio didn’t deal in half measures. Yet here she was caught between love and obligation.

Reaching for Agatha’s other hand, Rio met her gaze, determination in her eyes. “For as long as I can be here, I’ll do everything I can to make it easier. And when I’m not…” She faltered, feeling the weight of her own helplessness. “When I’m not, just remember that I’m with you in every way I can be, even if you can’t see me. I’ll make sure these woods protect you. I’ll keep you safe.”

Agatha gave a small nod, her lips curving into a tired but grateful smile. “Thank you,” she murmured, her hand reaching up to gently brush a stray lock of hair from Rio’s forehead. “I don’t know what I’d do without you.”

Rio’s expression softened, and she gave Agatha’s hand a reassuring squeeze. “You’re stronger than you know,” she whispered, a faint smile tugging at her lips. “But I’ll be here as much as I can to remind you.”

They stayed that way for a moment, each taking comfort in the quiet presence of the other. Finally, Rio shifted, a glimmer of playfulness returning to her eyes. She moved her hand down to Agatha’s belly, her fingers brushing lightly over the swell, as if trying to connect with the tiny life growing inside.

“Hey, little one,” she murmured, leaning closer, her voice low and playful. “Listen up. Your mother is the strongest person I know, and you’d better be nice to her, or you’ll be dealing with me. Stop doing acrobatics in there, you keep punching her bladder.”

Agatha let out a soft laugh, her fingers lacing through Rio’s hair as she watched her with an affectionate smile. “You’re going to scare them before they even have a chance to misbehave.”

Rio raised an eyebrow, a smirk tugging at the corners of her mouth. “Oh, I fully intend to. This child of ours will need a healthy respect for the rules. Otherwise, I’m afraid they’ll take after you a little too well.”

Agatha laughed, the sound rich and full despite her fatigue. “Is that right? And who’s the one always bending the rules to be here?”

Rio feigned innocence, lifting her gaze to meet Agatha’s. “That’s called dedication,” she replied with a grin, “a trait I hope they inherit.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, shaking her head as she continued to smile. “Dedication, sure. And I suppose they’ll get my knack for rule-breaking along with your sense of duty. That’s a dangerous combination.”

Rio’s expression softened, her hand moving gently over Agatha’s belly as if she were imagining the future she barely dared to hope for. “Maybe so,” she said, her voice quiet but filled with warmth. “There are worse things.”

“Can you stay awhile?” Agatha asked, hating how small her voice sounded.

“Sure dear, I’ll just call for world peace for a little longer. No big deal,” Rio teased. She stood and leaned down to kiss Agatha. “I can stay a little longer. What do you need from me?”

“Right now I need to lay down,” Agatha said tiredly.

Rio nodded and led her to the bed tucked in the corner of the room.

Agatha looked up at Rio, her expression softening, a hint of something unspoken glimmering in her eyes. She hesitated, then gave a small, almost shy smile. “I miss you, you know,” she murmured, her voice barely above a whisper. “Not just you being here… but your touch. All of that feels so distant sometimes.” She paused, biting her lip. “It’s like there’s a part of me that’s constantly waiting, missing you, even when you’re right here.”

Rio’s gaze softened as she reached out, tucking a loose strand of hair behind Agatha’s ear. “I know,” she replied quietly, her thumb brushing gently over Agatha’s cheek. Her mind drifted, unbidden, to memories of their more intimate moments—the quiet laughter they shared in the dark, the way Agatha’s fingers traced patterns along her, the warmth and closeness that wrapped around them like a shield from the world. She felt her heart quicken at the thought, longing settling in her chest like a weight.

Agatha’s lips curved in a gentle smile, as if she, too, were lost in the memory. “I think about it sometimes,” she admitted, a faint blush coloring her cheeks. “I know I’m not exactly graceful right now, but… well…” Her voice trailed off, and she looked up at Rio, a soft glimmer of mischief in her eyes.

Rio chuckled, the sound low and warm. “I think graceful is highly overrated,” she replied with a grin, her fingers tracing small, comforting circles over Agatha’s hand. “But perhaps,” she added, her voice softening as her gaze drifted to Agatha’s shoulders, tense from carrying the weight of the baby, “a massage might do for now?”

Agatha’s eyes lit up, and she nodded with eager enthusiasm. “Yes, please. That sounds… wonderful.” She leaned back, trying to find a comfortable position as Rio gently guided her to sit at the edge of the bed, reaching for a small bottle of lavender-scented oil she’d brought a few visits ago.

Rio chuckled softly. “I think I have a pretty good idea,” she replied, her voice filled with warmth. “You’ve been carrying a lot—literally and otherwise. I’d be a poor partner if I didn’t make sure you were taken care of.”

Agatha smiled, her eyes still closed as she leaned into Rio’s touch, letting herself be cared for in a way that she often struggled to allow. “You always know just what I need,” she whispered, feeling a wave of gratitude wash over her. 

Rio’s hands moved down her back, tracing over each curve with a reverence that spoke of her love, her fingers working away every bit of tension they found. For a moment, the world outside their cabin felt far away, as if it were just the two of them, caught in this quiet, tender moment.

As the massage continued, Agatha felt her worries slip away, her heart filled with a deep, steady peace she rarely allowed herself to feel. She reached out, squeezing Rio’s hand as she whispered, “Thank you… for being here. For everything.”

Rio leaned down, pressing a soft kiss to Agatha’s shoulder. “Always,” she murmured, letting her lips linger there as if to seal her promise. “For as long as you need me. C’mere, let me get your legs.”

Flowers of every color were scattered along the windowsill, filling the room with a faint, sweet perfume.

So if you’re listening in there, little one, you’d better make things easy on her, understand?” She rubbed gentle circles over Agatha’s belly, her fingers light, as if coaxing an agreement from the unborn listener. “It’s both of our jobs to keep her happy. So no slacking, junior.”

Rio’s grin widened, and she shrugged, not breaking eye contact with Agatha’s belly. “I don’t see why not,” she replied with a smirk. “Someone has to get them in line before they get here.”
