She tilted her head thoughtfully, amusement lighting her eyes as she considered the baby nestled between them. “You know, I’m trying to picture what kind of mothers we’ll be,” she said, casting a sidelong glance at Rio. “But all I can see is you being the one who spoils them rotten.”

Rio scoffed, her brows lifting in mock offense. “Me? Spoiling them?” She leaned back, crossing her arms with an exaggerated pout. “Excuse me, but I think we both know who the soft one in this relationship really is.”

“Oh, really?” Agatha shot back, arching an eyebrow. “I seem to remember you bringing me flowers every single time you come back to the cabin. And don’t think I haven’t noticed how you get all teary every time you feel the baby kick. That’s not exactly the behavior of someone who’s going to be strict.”

Rio huffed, though she couldn’t hide the small, embarrassed smile tugging at her lips. “Alright, fine. I might have a soft spot, but that doesn’t mean I’ll be the one giving in every time they want something ridiculous. That’ll be you.”

“Me?” Agatha laughed, shaking her head as she settled back against the pillows. “Please, you’re the one who’s already talking to them in soft, endearing tones. I’m pretty sure you’ll melt the first time they give you those big, pleading eyes. You can’t even refuse that dog of yours anything.”

Rio smirked, trailing her hand gently over Agatha, lost in thought. “Maybe… but if they start picking up bad habits, we’ll know who to blame.” She gave Agatha a pointed look, her eyes twinkling with mischief.

“Oh?” Agatha replied, her tone just as teasing. “What bad habits are you so worried about?”

Rio’s lips curved into a smirk as she leaned forward, resting her forehead against Agatha’s. “Well, for starters, that sharp tongue of yours,” she murmured, tapping her fingers playfully against Agatha’s side. “Or your tendency to act first and think later. Imagine a tiny little troublemaker, running around, charming everyone into their schemes.” 

Agatha rolled her eyes, but couldn’t keep the grin from her face. “And I suppose they’ll get their brooding and self-righteous streak from you, then? They’ll probably be a master of sarcasm before they can even walk.” 

Rio snorted. “Oh, absolutely. They’ll have to be, with you around,” she teased, her eyes softening as she gazed at Agatha. “But they’ll be brave, too. And stubborn as anything. I wonder if we’re ready for that.”

Agatha’s smile softened, and she reached to brush her fingers along Rio’s cheek. “I think… they’ll have all the best parts of us. They’ll be strong and clever, and, if we’re lucky, maybe just a little bit rebellious.”

Rio laughed, leaning in to press a kiss to Agatha’s forehead. “Then we’re going to have our hands full,” she said, feigning exasperation, though the pride in her voice was unmistakable. 

Agatha leaned into her, wrapping an arm around her neck and letting her fingers trail through Rio’s hair. “I suppose we’re in for a lifetime of spoiling, discipline, and a little chaos in between.”

“Sweetheart, we were already on track for that.” Agatha laughed.

“Well, now there’s going to be a little monster running around too. I’m going to have to keep my eyes on two of you.”

Agatha slapped her shoulder in mock horror, “You did not just call our baby a little monster,” she said with an exasperated smile.

Rio let out a chuckle, feigning innocence as she arched a brow. "What? I’m just being realistic." She placed a hand on Agatha’s belly again, rubbing gentle circles over it. "I mean, they’ll have your stubborn streak. That alone qualifies them as a handful."

Agatha scoffed, though her eyes sparkled with amusement. "Right, you wouldn’t know anything about being stubborn, my love,” she drawled sarcastically. “Between the two of us, this child’s bound to be… let’s say spirited. ”

Rio smirked, clearly enjoying herself. “Spirited. Now there’s a polite way to put it.” She leaned down and spoke softly, directly to the bump. “Hey, little one, you don’t need to be too spirited, alright? Your mother here might not admit it, but she can only handle so much chaos in her life. And I don’t like to be upstaged.”

Agatha laughed, rolling her eyes. “Says the one who literally rules the Underworld. Between that and this kid I think you’re going to be the one needing a nap.”

“I’ll find a way to manage.” Rio’s voice was soft, her fingers tracing gentle patterns across Agatha’s stomach.

Agatha relaxed into her touch, letting herself picture it—the three of them, sharing this quiet life. Her voice turned wistful. “Do you think they’ll have your dark hair?” She paused, a hint of shyness creeping in. “I think they’d look beautiful with it.”

Rio’s expression softened, a trace of wonder in her eyes. “Maybe,” she murmured, her hand shifting to gently squeeze Agatha’s. “And your eyes. I’d like that.” She hesitated, a tender vulnerability slipping through her usual confidence. “Do you think… do you think they’ll be happy?”

“They’ll be cherished. Of course, they will be.” Agatha said softly, brushing a thumb over Rio’s cheek. “They’ll have a garden to grow up in, a river to play by… mothers who loves them more fiercely than anything else in this world.” She leaned forward, kissing Rio gently, pouring all her affection into the touch.

Rio pulled her close, lingering in the kiss as her heart swelled with the magnitude of what they were creating. “I guess I’m going to have to break it to Cerberus that he’s going to be a big brother,” she said. She didn’t let Agatha see it, but internally she recoiled as her thoughtless words reminded her that she still hadn’t fully considered what this child’s place would be in the underworld.

Agatha’s expression softened, and she tilted her head thoughtfully. “Do you think they’ll be a boy or a girl?”

Rio sat back for a moment, considering the question, her gaze distant as she looked at Agatha. “You know, I haven’t given it much thought,” she admitted, brushing her thumb absentmindedly over Agatha’s hand. “I only know…” She paused, her eyes turning bright with a quiet, protective fierceness as she looked back at Agatha. “I only know that they’ll be loved. And they’ll know who you are, Agatha. They’ll know the strength and kindness they came from. They’ll know how powerful the woman they came from is. The magic that brought them here.”

Agatha’s face softened, and she leaned forward, brushing a tender kiss over Rio’s lips. “You’ll be just as much a part of them, you know.”

Rio smiled, her voice barely above a whisper as she murmured, “I think that’s what I’m most afraid of.”

Agatha pulled back slightly, her hand moving to cradle Rio’s face. “What’s there to be afraid of?” she asked, her voice gentle yet firm, trying to pierce through the shadows of doubt in Rio’s gaze. “You’ll be an incredible mother. Fierce, protective… and probably more patient than I will be,” she added with a soft laugh. 

Rio’s lips quirked in a faint smile, but her eyes betrayed her lingering uncertainty. “Death doesn’t nurture, Agatha,” she said, her voice laced with quiet resignation. “I’ve always been the end of things, not the beginning.” She looked down, tracing Agatha’s fingers with her own, as if the answer might be hidden in the lines of her lover’s hand.

Agatha’s hand covered hers, warm and steady. “But love does,” she whispered. “You are so much more than your duty, Rio. You’ve given me a chance to be strong, to heal, to live more fully. And that’s what you’ll give to our child, too.”

Rio closed her eyes, her features softening as Agatha’s words washed over her, soothing the uncertainty that twisted within. She wanted to believe it, to hold onto this fragile hope that had begun to bloom inside her like the flowers she brought Agatha. She opened her eyes, still uncertain, but a glimmer of warmth shone there, a faint ember of belief beginning to take root.

Agatha’s fingers traced gentle circles over Rio’s hand, anchoring her. “Now, back to the question,” she teased lightly, hoping to lighten the mood. “Boy or girl? Any preferences?”

Rio tilted her head thoughtfully, a faint smirk tugging at her lips as she considered it. “Well,” she began, “if it’s a girl, I suppose we’ll have someone to inherit your stubbornness. This world needs more women who are strong and unafraid of their power. And if it’s a boy, well… then perhaps he’ll learn all of my terrible habits, just to give you endless grief. Perhaps he’ll be harsh until he meets someone who turns him into a hopeless romantic that brings them flowers every day.” Her expression softened, the smirk giving way to something genuine and tender. “But honestly… no. I already couldn’t love them more. They’ll be ours, and that’s all I need to know.”

Agatha’s smile was radiant, filled with love and quiet pride. “Then I suppose we’ll just have to wait and see,” she whispered, reaching up to kiss Rio again, their foreheads resting together as they breathed in the warmth and comfort of each other’s presence.

Rio sighed, her fingers brushing tenderly over Agatha’s belly as if making a silent promise. “I may be afraid, but… I’m going to try, for both of you. I’ll do whatever it takes.” 

Agatha brushed a hand over Rio’s hair, soothing her. “And that’s more than enough.”

Rio hummed and rolled them to their sides, draping one arm protectively over Agatha and holding her close. Her breath evened out and though Agatha knew that Rio didn’t need to sleep, she was glad she was taking a few moments to rest.

Agatha lay awake, the quiet weight of her own thoughts settling in. She reached a hand over her stomach, placing it just above where Rio’s still rested, gently tracing small circles as she felt the soft flutter of movement from within. It was a tender, intimate reminder of the life they had created, yet beneath her warmth, a chill ran through her—a shadow of a memory she thought she’d long since buried.

Her mother’s face came to her, unbidden, sharp and cold. Even in her faintest memories, Agatha couldn’t recall her mother’s eyes holding any warmth. It was strange; she had known her mother’s touch, her voice, but never the feeling of being truly loved or cherished. All the tenderness she had found in Rio, she had only once dreamed of knowing.

Agatha’s jaw tightened. She vowed, silently, fiercely, that her child would never know the kind of hollow ache she had felt growing up. She would be a different kind of mother—loving, patient, proud. Their child would know laughter and warmth, encouragement instead of scorn, support instead of judgment.

But in the same breath, fear twisted in her chest. Was there any part of her mother within her? Was there a bitterness that could emerge if pushed, some shard of her mother’s cruelty buried deep within? She closed her eyes, willing the doubt to fade, reminding herself that she’d already broken free from her mother’s legacy in so many ways. She had found love in Rio, someone who had shattered the armor Agatha had so long held close to protect herself. And now, in their child, she would pour everything she had learned of love and devotion.

Her thoughts drifted to Rio. A soft smile curved her lips as she imagined Rio’s interactions with their child—playful and tender, Rio’s gentleness hidden beneath her dry humor, her patience unyielding. She could already see Rio, crouched beside a toddling little one, handing them flowers and explaining their meanings with the utmost seriousness, a glint of warmth in her eyes that she never showed to the world. She imagined Rio patiently guiding their child, teaching them strength without harshness, loyalty without obligation. 

Agatha’s heart softened further as she imagined Rio telling their child stories, her low voice weaving tales of bravery and courage, her eyes bright with love. And she knew, deeply and without doubt, that their child would be safe and cherished. Because Rio would protect them with all the fierce loyalty Agatha had come to love, and Agatha would make sure that their child would know, every day, that they were wanted.

Agatha shifted uncomfortably, her whole body was always uncomfortable now, and turned to face her love. She brushed her fingers over Rio’s sleeping face, the depth of her gratitude swelling up in her. The love they had created was already reshaping the edges of her world, mending wounds she hadn’t even known were still there. With a gentle kiss to Rio’s forehead, she whispered a promise only the night would hear: to be the mother she’d never had, to give their child a life filled with the love that had, against all odds, finally found her.

As she nestled against Rio once more, burying her head against her chest, she closed her eyes, finding comfort in the warmth they shared.

Soon there’d be three of them.

She listened to the steady rise and fall of Rio’s breathing, the quiet, grounding rhythm that had become her anchor in recent months. The thought of soon becoming a family of three filled her with an almost overwhelming mix of emotions. She imagined their child, bundled close to her, small and warm, with Rio by their side, guiding them and protecting them with a fierce yet gentle hand. 

Agatha knew Rio would guard their child with a ferocity that nothing could break.

And with that thought came another, quieter one that both comforted and frightened her: how different her own childhood had been. Agatha had always told herself that she was fine, that she’d built herself strong on the foundation of her own resilience. But the idea of offering her child a life so different, so free from the isolation and fear she’d grown up with, brought a pang of something bittersweet.

Her fingers brushed lightly over Rio’s cheek, her heart swelling with a quiet determination. She would be there for their child in all the ways her own mother hadn’t been. She’d be a constant, a source of strength and warmth, of kindness and encouragement. And when their child faced their own struggles and hurts, as all children do, Agatha would be there—not as a shadow but full in her support, present and unwavering. 

With a soft sigh, she sank deeper into Rio’s warmth, inhaling deeply the scent of her. Before long, there would be a pair of small feet running across the floor, laughter filling every corner. She could already imagine Rio’s amused grin as their child’s questions inevitably turned into mischievous explorations and little rebellions—rebellions Agatha knew she’d find herself smiling over even as she tried to be stern.

Agatha closed her eyes, her heart wrapped in the warmth of a future she hadn’t dared to dream for herself. She was still tired, her body aching from the weight of the baby and the sleepless nights, but at this moment, she felt a new kind of strength—one that would carry her through each hard day, each long night. For she knew, soon, there would be three of them, bound together by the love she had fought so hard to find.

up next, the baby isn't due for three more months, but how long can winter be kept at bay? Rio finds a solution.

The Prophecy

Chapter Summary

The Fates speak

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Stolen child, born of two

shade between the seasons.

Born of Death, taken life

mother’s greatest treason.

 

Carried above, birthed in a tomb

he must remain amongst the blooms.

 

Should they neglect the fruit of the vine,

should seasons fall out of time,

should a child of darkness look behind,

with equal indifference and pride

the fractured wall will again divide.

 

Where Death walks,

shadows fall.

When she cries,

so will all.

 

 

Chapter End Notes

keeping it light.

The Path Forward

Chapter Summary

Rio reckons with the prophecy shared.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

To say Rio was displeased was an understatement. She had kept her composure in check as The Fates delivered their message. It would cause even more problems if they saw how much her supposed neutrality had been compromised.

But as soon as they stopped their chant and vanished, Rio allowed herself to feel the rage pierce through her. So strong was her fury that she could heel her domain shifting and warping in response. She heard the crash and rumble of buildings collapsing to be swallowed by the ground. She didn’t care. She’d let it all crumble if she had to . “A mother’s greatest treason,” indeed.

She turned the prophecy over in her mind. The Fates always spoke truths however cloaked and obfuscated they may be. But they were truths all the same. That’s why she had called upon them and asked, “Tell me of our child.” Having found no other more clever solution she tossed her line out into the web of existence and fortune. The danger of looking into the void is what you will find looking back at you.

“He must remain among the blooms,” didn’t seem very open to interpretation. In order to be safe, their child, their son , would need to be kept in the mortal world. There were no blooming fields here. And if he never saw this place fully, that would resolve the matter of “a child of darkness” not being able to look behind.

Rio grimaced, poking her cheek with her tongue as a brutal finality sank in. This was it then. They would have their child. But he would be restricted to the overworld alone. Never would he bring light to the shadowed walls here. Never could he visit the places where his mothers had woven the love story that created him. Rio scowled as her stomach twisted with another sick realization.

She would never get to share her life, her domain, everything she had built with her son. The cold sickly feeling constricted around her heart as she reached another certainty. If their son must stay on the surface, he needed his mother with him. Agatha could not leave him alone. And Rio couldn’t keep him.

All the visions she’d allowed herself to imagine of the three of them, together as a family, shattered. Her love, her two greatest loves, would walk together. And again, as it always was, and always would be, Death would walk alone.

She had been a fool ever to consider any other path for herself. This was always how it ended.

In letting herself fall for the witch who had stumbled into her world, she had damned them both.

Agatha.

Her heart twisted viciously as she nearly cried out in pain. How could she possibly explain this to Agatha? How could she tell her that the love she felt was the strongest power she held, but still wouldn’t be enough to wield against Fate’s decree? How to explain that a child meant to be raised together, would carry more of Agatha’s influence than her own?

She will walk in light, and I will remain here, as I always have.

But she wasn’t ready to relinquish this last part of their time together, not just yet. She would make one final plea to the seasons, to the world above, a small gift to Agatha, a chance to welcome their son in the warm embrace of summer. She would delay Agatha’s return as long as possible, allowing the earth to hold her, the child to be born in warmth and light. Perhaps, this way, she could offer Agatha some solace, even if she could never be there to see it herself.

The only way to sever Agatha’s bond to the underworld was to break their pact. 

She would have to undo the vow she had made in exchange for Agatha’s coven’s safety—now that Agatha’s ties to that coven were gone that protection had lost its meaning anyway. Perhaps the world would shift, the seasons strain, and her realm might grow colder with the loss of that warmth. But the Fates had been clear, and her family deserved a chance to live freely in the sunlight, without the tether of darkness pulling her back.

But how to tell her? How could she possibly explain that the world they had built, would soon be lost? How to explain that their son would never know this place? That he would only know his mother from the stories Agatha would tell of her?

Rio pictured the way Agatha’s face would fall when she told her this. There was no way to soften it. No way to make her understand that it wasn’t her love that had faltered, but the cruel nature of her own being—bound to endings, bound to separation.

Taking a steadying breath, Rio summoned all the resolve within her. When the time came, she would spin the best version of this truth she could manage, something that might at least offer Agatha a sliver of hope and comfort as she moved forward without her. She would tell her of the warm summer that awaited them, of their son’s need for sunlight and blooming fields. How she wanted his first vision to be of the mothers who loved him surrounded by flowers in the little cabin found just for them.

She would leave out the last piece—that the underworld would soon close to Agatha forever, leaving Rio with only a memory of the light that had once graced her life.

Her hand moved reflexively to her chest, where the ache was sharpest. She straightened, pressing her fingers against it as if to absorb the pain. For Agatha. For their son. They would live in the light, and she would remain here, cloaked in shadows, watching over them from a distance that would never shrink.

One day, Agatha would hate her for this. But if it meant that their son could live, untouched by the darkness that had once claimed her, then that would be enough.

Rio returned to the cabin carrying a small bouquet of flowers. Red carnations for everlasting love and devotion. Heather for protection from harm and good fortune. In the center a single daisy, new beginnings, and forgiveness.

“You’re late,” Agatha said, concern marking her features as Rio breezed through the door.

“Well,” Rio paused, she would need to choose every word carefully. “I’ve been thinking…” She made her way to Agatha and kissed her cheek. These little mundane rituals she would miss most. “Maybe it would be nice for the kid’s first impression of life to be… I don’t know, a beautiful summer sunset instead of creepy darkness?” Rio continued her playful tone, this was the most important performance she’d ever given. “I don’t think anyone up here would mind if summer lasted just a little bit longer.”

She smiled hopefully at Agatha. Hoping, praying, that she would accept this idea, encourage it, or simply be too tired to question her further.

Agatha tilted her head thoughtfully. “You can do that? Just change the pact? I thought that wasn’t allowed.”

Rio shrugged playfully, “Eh. I’m already giving you special treatment by bending the rules to come visit as often as I do. What’s the difference if I do it a little longer.”

Please, Agatha. Trust me. Don’t question this. Let us have just a little more peace.

“Well, as long we’re together, I don’t care where we are,” Agatha said finally, smiling adoringly at her love. “Can you put some tea on?” 

Rio’s shoulders relaxed, relief washing over her like a quiet tide. Agatha had accepted her proposal with that open-hearted trust, the same trust that had disarmed Rio from the beginning. She placed the bouquet on the table beside Agatha, lingering for a moment to gently brush her fingers along Agatha’s cheek. 

"Of course my love, coming right up," she said, trying to keep her tone light. Her hands moved on autopilot, filling the kettle, lighting the stove, and arranging the tea leaves. The quiet routine settled her nerves slightly.

Glancing back at Agatha, who had settled back into her chair, her eyes weary but soft, Rio felt the ache in her chest intensify. She wanted to remember every small detail of these moments—the quiet smiles, the ease between them, the promise that somehow lingered in the air of the cabin, even if it was one she could never keep.

The kettle whistled, snapping her back to the present. She poured the tea into two delicate mismatched mugs. Carrying the tray over, she handed her the cup, allowing their fingers to brush for just a moment longer than necessary.

This was it—the beginning of the end she’d quietly dreaded. But the decision was made, and the spell was already forming in her mind. Still, she sat beside Agatha, fingers intertwined, savoring the fleeting closeness that would soon be all she had left of her beloved.
