A New Thread

Chapter Summary

Threads of fate begin to converge.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

The boy swallowed hard, meeting her gaze. “I followed the Witches’ Road,” he said. His voice was soft, almost reverent. “The path that only she knows, the one that leads you to what you want most.”

Rio’s brow arched, a mix of curiosity and disbelief crossing her features. She crossed her arms, studying him with newfound intrigue. “And what did she tell you was at the end of that road?”

His eyes softened, and for a moment, his gaze drifted as if he were remembering a far gentler memory. “I asked her once, what she’d found when she walked it,” he replied. “She said ‘Be careful what you seek Billy, at the end I found my greatest love and my biggest heartbreak.’” His voice trembled slightly, a glimmer of sadness in his gaze. “She told me she hoped I’d have better luck.”

The words hit Rio like a blow, knocking the breath from her lungs. Her face went still, her usual mask of iron slipping. Silence settled over them, thick as the iron walls that encased her domain. Rio’s gaze fell to the ground, and when she spoke, her voice was barely a whisper, laced with an ache she couldn’t contain.

“It’s a trick boy,” she murmured. “It doesn’t lead to what you want most, only what you’re willing to lose for it.”

Billy frowned, his young face furrowing with confusion. “She said you were waiting there,” he insisted, voice small. “She said that road brought her to you.”

Rio’s eyes sharpened, the faintest glimmer of anger twisting beneath her sorrow. “And what makes you think that road will lead you to your brother?” she demanded, her voice cutting.

“Because Agatha believed it would,” he replied fiercely, his voice suddenly full of the same unyielding certainty that had once blazed in Agatha herself. “She told me that if I sang as I went, the magic would lead the way.”

Rio looked at him, the stubborn tilt of his chin, the fierce gleam in his eyes, so much like Agatha’s. He wasn’t their son but she could see her influence all over him. She felt a pang in her chest and wondered how much time Agatha had spent with him. How much she had shared. No , she wouldn’t be jealous of a child.

Her lips curved into a bitter smile. “And so you came,” she said softly, “to sing me a little song, did you? She didn’t send you here to help you out, she sent you as a message to me. You don’t know her like I do.”

Billy held his ground, meeting Rio’s mocking gaze with a resolve that surprised even her. “Maybe I don’t,” he said carefully, voice steady. “But I know she wouldn’t just send me to my death—not without a way out.”

Rio scoffed, crossing her arms. “You wouldn’t be the first Agatha sent to their death without blinking. Didn’t she tell you? Sending me a few souls used to be her way of getting my attention. You think that your way out is a magic song ?” Her voice was laced with skepticism, but there was a flicker of curiosity in her eyes.

He hesitated, gripping the strap of his worn pack as if it were a lifeline. “Agatha saw something in me. She said I had the touch of a muse,” he replied, his voice uncertain but brave. “She said that sometimes… sometimes words can reach where nothing else can.”

Rio’s gaze darkened. The boy might have been naïve, but he was far from foolish, and Agatha had known that. The thought stung—a sharp, bitter pang in her chest. Agatha had chosen him, of all people, to stand in this place and challenge her. She wasn’t certain if she felt anger, betrayal, or a twisted sense of pride that Agatha would still defy her from afar. Why hadn’t she come here herself if she knew the way?

“Muses are fickle,” Rio murmured, her voice low and dangerous. “But you’re right, boy. Their words can bend fate, pluck the strings of destiny. My dear wife always had a knack for finding loopholes.”

She took a step forward, her eyes gleaming with something that lay between cruelty and grudging respect. “If you truly are a muse,” she said, her tone cold as the iron walls around them, “then sing, boy. Show me this gift she claims you have. Let me see if you have even a fraction of her power.”

Billy swallowed, clearly unsure. His fingers trembled slightly as he clenched them at his sides, but he didn’t back down. Slowly, he opened his mouth, and a soft, tentative melody began to fill the space between them.

 

"Cloaked by the river Lethe’s veil,

A child torn by two who refuse to yield.

Forever searching Elysian fields

Death she takes, and Nature she heals

 

Down by the river,

he bends to play.

Caught in between

night and day.

 

Love carried him in

It carried him out.

Hearts once together

Bleeding with doubt.

 

Flowers they bloom,

Then they rot.

A love so pure

Cannot be forgot.

 

One day in the fields,

Three will stand.

Walking together,

Hand in hand."

 

His voice was untrained, raw, but there was an aching purity to it, a truth that rang out in each note. The song was one of longing, of a bond unbroken by death or distance. His words echoed the pain of separation, the desperate hope of reunion. 

It was Agatha’s pain, Agatha’s love, carried on his voice like a whisper of memory, and Rio felt it slip past her defenses, winding its way through the bitterness she clung to like armor.

Her fists clenched as she watched him, her expression stony, but inside, her heart was torn anew. This boy—this mortal child—had somehow bridged the impossible, brought her face-to-face with the raw truth she had been trying to bury.

As Billy’s voice faded, Rio’s gaze lingered on him, cold but calculating. “So,” she murmured, her voice a brittle edge. “You think you’re her messenger, do you? That you can soften me with a song?”

Billy took a shaky breath. “I don’t know if I can,” he admitted, his voice barely a whisper. “But I’ll keep singing if it gets me closer to my brother. I’ll keep singing until I find him.”

Rio narrowed her eyes, but a flicker of something softer crossed her gaze. She almost admired his bravery—almost. “If you think your voice alone will carry you through the Underworld, you’re even more foolish than I thought.”

“Maybe,” he said, his chin tilting up in defiance. “But it’s all I’ve got. And Agatha believed in it. She believed in me.”

Rio looked at him for a long, hard moment. “Get out.” She said icily.

Billy blinked, taken aback. “What?” he stammered, his voice cracking.

“Leave.” Rio’s voice was steel, each word as cutting as the edge of a blade. “Turn around and walk out the way you came. Leave now, and perhaps I’ll let you live.”

The fire in his eyes dimmed, uncertainty shadowing his face. But after a heartbeat, he shook his head. “No,” he said, his voice small but firm. “I won’t leave without my brother.”

Rio’s lip curled, a faint sneer twisting her expression. “Do you know how many have made demands of me, boy? Mortals, gods, spirits—none of them dared refuse me when I granted them a second chance.” She took a slow, predatory step toward him, her shadow stretching out across the ground like the jaws of a trap.

“But Agatha—” he began, and Rio’s hand shot out, fingers tight around his jaw, cutting him off. He winced but didn’t pull back.

“Don’t,” she repeated, her voice low and venomous. “Do not bring that name back down here.” Her grip tightened, and Billy felt a chill seep into his skin like ice spreading through his veins.

Billy met her gaze, refusing to flinch. “She wondered,” he said, his voice steady despite the cold biting into him, “if you still cared.”

For a moment, something in Rio’s face softened, a crack in her armor that almost allowed the sorrow beneath to show. But it was gone in an instant, replaced by cold fury.

“Care?” Her laugh was bitter, a hollow sound that echoed through the desolate landscape around them. “If I cared, I would’ve spared you the agony of even stepping foot in this place.”

She released him, and Billy staggered back, clutching his jaw where the cold had burned him. “Then kill me,” he said, lifting his chin. “If you don’t care, if you really hate her, then go ahead and do it.”

The silence that fell between them was thick. Rio’s gaze bore into him, a mix of contempt and something else, something raw and unreadable. “You’re no more than a pawn in her game,” she hissed, but the words lacked their usual bite.

“Then I’ll play,” Billy shot back, his voice rising in desperation. “If it means getting to my brother, I’ll play any role you need me to.”

Rio’s eyes narrowed, her expression unreadable. “I see why she took you as her little pet. You’re just like her ” she said, almost to herself. “Stubborn to a fault. Reckless.”

She straightened, looking past him into the shadows of her domain, the vast, cold expanse that stretched into eternity. “Very well, boy,” she murmured. “If you’re so eager to play the hero, I’ll allow it. But don’t think you’ll find me so easily swayed.” 

Her voice turned sharp, commanding. “If you manage to find what’s been lost, I’ll be waiting. Then we’ll discuss what it costs.”

Billy swallowed, nodding, his determination undimmed. He took a step forward, his jaw set. 

But Rio lifted a hand, her expression dark and calculating. “Before you begin, remember this,” she warned. “If you falter, if you stumble, even for a moment—Agatha’s name will not save you.”

With that, she turned, the shadows parting before her as she strode away, leaving Billy to face the unknown path alone.

The boy’s song lingered in her mind, each line like a small dagger pressing against a part of her she'd tried to lock away. The song echoed as the prophecy whispered long ago by the Fates themselves had. Yet, it twisted in ways she hadn’t expected. It was as if the words themselves were bending, shaping to fit something new. 

She tried to push it away, but the echoes persisted, drawing threads between her own memories and the young boy’s song, binding her to a story she’d thought was closed.

"Cloaked by the river Lethe’s veil,  

A child torn by two who refuse to yield…”

Her son, the one who had vanished from her arms the instant she’d crossed into her realm as if the dark itself had swallowed him whole. She had tried, searched endlessly, and even invoked the river's keepers, but they gave her nothing but silence. 

The Lethe’s magic hid her child from her grasp, as if he were both here and nowhere, kept between life and death, day and night. She had raged against it, thinking that perhaps it was Nature’s way of reclaiming what she, Death, had tried to claim for herself.

"Forever searching Elysian fields…”

Rio’s fists clenched. The Elysian Fields, that elusive paradise reserved for the purest mortals, a place she herself could never tread. If her son was somehow there, she would have to find another way—someone with enough love and magic to guide him back. Someone whose steps could walk where hers could not. Agatha had sent this boy, this unlikely messenger, instead of coming here herself. But why?

“Death she takes, and Nature she heals…”

She bit back the twist of bitterness at the thought. It had always been this way between them—a constant push and pull. But nature could not heal what had been taken. The wound left by her son’s absence was as raw as the day she’d crossed the river with him and felt him slip from her grasp. She was certain her wife would say the same. Some wounds couldn’t heal from nature or time.

Billy’s song continued to ring in her mind, its simple melody tugging at a deeper truth, a thread from the Fates’ prophecy that she’d long dismissed: “One day in the fields, three will stand. Walking together, hand in hand.”

The image it conjured was almost too painful to bear—a world where she, Agatha, and their son might stand together. Somehow overcoming the barriers of life and death, of separation and loss. Breaking the cycle.

Was such a reunion even possible? Or was it just a child’s dream, twisted into song, sent to mock her?

She closed her eyes, considering the old prophecy from every angle, every implication. Had Agatha believed in it? Had she believed it enough to send this boy to challenge her, to remind her that the story might not yet be over? She almost laughed at the thought—a foolish hope that perhaps the Fates themselves could be defied.

As she turned away from the empty darkness, she felt a shiver of something unfamiliar ripple through her—a fragile sliver of hope, buried beneath layers of grief and anger. If she could somehow uncover the truth, if she could follow the thread of this prophecy to its end, perhaps a different story could be told. 

Chapter End Notes

Been listening to The Prophecy and Epic III on repeat and I think it shows here

Don't Look Back

Chapter Summary

Test and trials

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

In the days that followed, Billy wandered through Rio’s domain, his determination unwavering as he searched for his brother’s spirit. When he finally found him—a pale shadow of the boy he once knew, hovering on the edge of memory—Billy felt his own heart lighten. Tommy was there , somehow still waiting for him. Call it a restless spirit, unfinished business, love persevering. Together, they made their way back to the heart of the underworld, to the waiting figure of Death herself.

When Billy approached Rio, he held his brother’s hand tightly, fear flickering in his eyes, though his voice was steady. “We found each other,” he said. “Now... will you let us go? Can I trust you?”

For a moment, Rio’s expression was unreadable, her gaze lingering on the brothers with a resigned distance. If she couldn’t hold onto what she wanted, perhaps she could at least grant them a chance at freedom. 

But she wasn’t ready to let them leave without a test, one last question to be answered for herself—could mortals truly change? Could anyone? Could she? Could someone ever let go of doubt entirely and place their trust in another, as she had once tried and failed to do?

She nodded slowly, issuing her final terms. “You will both leave, but in a single file. One follows, one leads. You cannot look back, not for anything. If you truly want to leave together, you’ll have to trust one another. Not a step out of place. Do you understand?”

Billy hesitated, gripping his brother’s hand even tighter, but his gaze remained steady. “We understand,” he said. And as he turned to lead Tommy out of the underworld, he glanced back one last time at Rio, an almost pitying look in his young eyes. “I hope... I hope you’ll find what you’ve lost, too.”

Rio watched them go, her jaw tight as they faded from her sight, swallowed by the shadows of her realm. She didn’t know if they’d make it. But she allowed herself to hope they would.

As silence settled around her once more, a strange hollowness filled her, as if something she’d barely dared to hold had slipped through her fingers. She turned away, her thoughts drifting back to the garden she’d long left abandoned. It had been nothing more than ashes, stones, and barren soil since Agatha’s wrath had torn it apart.

But as she approached, she saw two small blooms pushing up through the cracks—two slender flowers, delicate yet resilient, rising from the earth. A tribute to the kindness she had shown the brothers. She felt a pull, something soft and strange, stirring within her. 

Rolling up her sleeves, Rio knelt by the twin flowers. Slowly, deliberately, she dug her fingers into the soil, feeling its weight and warmth, feeling the pulse of the earth as she planted a new seed alongside them, her hands working without magic, without command.

She stayed there, kneeling in the dirt, letting the weight of the moment sink in, breathing in the faint, earthy scent of new life. The first seed of something that might yet grow.

“Nicky,” she called out softly, unknowing if he could hear her words. “We’re going to plant a garden for your mama. We’re going to make it something so beautiful. You and me. And when she’s ready… we’re going to share it with her. Just like I said. When she’s ready, she’ll come home.”

Agatha stirred as the morning light broke over the hills. But something else had caught her eye—a glimmer of deep, indigo nestled in the grass beside her. She blinked, her heart giving a sudden, startled leap. A single shadebloom had grown where she had slept, its petals as vivid and haunting as a memory come to life.

Her heart thudded as she stared at it, her anger momentarily forgotten. She hadn’t seen a shadebloom since…since before everything had fallen apart. Since they’d been happy, back in the days when their world was full of gardens and life and dreams for the future. 

She reached out slowly, almost afraid it would vanish if she dared to touch it. But it didn’t fade—it remained, stubborn and alive, as if it had waited for her all this time.

It struck her then, clear as day—this was Rio’s doing. It had to be. 

Somehow, after everything that had happened, Rio was reaching out to her, a quiet gesture in a language only they understood. Agatha’s heart tightened painfully, the weight of her anger and grief shifting, giving way to something else—a longing she’d tried so hard to bury.

Had Billy reached her, then? Had he softened Rio’s heart even a little? She closed her eyes. She was so tired. She was so tired of the rage that had burned through her, so tired of punishing herself and Rio, holding them both captive in a loss that seemed endless. 

And as she sat there, with the flower warm in her hand, she saw it clearly—she had lost her son, yes, but she didn’t have to lose her wife, too. Blaming Rio for their son’s absence, for something she herself couldn’t understand or control, wasn’t fair. It never had been.

Her thoughts drifted to Nicky, his words echoing in her mind as if he were there beside her, the gentleness with which he’d picked the flower Rio had left for him and announced, “I’ll keep it safe. So she knows I love her back.”

She swallowed hard, tears prickling her eyes. Maybe…maybe this shadebloom was Rio’s way of saying the same thing—that even after everything, she still loved her, still remembered what they had shared. Gently, Agatha lifted the bloom and tucked it behind her ear, feeling the cool petals brush her skin. The weight of her fury and sorrow began to lift, like a stone she could finally set down.

Agatha stepped through the misted woods, her heart racing with each hurried stride. She had no sense of how long she’d been walking, only that she was drawn forward by an undeniable pull.

And in an instant, she realized where that pull was coming from.

Rio was there, coming toward her from the other side stepping through a crack in a tree, her eyes wide and worn, her steps just as frantic. They both slowed as they closed the last of the distance, taking each other in. 

Agatha’s breath caught—Rio looked like she’d been through a war of her own, her hair tangled, her cheeks hollow, the weight of sleepless nights and relentless sorrow etched into every line of her face.

She knew she probably looked just as broken, just as undone. They stood there, eyes meeting across the small threshold, feeling the fullness of the absence that had eaten at them both.

Agatha held out her arms, her face softening, her heart aching with a forgiveness she hadn’t been sure she would ever feel again. Without a word, Rio collapsed into her, and Agatha pulled her close, wrapping her arms tightly around her, feeling Rio’s shuddering breath, the press of her heartbeat against her own. 

They clung to each other, each finding strength in the other’s presence, a silent understanding passing between them that needed no words.

“I’m sorry,” Agatha whispered, her voice breaking. “I hated you for so long, and I know it wasn’t fair. I know you were just as hurt…that you made the choice you thought you had to.”

Rio’s hand tightened on her back, her voice a hoarse murmur against Agatha’s shoulder. “I’m sorry too. I shouldn’t have decided alone. I shouldn’t have taken him without giving you a chance to say goodbye. I thought I was protecting you…but I was wrong.”

They pulled back, faces inches apart, each seeing the tears in the other’s eyes, the cracks in the armor they had built over so much pain. In that moment, there were no more walls, no more blame or hurt—only the fierce, unrelenting love that they had always shared

Agatha cupped Rio’s face, her fingers brushing against her cheek, and without another thought, she kissed her, pouring every bit of longing, every apology, every word she had never spoken into that single, searing kiss. Rio melted into her, returning the kiss with equal fervor as if nothing else mattered but this—this moment, this reunion.

Nothing else did matter, to either of them, except the fragile hope of starting again. They lost themselves in each other, in the fierce, undeniable love that had never truly died. It never would. 

When they finally broke apart, breathless and holding on tight, they stayed close, foreheads touching. 

“Let’s go find our son,” Rio whispered.

Agatha winced “Don’t, my love, don’t give me false hope now.”

“It’s not false. That boy you sent. The song he carried. I think it was a guide… I think I know where our boy is.”

Chapter End Notes

one more chapter, one piece of unfinished business

A Family Found

Chapter Summary

The lovers reunite with what was once thought lost.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Rio led her down a path that they had not walked before. As they moved through the dark here, along the outskirts of her city, Agatha noted the jagged metal towers, the smoke clouding the air, and the new oppressive heat that blanketed the landscape. “You’ve been busy down here.”

Rio nodded. “A distraction. When I arrived back here… with Nicky, I passed the threshold and he had slipped through my arms. I couldn’t find him. I couldn’t feel him here. And I couldn’t bear it. So I went to work.”

“My love,” Agatha gasped softly, reaching to take her hand, “all this time… I was so angry that you took him, without me getting to say goodbye, but I found the tiniest shred of comfort that at least he’d be near you.” She hesitated before adding in a small whisper, “You didn’t get to have him either.” The realization that they had both suffered the same agony broke her heart all over again.

“I did not.” She kept hold of Agatha’s hand, a tether and an anchor as they walked. “Tell me about the boy. The one you sent here.”

Agatha smiled, she was a clever witch but she had impressed even herself with that particular scheme. “He found me. He told me he’d had a vision about his missing brother, Toby or whoever. I didn’t pay attention but then he said that he knew he was in the underworld. And that some other meddling god had let slip to him that I was the only living person who had passed between the earth and your kingdom. So he willed his magic into a song that led him to find me.”

“Do you believe that? That he is some oracle or muse?”

“Beats me.” Agatha shrugged. “But he was young. Sweet and eager. So earnest… malleable. I thought that there may be a way to use him. I planted a seed of inspiration. I encouraged him to write a song about reunion and love. I convinced him that perhaps it would be enough to carry him to Death and thaw her heart.”

A wave of understanding hit Rio and she grinned at Agatha’s cleverness. “So you puppeted the strings and led him to me to deliver a prophecy,” she breathed, her voice full of pride and wonder.

Agatha beamed at her. “I did. And as you once told me, a prophecy spun by fate or muse will always come to pass in some way.”

She was pulled into a deep and passionate kiss. Rio pulled away, smiling brightly for the first time since the night their world had been torn asunder. “You clever, conniving witch.”

“Guilty.” Agatha chuckled before growing serious, “There is no power I would not claim, no path I would not walk, no opportunity I would not exploit to find a way back to you and our son,” she confessed.

Rio smiled proudly and squeezed her hand, “Well, all that’s left is to see if it holds any truth.”

They came to the banks of a massive river. But it did not rush or churn. It was eerily placid and still.

“This is the river Lethe. It… is tricky. To pass through it is to challenge yourself, it tries to wash memory away. But on the other side, is the path to Elysium. And if your pet is right, that’s where our son plays.”

Agatha nodded, already stepping forward. “Okay, let’s go.”

“Wait.” Rio pulled her into another tender kiss. “You go first. I will wait here and do my best to guide you across. Wait for me on the other side.”

“Okay.” She smiled at her wife, raising her hand to her lips and kissing her knuckles. “See you in a moment.”

She stepped down into the Lethe, and the chill was immediate, curling around her ankles like icy fingers, tugging her down. The water felt thick, more like mist than liquid, and as she waded deeper, a strange heaviness crept into her limbs, slowing her steps.

The river’s magic seeped into her, gentle at first—a soft, quiet nudge that lulled her racing thoughts into silence. She took another step, and a flicker of memory slipped away like smoke, vanishing before she could grasp it. Her fingers twitched as she tried to hold onto something, anything— why am I here? —but the answer melted into the river as soon as it formed.

Another step and her own name began to unravel, fading like an echo swallowed by the hungry river mouth. She knew there had been a purpose in coming here, but it slipped away from her too, swallowed by the river’s relentless flow. Her mind drifted, hazy and unfocused as if she were caught in a dream, and for a moment, she simply stood in the middle, lost.

Agatha turned, searching for something she couldn’t name, and her eyes met those of a woman on the river bank. She felt a strange tugging in her chest—a soft, wordless ache—but she didn’t recognize the beautiful ethereal woman standing at the river’s edge. Yet, despite the unfamiliarity, she felt drawn to her, bound by a thread she couldn’t remember weaving. Her heart beat painfully, insistently, and she felt something important —something she’d once known—shifting beneath the weight of the water.

She looked at the woman on the river bank, and though she didn’t know who this person was, she knew her, with a certainty that made her heart throb. Something about her seemed warm, familiar, precious. “I… know you,” Agatha murmured, her voice barely a whisper above the river’s pull. She lifted a hand toward her, almost like a question, and for a fleeting moment, she wanted to turn back, to leave the river and stay by this stranger’s side.

But Rio, her eyes shining with determination and sorrow, nodded to her. “Keep going, Agatha. Just a little further,” she urged, her voice steady, cutting through the fog clouding Agatha’s mind.

Hearing that name— Agatha —felt like someone had struck a match in the darkness. Agatha clung to it, letting it echo within her as she took another trembling step, the chill of the river deepening, clouding her mind with every inch. She staggered forward, her body aching with the effort, her thoughts drifting in fragments. Agatha… Agatha… She repeated the name to herself, holding onto it like an anchor.

Finally, her foot found solid ground, and as she stumbled forward, her mind began to clear. The fog lifted, and memories came rushing back all at once—her name, her purpose, the feel of her son’s small hands in hers, and most of all, the love that had driven her here. She turned, breath catching in her throat, and her eyes met Rio’s once more, fully seeing her, fully remembering.

Rio raised her hand in a little salute and Agatha’s brow furrowed as she beckoned her to cross. “Just a little further my love, your turn,” Agatha called.

At the river’s edge, Rio paused, her expression shadowed as she responded. “This is as far as I can go,” Rio murmured, the weight of countless centuries in her voice. “You can reach Elysium without me. My duties, the souls… I am bound to them, Agatha.”

Agatha, standing on the other side of Lethe’s shimmering, silver-tinged water, her memories of Rio and their son vivid and warm within her heart, looked back at her wife with fierce determination. “They need you, yes. But not as much as we need you,” she said, voice quiet yet strong. “You’ve guided the dead and ruled the Underworld with care, but now it’s time to come with me. Our family… we need you more.”

Rio hesitated, the tension in her shoulders betraying her conflict. She had been the keeper of the passage of death for so long, taking up a thankless mantle when no one else would. Yet here was Agatha, asking her to give it all up for a single chance at happiness—a chance Rio had long told herself was never meant for her.

“Please,” Agatha whispered, hand outstretched toward her. “You’re my family. Don’t let us slip away for a duty you don’t have to bear alone.”

She would not be fool enough to make the same mistake twice. Not after just finding her love again. Rio’s gaze softened, and she waded into the waters with a final, resigned breath. The chill coiled around her as she crossed, each step a quiet battle to hold onto her love for Agatha and Nicky. The further she went, the more she felt pieces of herself begin to drift, the centuries of her rule losing their hold on her heart. 

She let them go willingly, allowing the river to wash over her sense of duty and resolve. Her reasons, her purpose, the iron walls she’d built around her heart—they faded into the water’s pull.

When she reached the other side, she looked at Agatha, not as the queen of the Underworld, but as a woman whose heart beat only for the family that had been waiting for her.

Agatha’s hand was warm as she took Rio’s, grounding her as she emerged from the Lethe’s grasp. The quiet weight that had been so constant for centuries now felt like a distant memory, blurred and fading.

Agatha stepped closer, her thumb brushing softly over Rio’s knuckles, and her voice broke with quiet pride. “I know what you’re giving up for us,” she whispered, her gaze steady, her eyes full of unspoken love and gratitude. “You’ve carried so much, all on your own, and I’ve never known anyone stronger. I’m… so proud of you. And I love you. More than you could ever know.”

Rio felt a warmth spread through her chest, melting the last remnants of the icy resignation that had been her armor. She wanted to correct her, to tell Agatha that she hadn’t lost anything, that nothing could be more precious than what she stood to gain. But she could only pull Agatha close, pressing her forehead against hers, the words coming out as a whisper, raw and true.

“You and Nicky—you’re everything to me. Nothing matters more than that.”

Agatha held her tightly, her arms wrapping around her as if anchoring them both. For a long time, they stayed in each other’s arms, sharing the silence that spoke louder than words. Their breaths mingled, their hearts pounding in sync as the river's distant murmurs faded away.

When they finally broke apart, Agatha took Rio’s hand, her expression softened yet resolute. “Come on. We’ve made it this far. Let’s go find our son.”

Hand in hand, they left the river behind, moving toward Elysium’s mist-shrouded hills with hearts whole once more.

They stepped onto soft, dew-laden grass, greeted by the vast expanse of Elysium’s endless, rolling fields. The gloom faded and sunlight warmed their skin as they looked out across the landscape, where golden wildflowers danced in the gentle breeze. The fields stretched endlessly, vibrant and rich with life, each hill blending into the next under a radiant sky. 

The couple exchanged a glance, their fingers laced tightly together as they took in the beauty around them. It reminded them both, achingly so, of the garden of their courtship, when the weight of everything hadn’t yet settled on their shoulders. There was that same sense of possibility, of something precious unfolding, only now it felt more tangible, more earned.

They walked through the fields in quiet wonder, each step brushing against blossoms that shimmered as if dusted with stardust. And then, a voice, clear and bright, called out across the fields:

“Mami! Mommy!”

They froze, their eyes widening as they turned toward the sound. There, standing on a rise in the golden light, was their son. Whole, healthy, and glowing with life, he stood with his arms outstretched, his face lit up with a radiant, unburdened joy.

Agatha’s hand flew to her mouth, a sob breaking free as she watched him take off at a run, his feet light as air as he bounded toward them, his laughter filling the air like music. Rio felt her own breath catch, her heart swelling as their son barreled forward.

When he reached them, he threw his arms around them both, squeezing tight, as if he’d been waiting a lifetime to do so. They knelt next to him and wrapped their arms around him, holding him close, each overcome by the warmth, the life, the pure love that pulsed between them.

“Mommy,” he murmured into Agatha’s shoulder, “Mami told me you’d come.”

Agatha stroked his hair, her heart brimming with relief as she whispered, “We’re here now, my love. We’re here.”

And as they held him, standing together in the golden fields of Elysium, everything else fell away. In that moment, there was no past, no pain, no shadows—only the light of their family, whole and unbreakable, reunited at last.

The quiet hush of Rio’s domain greeted them as they crossed back into her realm, but it was nothing like the place they had left behind. Gone was the shadowed, forbidding expanse ruled by order and control. 

Now, nature had crept over everything, weaving itself into the stonework, transforming the dark corners into a peaceful sanctuary. Buildings once stark and foreboding were softened by vines heavy with blossoms, vibrant and alive, as though they’d been waiting for this very moment to unfurl. The air was warm and filled with the gentle hum of life.

Spirits drifted here and there, no longer bound to toil and labor but free to roam, settling in quiet places to rest. Rio had released her hold over them, and now they moved with a tranquil purpose, their presence lending the realm a serene beauty. 

This was no longer a kingdom of the dead; it was a place of peaceful transition, of memory and release. Rio’s rule had changed, softened by love and loss, and the underworld had blossomed in kind.

As they walked through the transformed realm, Nicky’s eyes were wide with wonder. When he stepped into their garden—a place once beautiful then broken—it burst into vibrant color around him. Flowers bloomed at his feet, bright blues and purples and whites, an explosion of life that covered the garden floor. The air felt lighter, softer, as though all the burdens they had once carried had been gently laid to rest.

At the heart of the garden stood the willow tree, its branches trailing down like gentle arms embracing the earth. Agatha felt a pang of nostalgia as they approached, memories of long nights spent beneath its boughs washing over her. It was where she and Rio had fallen in love, had spoken in quiet gentle voices of things dancing around things that they were both too afraid to say aloud. Words that now came to them freely. And now, here they were again, with their son in tow.

The three of them sat together in the cool shade, feeling the weight of their journey melt away. Rio reached to her belt, where her dagger hung, polished and gleaming. She held it out to Nicky, who looked up at her with wide, questioning eyes.

"Take it," Rio said softly. "This place—this life we share—it belongs to all of us now."

Nicky took the dagger reverently, his fingers wrapping around its hilt as he leaned forward, pressing the blade’s tip to the smooth bark of the willow. With careful strokes, he began to carve their initials into the tree. As each letter took form, the tree seemed to respond, its leaves glowing a little brighter, its branches swaying as if in acknowledgment of their bond.

When he finished, Nicky leaned back, his face beaming with pride. The three of them looked up at the tree, at the simple carving that would remain as a testament to the love they had fought so hard to preserve.

Agatha leaned her head on Rio’s shoulder, and Nicky crawled into her lap. They sat there together enveloped by the peace of their garden. The willow’s branches swayed gently above them, and for the first time in many lifetimes, they were at peace, together, under the shade of a love that had endured everything. 

In that moment, there was no kingdom, no duty, only family, beneath the willow tree, forever marked with their names.

They lived there happily, never to be separated again.
